201 of 756 DOCUMENTS



Zuckerman v. Town of Hadley


SJC-09169


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


442 Mass. 511; 813 N.E.2d 843; 2004 Mass. LEXIS 508


March 2, 2004, Argued  
August 24, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected September 14, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Land Court Department on July 12, 2000. The case was heard by Alexander H. Sands, III, J., on motions for summary judgment. The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.
ZUCKERMAN v. TOWN OF HADLEY, 10 LCR 236, 2002 Mass. LCR LEXIS 17 (2002).



DISPOSITION: Land Court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state supreme court transferred to itself on its own motion an appeal by defendant town from a summary judgment of the Land Court Department, Suffolk (Massachusetts), in favor of plaintiff landowner and declaring unconstitutional Hadley, Mass., Zoning Bylaws §§ 15.0.1-15.2.1, which regulated, for an unlimited duration in time, the number of building permits to be issued for single-family homes.


OVERVIEW: Fifteen years earlier the town had adopted its rate of development (ROD) amendment with the stated aim of enabling it better to protect its interest in retaining its agricultural character. The landowner's 66-acre tract was zoned for subdivision, but because of the ROD amendment, she could develop only a few home sites each year. She challenged the ROD amendment as unconstitutionally interfering with her ownership rights, and both the trial court and the state supreme court agreed. The state supreme court had previously held that it was permissible to enact such ordinances for a limited period, to allow a town time to develop a land use policy that recognized the rights of landowners while also promoting other values identified by the town. After 15 years, however, the town had failed to implement many of the suggestions made in studies it had commissioned, which might have enabled it to protect its agricultural character without aggressively excluding newcomers. The continued enforcement of the ROD amendment, with no end date in sight, unconstitutionally limited the landowner's right to make profitable use of her property.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the judgment.


 

202 of 756 DOCUMENTS


Coe v. Sex Offender Registry Bd.


SJC-09255


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


442 Mass. 250; 812 N.E.2d 913; 2004 Mass. LEXIS 486


June 30, 2004, Argued  
August 3, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on May 13, 2003. A motion to dissolve a preliminary injunction was heard by Bonnie H. MacLeod, J. The Supreme Judicial Court granted an application for direct appellate review.
Coe v. Franco, 2003 Mass. Super. LEXIS 150 (Mass. Super. Ct., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Sex Offender Registry Board commenced an action in the Suffolk Superior Court Department (Massachusetts) to dissolve a preliminary injunction that enjoined the Board from disseminating sex offender registration of appellee sex offenders on the Internet. The Supreme Judicial Court granted an application for direct appellate review to decide whether the trial court correctly dissolved the preliminary injunction.


OVERVIEW: Each sex offender was a Level Three sex offender and was required to register as such with the Board. The trial court initially concluded that the sex offenders had demonstrated a likelihood of success on the merits because the Sex Offender Act, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 6, §§ 178C-178Q, had not authorized Internet posting or dissemination of sex offender registration information. Subsequently, the governor filed the proposed Internet legislation. The appellate court held the trial court correctly concluded that the sex offenders received the process that was due through notice and a fair hearing prior to their designations as Level Three sex offenders as required by the Act and case law, and prior to any registration information being made available for dissemination. The Internet legislation was presumed to be constitutional. The sex offenders did not satisfy the heavy burden of showing the legislation did not bear a reasonable relation to a permissible legislative objective. The trial court correctly determined that sex offenders could not show a likelihood of success on the merits and, on that ground, did not abuse her discretion in dissolving the preliminary injunction.


OUTCOME: The order of dissolution was affirmed.

 

203 of 756 DOCUMENTS


Lavallee v. Justices in the Hampden Superior Court


SJC-09268


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


442 Mass. 228; 812 N.E.2d 895; 2004 Mass. LEXIS 422


June 30, 2004, Argued  
July 28, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected September 14, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on May 6, 2004. After consolidation, the cases were reported by Spina, J.



DISPOSITION: Order entered; remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, indigent criminal defendants represented by a public service agency, commenced an action against respondents, district court justices, alleging that the indigent defendants were detained because there were no available attorneys to represent them due to the Commonwealth's inadequately low compensation rates for such attorneys. Petitioners sought the court's intervention and relief under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 211, § 3.


OVERVIEW: Due to the low compensation rate paid to attorneys representing indigent criminal defendants, there was a shortage, which resulted in petitioners not having counsel available for assignment to them. Petitioners were thereafter held in lieu of bail or under preventive detention. They sought the court's use of its powers of superintendence to allow compensation to assigned attorneys at a higher rate than that provided by the legislature. The court found that petitioners were deprived of their right to counsel under Mass. Const. Decl. Rights art. 12, and that such deprivation resulted in severe restrictions on their liberty and other constitutional interests. The court noted that failure to provide counsel at early stages created concerns about whether petitioners would ultimately receive the effective assistance of trial counsel. The court reviewed the adequate remedies asserted by the Attorney General, and found that none provided the necessary "relief" for petitioners. Accordingly, the court found that petitioners established a case for relief under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 211, § 3. The court fashioned a remedy, which it indicated was to be modified by the justice assigned.


OUTCOME: The court exercised its powers of superintendence and held that upon a showing that no counsel was available to represent a particular indigent petitioner, despite good faith efforts, such petitioner could not be held more than seven days and the criminal case against such a petitioner could not continue beyond 45 days. The matter was remanded to a single justice for adjustment of the implementation mechanism.

 

204 of 756 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Walker


SJC-09223


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


442 Mass. 185; 812 N.E.2d 262; 2004 Mass. LEXIS 419


May 3, 2004, Argued  
July 23, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected September 14, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Norfolk. Indictments found and returned in the Superior Court Department on April 16, 1997; February 25, 1998; and July 25, 1998. A motion for joinder of indictments was heard by Herman J. Smith, Jr., J., and the cases were tried before Julian T. Houston, J. After review by the Appeals Court, the Supreme Judicial Court granted leave to obtain further appellate review.
Commonwealth v. Walker, 60 Mass. App. Ct. 255, 801 N.E.2d 267, 2004 Mass. App. LEXIS 3 (2004).



DISPOSITION: Appeals Court decision affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commonwealth sought further appellate review after the Massachusetts Appeals Court reversed convictions on three of four poisoning indictments against defendant. Defendant had been convicted of involuntary manslaughter, assault with intent to rape, drugging for purposes of sexual intercourse, assault and battery by means of a dangerous weapon (four indictments), and mingling poison with drink with intent to kill or injure (four indictments).


OVERVIEW: Defendant invited women to his apartment and served them drinks mixed with a prescription sleeping medication. The drinks rendered the women unconscious. At least one of the women was sexually assaulted while unconscious, and another died as a result of the combination of the drug and alcohol. Defendant was convicted of all charges but rape, and the appeals court affirmed eight of the convictions but reversed the convictions on three of four poisoning indictments. The court granted the Commonwealth's application for further appellate review and concluded that there was sufficient evidence for a rational jury to find defendant guilty of involuntary manslaughter, and that the definition of "poison" as used in Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 265, § 28, encompassed the medication. The court noted that a person of ordinary intelligence would be aware that there were risks associated with prescription drugs and that the jury was entitled to conclude that defendant's act of mixing his drugs with alcohol and serving the drink to victims showed an indifference to the risk of harm. Lastly, the court found that guilty verdicts of poisoning and involuntary manslaughter were not legally inconsistent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's convictions.

 

205 of 756 DOCUMENTS


Lopes v. Commonwealth


SJC-09188


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


442 Mass. 170; 811 N.E.2d 501; 2004 Mass. LEXIS 412


March 5, 2004, Argued  
July 9, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected September 14, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on March 23, 2001. A motion to dismiss was heard by Allan van Gestel, J. The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.
Commonwealth v. Philip Morris Inc., 1998 Mass. Super. LEXIS 350 (Mass. Super. Ct., 1998).



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff personal representatives appealed the judgment of the Superior Court Department, Suffolk (Massachusetts), which dismissed their suit. The personal representatives sought to enjoin the Commonwealth from recovering the cost of Medicaid care from their decedents' estates or, where the money had already been recovered, to require the Commonwealth to return the funds, from funds recovered in a national tobacco litigation settlement.


OVERVIEW: The personal representatives represented deceased residents who had received free medical care during their lives under the Commonwealth's Medicaid program, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 118E, § 15 et seq. The personal representatives based their claim on the premise that their decedents received such care for tobacco-related illnesses, and the Commonwealth already had recovered the cost of that care from settlement of its litigation against various manufacturers of tobacco products. They argued that the recovery from the decedents' estates amounted to double recovery and unjust enrichment, as well as violation of various state and federal statutory and constitutional provisions. The trial court dismissed the suit as barred by sovereign immunity. The court agreed that sovereign immunity barred the suit, because the legislature had never granted permission to have such relief as sought by the personal representatives. Additionally, the court held that the plain language of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1396b(d)(3)(B)(ii) precluded any claim against amounts recovered by the Commonwealth from a national tobacco litigation settlement, including a claim of setoff.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

206 of 756 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Mahar


SJC-09050


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


442 Mass. 11; 809 N.E.2d 989; 2004 Mass. LEXIS 302


February 6, 2004, Argued  
June 7, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus denied Mahar v. Hall, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 50906 (D. Mass., July 3, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Indictment found and returned in the Superior Court Department on March 3, 1997. Following review by this court, 430 Mass. 643, 722 N.E.2d 461 (2000), a motion for a new trial, filed on May 30, 2001, was heard by Thomas E. Connolly, J. The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.
Commonwealth v. Mahar, 2002 Mass. Super. LEXIS 133 (Mass. Super. Ct., Apr. 9, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Superior court order denying motion for new trial affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On its own initiative, the court transferred to itself from the Massachusetts Appeals Court an appeal by defendant from an order of the Superior Court Department, Suffolk (Massachusetts), denying defendant's post-trial motion for a new trial after his conviction of home invasion and related offenses. Defendant argued that counsel had been ineffective in advising him regarding rejection of a plea offer.


OVERVIEW: Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 265, § 18C, the home invasion statute that formed the basis for the most serious charge defendant faced, was interpreted in a decision of an intermediate appellate court shortly before defendant was charged as requiring a showing that the initial entry was unlawful. Since defendant entered the home involved by permission given without knowledge of his violent purpose, his trial counsel believed it unlikely that he could be convicted and, after consulting with her, defendant rejected a plea bargain. At trial, the court actually instructed the jury that the entry was unlawful if he entered the home for the purpose of committing a crime therein. While the high court agreed with defendant that counsel's ineffectiveness in advising at the plea stage could be the basis for post-conviction relief even if a defendant's conviction after rejecting the plea occurred in a fair trial, it found no inadequacy in the representation provided to defendant. It was not unreasonable for counsel to have thought, after studying the statute and case law, that her proposed instruction regarding consensual entry would be accepted. She was not ineffective in suggesting going to trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed denial of the motion, while recognizing that such a motion could be meritorious in other circumstances.

Soc'y of Jesus of New Eng. v. Commonwealth


SJC-09119, SJC-09121


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


441 Mass. 662; 808 N.E.2d 272; 2004 Mass. LEXIS 277


December 1, 2003, Argued  
May 13, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at Soc'y of Jesus of New Eng. v. Commonwealth, 442 Mass. 1049, 818 N.E.2d 559, 2004 Mass. LEXIS 746 (Mass., Nov. 24, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Civil actions commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on August 1, 2003. The cases were reported by Cordy, J.
Doherty v. Talbot, 2000 Me. Super. LEXIS 46 (Me. Super. Ct., Mar. 24, 2000)



DISPOSITION: Reported question answered in the negative; case remanded to trial court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A religious society and a priest sought relief under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 211, § 3 from an order of the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk (Massachusetts), which denied their motions to quash a subpoena duces tecum. A single justice of the court reserved and reported the question of whether the First Amendment, Mass. Const. Decl. Rights art. 2, and Mass. Const. amend. art. XLVI, § 1 protected the documents from production.


OVERVIEW: The priest had been charged with sexually assaulting two former students, and the grand jury sought documents in the possession of the religious society regarding the incident. The court held that (1) nothing in the doctrine of church autonomy deprived the court of subject matter jurisdiction over the underlying case; (2) pursuant to the balancing test under the free exercise clause of Mass. Const. amend. art. XLVI, § 1, the Commonwealth had a compelling interest in obtaining the documents; (3) enforcement of the subpoena did not violate the Establishment Clause of the First Amendment because the alleged inhibition on religion was not a "principal or primary" effect of the subpoena, nor did its enforcement result in any excessive government entanglement; (4) the right to freedom of association was not implicated because there was no issue of "privacy" with respect to the persons with whom defendant had associated; and (5) enforcement did not violate Mass. Const. Decl. Rights art. 2 because the production did not hurt the society or the priest in their performance of any religious rituals or ceremonies of worship.


OUTCOME: The court answered the question in the negative.

M.B. Claff, Inc. v. Mass. Bay Transp. Auth.


SJC-09177


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


441 Mass. 596; 808 N.E.2d 238; 2004 Mass. LEXIS 272


March 5, 2004, Argued  
May 7, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Plymouth. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on February 14, 1996. The case was tried before John J. O'Brien, J., and a motion for relief from judgment and for interest was heard by David A. McLaughlin, J. After review by the Appeals Court, the Supreme Judicial Court granted leave to obtain further appellate review.
M.B. Claff, Inc. v. Mass. Bay Transp. Auth., 59 Mass. App. Ct. 669, 797 N.E.2d 426, 2003 Mass. App. LEXIS 1107 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Leave was granted to plaintiff owner to review the judgment of the Appeals Court (Massachusetts), which denied the owner's motion for relief from judgment pursuant to Mass. R. Civ. P. 60(a) and (b)(6). The owner had commenced an action for compensation pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 79, § 14 upon dissatisfaction with the payment for the taking of his real property by defendant transportation authority.


OVERVIEW: A verdict in favor of the owner was returned. A judgment was entered in an amount reflecting a prior payment made by the transportation authority to the owner, with interest thereon from the date of judgment in a specific sum. The clerk had erred in calculating the amount of judgment interest by calculating it from the date of the judgment as opposed to the date of the taking and using the rate of 12 percent per year rather than the rate set by ch. 79, § 37, which was 3.61 percent a year. The owner filed his motion seeking to have the interest recalculated at the rate of seven percent. The lower court held that the statutory interest rate did not necessarily equate to constitutionally adequate compensation in all eminent domain cases, but that the owner had waived his claim for additional interest by failing to raise the issue in a timely manner. The court agreed and held that the owner's Mass. R. Civ. P. 60(a) motion was inappropriate to raise a constitutional challenge to the statutory interest rate used and that his Rule 60(b) motion articulated no extraordinary circumstances justifying relief. The court noted that the owner should have raised the issue at trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

209 of 756 DOCUMENTS


Liberty Square Dev. Trust v. Schwachman


SJC-09189


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


441 Mass. 605; 808 N.E.2d 245; 2004 Mass. LEXIS 273


March 5, 2004, Argued  
May 7, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected June 25, 2004


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Worcester. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on May 6, 1998. The case was heard by Ernest B. Murphy, J., and motions to amend the judgment were heard by him. The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner challenged the decision of the Worcester Superior Court Department (Massachusetts), which denied its motion, filed on the day of trial, asking the trial judge to determine the interest rate based on a "prudent investor" standard rather than on the statutory standard provided for in Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 79, § 37 to calculate the interest to be awarded as part of an eminent domain damages case.


OVERVIEW: Defendant city effected a taking of two parcels of land, and the landowner filed an action for its damages. The landowner did not introduce any evidence on the interest issue at trial, but instead sought leave to produce affidavits or testimony after trial. Affirming the trial court's judgment, the court first held that the trial judge did not abuse his discretion in agreeing to entertain the landowner's request, particularly where the city voiced no procedural objection at the time. Moreover, because the landowner's later "amended" motions were untimely, the court considered only whether the trial judge, in denying the original motion as filed, committed error. Concluding that he did not, the court noted that, on the landowner's own calculation, a rate as low as 6.5 percent would satisfy constitutional requirements and the rate set by § 37 was 5.88 percent for this particular taking. Because the landowner cited no precedent showing that this discrepancy was below constitutional requirements, it did not meet its burden of demonstrating that the statutory rate was so unreasonably low as to deprive it of just compensation for the delay in payment of its damages.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of the landowner's motion.

Stonehill College v. Mass. Comm'n Against Discrimination


SJC-09112


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


441 Mass. 549; 808 N.E.2d 205; 2004 Mass. LEXIS 271; 94 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 1641


February 3, 2004, Argued  
May 6, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected June 25, 2004.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Wilfert Bros. Realty Co. v. Mass. Comm'n Against Discrimination, 543 U.S. 979, 125 S. Ct. 481, 160 L. Ed. 2d 356, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 7420 (2004)
Judgment entered by Wilfert Bros. Realty Co. v. Mass. Comm'n Against Discrimination, 2006 Mass. Super. LEXIS 142 (Mass. Super. Ct., 2006)
Related proceeding at, Decision reached on appeal by Keyland Corp. v. Mass. Comm'n Against Discrimination, 2006 Mass. App. Unpub. LEXIS 100 (Mass. App. Ct., Dec. 14, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Bristol. Middlesex. Dukes. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on November 27, 2002. A motion to dismiss was heard by David A. McLaughlin, J. A proceeding for interlocutory review was heard in the Appeals Court by Charlotte A. Perretta, J. The Supreme Judicial Court granted an application for direct appellate review. Civil actions commenced in the Superior Court Department on February 27, April 9, and June 25, 2002, respectively. Questions of law were reported by Peter W. Agnes, Jr., Charles T. Spurlock, J., and Margaret R. Hinkle, J. The Supreme Judicial Court granted requests for direct review.
Wilfert Bros. Realty Co. v. Commonwealth, 2002 Mass. Super. LEXIS 454 (Mass. Super. Ct., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Findings entered; remanded to trial courts.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Complainant employees filed separate complaints with the Massachusetts Commission Against Discrimination (MCAD), alleging that respondent employers committed illegal discrimination. The MCAD found in favor of the employees in all four cases, and the Superior Court of Massachusetts, in and for Suffolk, Bristol, and Middlesex (Massachusetts), denied the employers' request for a jury trial de novo. The employers appealed.


OVERVIEW: Four employees who worked for different employers filed separate complaints with the MCAD, pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 151B, § 5, claiming that they were victims of illegal discrimination. The MCAD found that all four employers committed illegal discrimination, and it ordered each employer to compensate the employee. The four employers filed separate actions, pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 151B, § 6, seeking judicial review, and they requested a jury trial on the employees' allegations. The supreme judicial court held that (1) employers who sought judicial review of an action filed under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 151B, § 5 were entitled to review under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 30A, which did not include a jury trial on the employee's claims; (2) case law which allowed the MCAD to award damages for emotional distress was still valid; but (3) a finding of discrimination or retaliation was no longer sufficient, by itself, to permit an inference or presumption of emotional distress, and trial courts were required to ensure that a decision by the MCAD which awarded damages for emotional distress was supported by the evidence.


OUTCOME: The supreme judicial court struck the employers' request for a jury trial and remanded the cases to the superior court for review to determine if the MCAD's decision was supported by adequate evidence and did not violate the law.

 

211 of 756 DOCUMENTS


Peterson v. Comm'r of Revenue


SJC-09096


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


441 Mass. 420; 806 N.E.2d 78; 2004 Mass. LEXIS 159


February 5, 2004, Argued  
April 6, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at, Certified question answered by, Remanded by Peterson v. Comm'r of Revenue, 444 Mass. 128, 825 N.E.2d 1029, 2005 Mass. LEXIS 169 (Mass., Apr. 26, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on March 25, 2003. The case was reported by Sosman, J.



DISPOSITION: Matter was remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers challenged § 32 of the Revenue Enhancement Act of 2002, 2002 Mass. Acts 186, alleging that it violated Mass. Const. amend. art. 44 because it imposed different rates of taxation during 2002 on income derived from the same class of property. The matter was reserved and reported by a single justice for determination by the full court, based on a statement of agreed facts.


OVERVIEW: Prior to the enactment of the Act, long-term capital gains tax rates differed, based on the length of time that the asset was kept prior to sale or exchange. Each of the complaining taxpayers realized income from long-term capital gains in the calendar year after May 1, 2002, and were liable for a higher tax than if the same income had been realized prior to May 1, 2002. Accordingly, they challenged § 32 of the Act, alleging that it violated the uniformity requirement of Mass. Const. amend. art. 44 because it imposed different rates of taxation on income derived from the same class of property. The court first determined that long-term capital gain income was in fact income derived from property within the meaning of art. 44. Accordingly, it was subject to the uniformity requirement. The court concluded that the result of the effective date of May 1st for changing the long-term capital gains tax rate resulted in two separate tax rates on long-term capital gains realized in calendar year 2002, which violated Mass. Const. amend. art. 44. The court remanded for a determination of whether the effective date of the rate change was January 1st of 2002 or 2003.


OUTCOME: The court held the challenged section of the Act invalid, and remanded the matter for further proceedings as to when the change in rate became applicable.

 

212 of 756 DOCUMENTS


Pielech v. Massasoit Greyhound, Inc.


SJC-09080


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


441 Mass. 188; 804 N.E.2d 894; 2004 Mass. LEXIS 133; 93 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 749


December 1, 2003, Argued  
March 11, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Bristol. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on June 15, 1993. The case was heard by John J. O'Brien, J., on motions for summary judgment. Following review by this court, 423 Mass. 534, 668 N.E.2d 1298 (1996), a motion to amend the complaint was heard by Mitchell J. Sikora, Jr., J., and the case was consolidated by him with a second action commenced in the Superior Court Department on February 28, 1997. The consolidated cases were tried before John A. Tierney, J. The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.
Pielech v. Massasoit Greyhound, 1994 Mass. Super. LEXIS 653 (Mass. Super. Ct., 1994).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee employees sued appellant employer in the Superior Court for Bristol County (Massachusetts) for discrimination under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 151B, § 4(1A). The court denied the employee's motion to add a Title VII claim, and denied the employer's directed verdict motion. The jury found for the employees and awarded them damages. The trial judge denied the employer's motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict. The parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: The two employees, practicing Roman Catholics, alleged that they were discriminated against after the employer terminated their part-time jobs when they refused to work their regularly scheduled shift, which fell on Christmas Day. Pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 151B, § 4(1A), the jury found that the employer discriminated against the employees and that its refusal to accommodate the employees' religious beliefs was not because of an undue hardship. On appeal, the court found that the changes to ch. 151B, § 4(1A), brought about by 1997 Mass. Acts ch. 3, § 2, had a substantial effect on the employer's rights. Therefore, the retroactive application of those changes violated the employer's due process rights under the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution and Mass. Const. Decl. Rights art. 10. Accordingly, judgment notwithstanding the verdict should have been granted to the employer.


OUTCOME: The denial of the employer's motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict with respect to the issue of the retroactive application of the amended statute was reversed; the judgment for the employees was reversed and judgment was directed to be entered for the employer; and the motion judge's denial of the employees' motion to amend their complaint was affirmed.

 

213 of 756 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Knapp


SJC-09084


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


441 Mass. 157; 804 N.E.2d 885; 2004 Mass. LEXIS 130


December 2, 2003, Argued  
March 10, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected April 26, 2004. As Corrected March 19, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Suffolk. Civil action filed in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on July 8, 2003. The case was reported by Spina, J.



DISPOSITION: Case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A single justice of the Massachusetts Supreme Judicial Court asked the entire court, on a reservation and report, whether any provision of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 123A permitted the release of a person on probationary conditions after a judge had found probable cause to believe that the person was sexually dangerous and the Commonwealth had petitioned for a trial.


OVERVIEW: Before respondent, a sexual offender, was scheduled to be released from custody, the Commonwealth sought his commitment as a sexually dangerous person. The trial court found probable cause that he was a sexually dangerous person. At the conclusion of the Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 123A, § 13(a) examination period, the Commonwealth moved that he be further committed pending the trial on its petition. The trial judge denied the motion and allowed him to be released. The reviewing court found that Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 123A required that he be confined in a secure facility until the conclusion of trial. Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 123A, §§ 13, 14 required confinement at a secure facility after a finding of probable cause. The requirement that he be confined in a secure facility until the conclusion of trial did not violate due process. Given the procedural safeguards that protected him under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 123A, § 14, confinement was narrowly tailored to further a legitimate and compelling governmental interest, which was protection of the public from harm by persons likely to be sexually dangerous.


OUTCOME: The question was answered in the negative. The case was remanded for the single justice for proceedings consistent with the reviewing court's opinion.

215 of 756 DOCUMENTS


Fitchburg Gas & Elec. Light Co. v. Dep't of Telcoms. & Energy


SJC-08950


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


440 Mass. 625; 801 N.E.2d 220; 2004 Mass. LEXIS 9


October 8, 2003, Argued  
January 8, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected January 27, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on February 3, 2003. The case was reported by Cordy, J. Scott J. Mueller (Meabh Purcell with him) for the plaintiff.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the Department of Telecommunications and Energy, determined that plaintiff utility company overcharged its gas customers, and ordered it to refund the amount to ratepayers. The utility appealed under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 25, § 5. A single justice reserved and reported the matter, without decision, to the full court.


OVERVIEW: The Department found that the utility company improperly overcharged its ratepayers $ 675,052 by including inventory finance charges (IFCs) in both its base rate and its supplemental cost of gas adjustment clause (CGAC). On appeal from the refund order, the utility company claimed that, in the absence of evidence that a specific amount in its 1984 base rate was attributable to IFCs, the Department lacked substantial evidence that the company double charged consumers. The court disagreed. That the exact amount of IFCs collected through the base rate was unknown did not detract from the substantial weight of the evidence demonstrating that such charges were included in the base rate. The utility company also maintained that, in any event, any overcharges were not illegal as a matter of law, but the court determined that it failed to carry its heavy burden of proving that its overcharges were either permitted or endorsed by the Department. Next, the court determined that an order retroactively adjusting a CGAC was well within the Department's general supervisory authority over utility costs. The court also rejected the argument that the order constituted a confiscation.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case to county court where a judgment was to be entered affirming the Department's findings that the utility company illegally overcharged its customers $ 675,052, and its order requiring the utility company to reimburse its ratepayers for the overcharges in the manner specified by the Department.

 

216 of 756 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Cheney


SJC-09029


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


440 Mass. 568; 800 N.E.2d 309; 2003 Mass. LEXIS 902


November 3, 2003, Argued  
December 15, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected January 12, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Middlesex. Indictment. Constitutional Law, Separation of powers. Executive. Indictments found and returned in the Superior Court Department on July 31, 1997. Motions for pretrial probation and for trial were heard by Maria I. Lopez, J., and the cases were dismissed by her. The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Judge's orders vacated; case remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commonwealth appealed the Massachusetts Superior Court's dismissal of the indictments charging defendant with rape of a child under 16. The trial dismissed the case based on the "interests of public justice." The issue was whether Mass. Const. Decl. Rights art. 30 permitted a judge, prior to verdict, finding, or plea, to dismiss a legally adequate criminal indictment in the "interests of public justice" over the Commonwealth's objection.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled not guilty to all four indictments and moved for disposition under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 276, § 87, asking the court to place him on pretrial probation and to continue the case without a change of plea or an admission to sufficient facts. The Commonwealth objected to the use of pretrial probation as a disposition, requested that the indictments proceed to trial, and, in the alternative, demanded that the judge hold a hearing pursuant to Brandano before dismissing the indictments. The trial court placed defendant on pretrial probation for six months and indicated her intent to dismiss the case. The trial court denied the Commonwealth's motion to reconsider. The appellate court held that Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 265, § 23, explicitly forbid a prosecution of rape of a child from being placed on file or continued without a finding. The conclusion that judicial power did not extend to authorize a judge to dismiss an otherwise legally adequate indictment, prior to verdict, finding, or plea, in the "interests of public justice" was inescapable, as it would be a violation of the separation of powers as set out in Mass. Const. Decl. Rights art. 30.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was vacated. The matter was remanded for further proceedings.

 

217 of 756 DOCUMENTS


Goodridge v. Dep't of Pub. Health


SJC-08860


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


440 Mass. 309; 798 N.E.2d 941; 2003 Mass. LEXIS 814


March 4, 2003, Argued  
November 18, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected December 4, 2003.
Related proceeding at Opinions of the Justices to the Senate, 440 Mass. 1201, 802 N.E.2d 565, 2004 Mass. LEXIS 35 (2004)
Related proceeding at Largess v. Supreme Judicial Court for Mass., 317 F. Supp. 2d 77, 2004 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 8461 (D. Mass., 2004)
Appeal dismissed by Doyle v. Goodridge, 444 Mass. 1006, 827 N.E.2d 1255, 2005 Mass. LEXIS 228 (Mass., May 27, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on April 11, 2001. The case was heard by Thomas E. Connolly, J., on motions for summary judgment. The Supreme Judicial Court granted an application for direct appellate review.
Goodridge v. Dep't of Pub. Health, 2002 Mass. Super. LEXIS 153 (Mass. Super. Ct., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Superior court's grant of summary judgment for the Department of Public Health vacated; case remanded to superior court for entry of judgment for the plaintiffs. Entry of judgment to be stayed for 180 days to permit Massachusetts Legislature the opportunity to take any action deemed necessary in light of this opinion.



CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff marriage license applicants sued defendants, the state public health department and commissioner, in the Suffolk Superior Court Department (Massachusetts) for a judgment that their exclusion from access to marriage licenses violated Massachusetts law. The trial court granted defendants' summary judgment motion and denied that of the applicants. The applicants appealed, and the state supreme court granted direct appellate review.


OVERVIEW: The applicants could not obtain marriage licenses because same-sex marriages were not recognized. The state supreme court held Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 207, the marriage licensing statute, did not permit same-sex couples to marry. Denials of the applicants' attempts to marry involved individual liberty and equality safeguards of the Massachusetts Constitution, protecting freedom from unwarranted government intrusion into protected areas of life and freedom to partake in state benefits. Under the equality and liberty guarantees, regulatory authority had to be rationally related to a permissible legislative purpose. Chapter 207 was not rationally related to the Commonwealth's asserted rationales for prohibiting same-sex marriage: (1) providing a favorable setting for procreation; (2) ensuring a two-parent family with one parent of each sex for child rearing; and (3) preserving state and private financial resources. Procreation was not a necessary component of civil marriage, forbidding same-sex marriage would not increase opposite-sex marriages in which children were raised, and a ban on same-sex marriage was not justified by the alleged financial independence of same-sex couples.


OUTCOME: The trial court's summary judgment was vacated, and the matter was remanded to the trial court for entry of judgment, which was stayed for 180 days to allow the legislature to take such action as it deemed appropriate.

 

218 of 756 DOCUMENTS


General Mills, Inc. v. Comm'r of Revenue


SJC-08935


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


440 Mass. 154; 795 N.E.2d 552; 2003 Mass. LEXIS 637


May 8, 2003, Argued  
September 15, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected September 24, 2003.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by General Mills v. Comm'r of Revenue of Ma, 541 U.S. 973, 158 L. Ed. 2d 468, 124 S. Ct. 1878, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 2581 (U.S., Apr. 5, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Suffolk. Appeal from a decision of the Appellate Tax Board. The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court transferred to itself on its own initiative an appeal by plaintiffs, a parent corporation and its former subsidiaries, and a cross-appeal by defendant Massachusetts Commissioner of Revenue from a decision of the Appellate Tax Board, Suffolk (Massachusetts), that granted in part and denied in part the parent's and subsidiaries' claims for abatement of taxes paid at the time the subsidiaries were sold.


OVERVIEW: The parent corporation, a Minnesota food producer, owned two upscale mail order retailers, one in Washington and one in Massachusetts. The parent did not interfere in the subsidiaries' management, and ultimately sold both of them. When it sold the Massachusetts subsidiary, in a two-step transaction involving sales of tangible and intangible assets, the parent elected to treat the sale of stock as a sale of assets pursuant to I.R.C. § 338(h)(10). The court upheld as supported by substantial evidence all the administrative determinations. First, since the three entities did not operate as a unitary business, the sale of the Washington subsidiary had nothing to do with Massachusetts at all. Computing Massachusetts gross income just as federal gross income was computed, the income realized by the Massachusetts subsidiary from the deemed sale of assets was gross income in Massachusetts. Finally, since a sale of trademarks and other intangibles in a separate transfer through a specially established Delaware entity was undertaken solely to avoid taxation in Massachusetts, the sales of tangibles and intangibles were treated as a single source of gain taxable to the parent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the administrative decision.

Commonwealth v. Delisle


SJC-08898


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


440 Mass. 137; 794 N.E.2d 1191; 2003 Mass. LEXIS 633

DISPOSITION: Order revoking probation affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On its own motion, the court transferred to itself defendant's appeal from a judgment of the Superior Court Department, Suffolk (Massachusetts), revoking his probation and sentencing him to serve his previously suspended sentence. He argued that revocation amounted to the imposition of a substantial penalty for the exercise of his U.S. Const. amend. V right against compelled self-incrimination.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was convicted of violating an abuse protection order, assault and battery, witness intimidation, and attempted extortion, part of his sentence was suspended, subject to his compliance with certain probation conditions. One of the conditions was to participate in personal counseling or therapy. Defendant was expelled from a private counseling program, in which he had been enrolled, for noncooperation that included additional incidents of domestic abuse. When he sought to re-enroll, one of the conditions set by the program was his writing a letter acknowledging his acts of domestic violence. He refused, and his probation was revoked. On appeal, defendant argued that the letter requirement violated his guarantees against self-incrimination under U.S. Const. amends. V and XIV and Mass. Const. Decl. Rights art. XII (although he failed to flesh out the latter argument). The high court held that there had been no State compulsion. The counseling program not the State, had set the letter requirement after defendant had placed himself in noncompliance after being expelled.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order revoking probation.

Querubin v. Commonwealth


SJC-08826


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


440 Mass. 108; 795 N.E.2d 534; 2003 Mass. LEXIS 628


May 6, 2003, Argued  
September 9, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected October 28, 2003. As Corrected September 24, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on July 11, 2002. The case was reported by Spina, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order by the Supreme Judicial Court for the County of Suffolk (Massachusetts) that denied his motion to be admitted to bail under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 276, § 57; defendant that his constitutional due process rights were violated.


OVERVIEW: After defendant eluded police and failed to appear before a grand jury, he was held without bail. The supreme judicial court held that § 57 was narrowly tailored to the State's legitimate and compelling interest in assuring defendant's presence at trial. The trial judge's inherent powers included the power to order defendant held without bail. The trial court held a hearing and considered the factors for bail under Mass. Super. Ct. Bail R. 2 (1972) in determining that defendant was a flight risk. Defendant was known to use an alias, eluded several police officers, and failed to appear. Therefore, defendant's due process rights under U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Mass. Const. Decl. Rights art. 12 were not violated. The standard for admitting a person to bail was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

Paquette v. Commonwealth


SJC-08938


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


440 Mass. 121; 795 N.E.2d 521; 2003 Mass. LEXIS 629


May 6, 2003, Argued  
September 9, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected September 24, 2003.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by PAQUETTE, DONALD v. MASSACHUSETTS, 540 U.S. 1150, 157 L. Ed. 2d 1044, 124 S. Ct. 1153, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 697 (U.S., Jan. 20, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on October 21, 2002. The case was reported by Spina, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order by the Fall River District Court (Massachusetts) that revoked his bail pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 276, § 58; defendant claimed, inter alia, that his constitutional rights to substantive and procedural due process were violated.


OVERVIEW: After a defendant was arrested and arraigned for violating an abuse prevention order, he was released on his own recognizance. He was later arrested for violating the same order. The judge found probable cause to believe that defendant had committed a new crime while on bail and that he was dangerous. The judge denied defendant's request to reopen because defendant's arguments went to the merits of the case. The supreme judicial court held that § 58 was not vague and did not violate substantive or procedural due process. Defendant's liberty not violated. The judge had the inherent power to revoke bail for breach of any condition of release. The judge could properly rely on the information in the police report to determine probable cause. Defendant was given a hearing and the judge made findings on a preprinted form.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

 

222 of 756 DOCUMENTS


Haverty v. Comm'r of Corr.


SJC-08951


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


440 Mass. 1; 792 N.E.2d 989; 2003 Mass. LEXIS 583


April 8, 2003, Argued  
August 8, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on June 30, 1995. After review by this court, 437 Mass. 737, 776 N.E.2d 973 (2002), further proceedings were had before Patrick J. King, J. An application for leave to prosecute an interlocutory appeal was allowed by Cordy, J., in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk, and the case was reported by him.
Haverty v. Comm'r of Corr., 437 Mass. 737, 776 N.E.2d 973, 2002 Mass. LEXIS 630 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Question answered; case remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court Department, Suffolk (Massachusetts), granted plaintiff inmates' prayer for earned good time credit under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 127, § 129D. Defendant commissioner of correction's application for interlocutory review and a stay were granted by a single justice of the instant court, who reported the matter to the full court with questions regarding the trial judge's power to grant equitable relief.


OVERVIEW: The inmates had been improperly housed in near solitary confinement for nondisciplinary reasons, and were entitled to procedural protections. The commissioner argued that the trial court erred by fashioning an equitable remedy that awarded good time credits that were not earned, in disregard of the requirements of § 129D. The high court held that the trial court did not have the power to grant equitable relief to the inmates in the form of good-time credits. The commissioner's decision to limit the opportunities for inmates in the East Wing to earn good time credits was based on a rational determination to allocate resources where they could be utilized most effectively. That decision was within the commissioner's discretion. The inmates were not illegally denied the opportunity to earn good-time credits. The administrative decision that resulted in the wrongful confinement of the inmates was unrelated to the decision to offer fewer opportunities to earn good-time credits, and, therefore, the order necessitated by the former should not have implicated the latter.


OUTCOME: The question was answered in the negative. The trial court erred in grating good-time credits.

 

223 of 756 DOCUMENTS


Brittle v. City of Boston


SJC-08844


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


439 Mass. 580; 790 N.E.2d 208; 2003 Mass. LEXIS 449


January 9, 2003, Argued  
June 20, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.
Brittle v. City of Boston, 54 Mass. App. Ct. 820, 768 N.E.2d 576, 2002 Mass. App. LEXIS 738 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff police officer (employee) was suspended after being indicted for stalking and threatening. He was then indicted in federal court on numerous drug-related charges. After pleading guilty to all of the federal charges, he sought back pay, pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 268A, § 25. The trial court granted summary judgment to defendant city, which was reversed by the Appeals Court (Massachusetts). The city was granted further review.


OVERVIEW: While the federal case was proceeding to trial, the city obtained an order of nolle prosequi of its pending indictments, as the state and federal charges were directly related. In seeking compensation, the employee argued that he was entitled to back pay because the original indictments terminated without a finding or verdict of guilty. The highest appellate court found that the relief sought was neither compelled by the language of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 268A, § 25, nor consistent with the statute's purpose. The employee was under indictment during the entire period. He was never eligible to perform any public duties during that time and was most assuredly not entitled to reinstatement. The highest appellate court found that the criminal proceedings against him did not terminate until he pleaded guilty to the federal indictments. Those proceedings were considered to have terminated in a finding or verdict of guilty, under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 268A, § 25. The employee could not benefit from his criminal conduct at the expense of the taxpayers merely because the federal and state prosecutors cooperated to bring him to justice, and dismissed the state charges.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed, denying the employee all compensation lost during his suspension.

 

224 of 756 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Quinn


SJC-08881


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


439 Mass. 492; 789 N.E.2d 138; 2003 Mass. LEXIS 439


March 7, 2003, Argued  
May 30, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected July 10, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Suffolk. Complaint received and sworn to in the West Roxbury Division of the District Court Department on April 6, 2001. A motion to dismiss was heard by Robert C. Rufo, J., and questions of law were reported by him to the Appeals Court. The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the matter from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Our answers to the reported questions are: 1. Exposure or attempted exposure of genitalia is not an essential element of an open and gross lewdness offense prosecuted under G. L. c. 272, § 16. 2. The defendant did not have fair notice that exposure of "thong" clad buttocks could be prosecuted as an open and gross lewdness offense under G. L. c. 272, § 16.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with open and gross lewdness, under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, § 16, after pulling his pants down in front of four 13-year-old girls, exposing his buttocks, along with a pair of red "thong" underwear. After denying his motion to dismiss, the judge reported two questions to the Appeals Court (Massachusetts): was exposure of genitalia an essential element of the charge, and was there fair notice? The report was then transferred.


OVERVIEW: The trial court reported the instant questions to the lower appellate court, pursuant to Mass. R. Crim. P. 34. The highest appellate court then transferred the report to itself. Defendant argued that showing his "thong" underwear was not a crime, and pointed to the number of people who were seen wearing "thongs" on public beaches. The highest appellate court found that it could be a crime. A conviction of open and gross lewdness required the Commonwealth to prove, among other elements, intention, manner, and impact. The gross lewdness had to be done in such a way as to produce alarm or shock, and it had to, in fact, cause alarm or shock to the victim. Therefore, exposing buttocks, with "thong" underwear, such as defendant did to the 13-year-old girls, in a school area where it was totally unexpected, could constitute gross lewdness, while wearing the same "thongs" on a beach might not. There was no requirement for the exposure of genitalia. However, the highest appellate court found that defendant in the instant case was not provided fair notice that deliberately exposing his thong-clad buttocks might be illegal. The statute was therefore unconstitutionally vague as applied to him.


OUTCOME: Exposure or attempted exposure of genitalia was not an essential element of an open and gross lewdness offense prosecuted under the instant statute. Defendant did not have fair notice that exposure of "thong" clad buttocks could be prosecuted as an open and gross lewdness offense under the statute.

Globe Newspaper Co. v. DA for the Middle Dist.


SJC-08818


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


439 Mass. 374; 788 N.E.2d 513; 2003 Mass. LEXIS 427


January 6, 2003, Argued  
May 15, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on November 4, 1998. The case was heard by Margaret R. Hinkle, J., on motions for summary judgment. The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.
Globe Newspaper Co. v. Conte, 2001 Mass. Super. LEXIS 328 (Mass. Super. Ct., 2001)



DISPOSITION: On direct review, case was remanded to the Superior Court for modification.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff newspaper sued defendant district attorneys, seeking a judgment declaring that information the newspaper requested was subject to disclosure under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 66, § 10. The Superior Court, Suffolk (Massachusetts), held that certain docket numbers the newspaper requested were subject to disclosure, and the district attorneys appealed. The state supreme court transferred the case from the intermediate appellate court.


OVERVIEW: A newspaper sent a request to the Attorney General of Massachusetts and to each district attorney in Massachusetts requesting the docket number, defendant's name, municipality, and charge for each case involving municipal corruption that was prosecuted between 1993 and June 1998. The Attorney General and two district attorneys provided the information, but other district attorneys refused to provide the information, arguing that the Massachusetts Criminal Offender Record Information (CORI) statute, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 6, § 167 et seq., prohibited them from releasing the information. The newspaper sued the district attorneys who refused to release the information and obtained a judgment declaring that certain docket numbers were subject to disclosure. On appeal, the state supreme court held that docket numbers of criminal cases prosecuted in public judicial proceedings, correlated with information that was also available from a court or other public records, but not correlated with defendant-specific information, were public records that were subject to mandatory disclosure under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 66, § 10, and disclosure was not prohibited by the CORI statute.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court held that the trial court's declaration was correct with respect to the type of records requested by the newspaper, but the wording of the trial court's declaration had to be modified slightly to avoid erroneous application of the declaration to other types of record requests, and it remanded the case to the trial court for modification of its declaration.

Town of Sudbury v. Scott


SJC-08759


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


439 Mass. 288; 787 N.E.2d 536; 2003 Mass. LEXIS 356


November 5, 2002, Argued  
May 1, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified May 22, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Land Court Department on March 27, 2000. The case was heard by Peter W. Kilborn, J., on motions for summary judgment. The Supreme Judicial Court granted an application for direct appellate review.
Town of Sudbury v. Mahoney, 2001 Mass. LCR LEXIS 109 (2001)



DISPOSITION: Vacated, remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff town sought specific performance of its option to purchase a locus on the same terms as defendant trustee, pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 61A, § 14, alleging that defendant corporation's sale to the trustee was for nonagricultural purposes. The Land Court Department (Massachusetts) granted summary judgment for the trustee. The town appealed.


OVERVIEW: The locus was assessed as agricultural land and thus was taxed at a lower rate than other land. Defendant former locus owners transferred the locus to defendant corporation, which they formed, and the corporation sold the locus to the trustee for the benefit of defendant trust. The trustee warranted by recorded affidavit that he would use the locus for agricultural purposes. He later contracted to sell the locus to defendant developer, which planned to build residences thereon. Under § 14, if agricultural land was sold for or converted to non-agricultural uses, the town had, for 120 days, a first refusal option to buy the land. The land court found that the town's evidence did not show that, when the trustee acquired the locus, he intended to use it entirely for nonagricultural purposes. The appellate court vacated the judgment. The town presented evidence indicating that the trustee never intended to use the locus for agricultural purposes. The land court's finding that the trustee intended to retain a large portion of the locus in agricultural use was inappropriate in the summary judgment context, as in so doing the trial court posed and then decided a question of fact.


OUTCOME: The judgment was vacated and the case was remanded for further proceedings. If it was determined that the trustee acquired the locus for nonagricultural use, the land court was to determine (a) when the town received constructive notice that the trustee acquired the locus for nonagricultural use, and (b) whether the town exercised its option to purchase within a reasonable time of receiving constructive notice.

Keene v. Brigham & Women's Hosp., Inc.


SJC-08894


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


439 Mass. 223; 786 N.E.2d 824; 2003 Mass. LEXIS 347


January 9, 2003, Argued January 9, 2003  
April 22, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified May 15, 2003.
Motion denied by Keene v. Brigham & Women's Hosp., Inc., 2004 Mass. Super. LEXIS 67 (Mass. Super. Ct., Feb. 20, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Norfolk. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on May 12, 1995. A pretrial motion for sanctions was heard by Thomas E. Connelly, J., and a hearing on assessment of damages was had before Judith Fabricant, J. After review by the Appeals Court, the Supreme Judicial Court granted leave to obtain further appellate review.
Keene v. Brigham & Women's Hosp., Inc., 56 Mass. App. Ct. 10, 775 N.E.2d 725, 2002 Mass. App. LEXIS 1184 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Judgment imposing liability on the defendant affirmed. The assessment of damages in the judgment vacated. Damages are to be assessed in the amount of $ 20,000 plus interest and costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant hospital appealed from a judgment of the Massachusetts Appeals Court affirming a trial court's entry of default judgment in favor of plaintiff severely injured child, suing by his parents, as a sanction for the hospital's loss of medical records, and affirming the additional sanction of striking the affirmative defense of the Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 231, § 85K, cap on damages awardable against public charities.


OVERVIEW: The child was severely handicapped by neonatal meningitis that was not diagnosed or treated in time. By the time the child's parents requested his medical records from the hospital, the records for a critical 18-hour period had disappeared, so it was not possible to determine who had been treating him. The child therefore sued only the hospital. The high court found no abuse of discretion in the trial court's decision to impose the extreme sanction of summary judgment for what was in essence spoliation of evidence, since it was not at all clear that the loss of the records, which violated Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 111, § 70, had been purely an accident, and, in any case, the harm suffered by the child and his family as a result of the destruction of the evidence was in itself catastrophic, as it deprived them of a cause of action against persons whose liability was not limited by Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 231, § 85K. Since the $ 20,000 statutory cap on damages awardable against charities admitted of no exceptions, however, even though it was presented as an affirmative defense for pleading purposes, it was not a defense that the trial court had the power to strike.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the default judgment as to liability, but vacated the assessment of damages and directed that damages be assessed in the amount of the statutory cap, plus interest and costs.

 

228 of 756 DOCUMENTS


Route One Liquors, Inc. v. Sec'y of Admin. & Fin.


SJC-08880


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


439 Mass. 111; 785 N.E.2d 1222; 2003 Mass. LEXIS 264


February 3, 2003, Argued February 3, 2003  
April 3, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified May 15, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Norfolk. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on April 17, 2001. The case was heard by Robert A. Mulligan, J., on motions for summary judgment. The Supreme Judicial Court granted an application for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs,18 parking lot operators and owners, sued defendant Massachusetts Secretary of Administration and Finance, seeking a declaratory judgment that 1999 Mass. Acts ch. 16, as amended by 2000 Mass. Acts ch. 72, §§ 4-6, dealing with an excise tax, was unconstitutional. The Superior Court, Norfolk (Massachusetts), entered judgment, granting the Secretary's motion for summary judgment. The owners' application for direct review was granted.


OVERVIEW: The law created a parking and traffic management zone, which was defined as the area within the Towns of Foxborough, Sharon, Walpole, and Wrentham, Massachusetts, within a three mile radius of the center of a football stadium. It provided that an annual aggregate amount of $ 400,000 would be collected from those who were licensed to operate open-air parking lots within the parking and traffic management zone for stadium events, under Mass. Acts ch. 16, § 7(b)(2), as amended by 2000 Mass. Acts ch. 72, § 4. The owners argued that the law at issue was unconstitutional under numerous provisions of the state and federal constitutions. The secretary conceded, for purposes of the instant litigation, that this was an excise tax. The appellate court found that the power of the state to impose excises on business corporations was very broad, subject only to reasonableness. The instant tax did not constitute an improper taking. It was undertaken with a valid public purpose and the taxes were to be deposited into the general fund. The promotion of public safety was an important public purpose, and any private benefits were merely incidental. The law was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

229 of 756 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Dykens


SJC-07835


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


438 Mass. 827; 784 N.E.2d 1107; 2003 Mass. LEXIS 192


January 10, 2003, Argued  
March 14, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motions ruled upon by Dykens v. Allen, 2005 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 14601 (D. Mass., June 17, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Essex. Indictments found and returned in the Superior Court Department on June 12, 1996. The cases were tried before Joseph A. Grasso, Jr., J., and a motion for a new trial, filed on March 1, 1999, was heard by him.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed. Order denying motion for a new trial affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 278, § 33E, the court granted direct review of a judgment on jury verdict of the Superior Court Department, Essex (Massachusetts), which convicted him of first-degree murder, kidnapping, and aggravated rape. On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court conducted the jury charge in a manner that deprived him of a public trial by jury and that his counsel was ineffective.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged and convicted as a principal in a brutal rape-murder, although he claimed to have been too drunk to form an intent to assist his friend in the actual violence. The high court, as it was required to do in capital cases, reviewed the proceedings in detail, and found no error. The trial court acted within its discretion in allowing jurors to take notes during the complicated part of the charge dealing with liability as a principal, but forbidding them to take notes during the general instructions, because such principles as reasonable doubt were constantly reiterated throughout the charge. There was also nothing unreasonable about forbidding people to enter or leave the courtroom during the charge. As these actions were proper, counsel was not ineffective in failing to object to them, nor should counsel have objected to jury instructions that were correct statements of law, or, in one case, at worst harmless error. Counsel's frank admission that defendant was present during the crime did not preclude the presentation of the best defense possible for a client who offered very few bases for a defense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of conviction as well as the trial court's denial of defendant's motion for a new trial.

Commonwealth v. Blevines


SJC-08810


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


438 Mass. 604; 782 N.E.2d 491; 2003 Mass. LEXIS 104


December 3, 2002, Argued  
January 30, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Plymouth. Complaint received and sworn to in the Brockton Division of the District Court Department on September 10, 1999. A pretrial motion to suppress evidence was heard by James F.X. Dinneen, J. An application for leave to prosecute an interlocutory appeal was allowed by Abrams, J., in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk, and the appeal was reported by her to the Appeals Court. After review by the Appeals Court, the Supreme Judicial Court granted leave to obtain further review.
 Commonwealth v. Blevines, 54 Mass. App. Ct. 89, 763 N.E.2d 522, 2002 Mass. App. LEXIS 282 (2002).



DISPOSITION: Order denying motion to suppress reversed; case remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commonwealth applied for further appellate review after the appeals court (Massachusetts), in an interlocutory appeal, concluded that the district court should have allowed defendant's motion to suppress evidence.


OVERVIEW: A police officer approached defendant after observing him with an open container. When defendant gave what the officer concluded to be a false name and age, the officer arrested defendant for drinking in public and frisked him, recovering a key chain, which he placed on the police car's roof. The officer, along with another, used the keys to unlock a nearby car, in hopes of ascertaining defendant's identity, at which time one of the officers noticed cocaine in the car through the front windshield. Defendant was charged and sought to suppress the keys and cocaine. The district court denied the motion to suppress, but the appeals court determined that suppression was required, and reversed the district court's denial of the motion to suppress. The supreme court held that the search and seizure of the keys was permissible under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 276, § 1 as a search incident to arrest where the hard object could have been used as a weapon. However, the use of the keys as an investigatory tool was improper and the impropriety tainted the discovery of the cocaine because the police were entitled to remove the keys only for safety reasons and not for investigative purposes.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the district court's order denying the motion to suppress and remanded the case to the district court for further proceedings.

First Justice of the Bristol Div. of the Juvenile Court Dep't v. Clerk-Magistrate of the Bristol Div. of the Juvenile Court Dep't


SJC-08812


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


438 Mass. 387; 780 N.E.2d 908; 2003 Mass. LEXIS 5


October 10, 2002, Argued  
January 7, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Modified January 10, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on December 24, 2001. The case was reported by Greaney, J.



DISPOSITION: Case remanded to the single justice for the entry of a suitable judgment in the county court in accordance with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A single justice reported to the full court an action commenced in Suffolk County (Massachusetts) in which plaintiff judges challenged the constitutionality of statutory amendments contained in 2001 Mass. Acts ch. 177, arguing that they granted powers to defendant clerks and probation commissioners that contravened Mass. Const. Decl. Rights art. 30 and that the amendments were enacted in violation of Mass. Const. amend. art. 63.


OVERVIEW: The amendments challenged by the judges inserted new language into many statutes dealing with court administration, defining the responsibilities of court clerks, probation commissioners, and others, for running their offices and filling vacancies. The amendments provided for review by and consultation with the Massachusetts Chief Justice for Administration and Management on decisions. The high court held that the amendments did not violate separation of powers principles, nor did they usurp the judges' inherent powers to run their courtrooms. Construed narrowly, the amendments simply clarified administrative powers that the clerks and commissioners had exercised all along. The high court saw no reason to interfere in the legislative decision to enact the amendments as part of an appropriations bill, deferring to the legislature's power to determine its own internal processes.


OUTCOME: The court found no constitutional problems with the amendments and remanded the matter to the single justice for entry of a suitable judgment, in the county court, in accordance with its opinion.

Greater Boston Real Estate Bd. v. Dep't of Telcomms. & Energy


SJC-08761


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


438 Mass. 197; 779 N.E.2d 127; 2002 Mass. LEXIS 859


October 8, 2002, Argued  
November 27, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected January 17, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on November 3, 2000. The case was heard by Mitchell J. Sikora, J., on a motion for summary judgment. The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Case remanded to the Superior Court for an order vacating both the injunction and the declaratory judgment. Judgment entered declaring that both the second paragraph of the definition of "utility" in 220 Code Mass. Regs. § 45.02, and 220 Code Mass. Regs. § 45.04(2)(h) are invalid as beyond the authority of the Department of Telecommunications and Energy under G. L. c. 166, § 25A.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Massachusetts Department of Telecommunications and Energy and the Smart Buildings Policy Project appealed a Suffolk Superior Court (Massachusetts) ruling that Mass. Regs. Code tit. 220, §§ 45.02, 45.03(1) (2000) effected an unconstitutional taking. The ruling also permanently enjoined the Department from implementing the regulations as to private landowners. The supreme court transferred the case on its own motion.


OVERVIEW: The second paragraph of the definition of "utility" in Mass. Regs. Code tit. 220, § 45.02 (2000), which included commercial and multiple dwelling unit buildings, reached private parties who were outside the legislatively granted scope of the department's authority, and was thus ultra vires. Mass. Regs. Code tit. 220, § 45.03(1) (2000) was similarly invalid. The Department's expansion of the definition of "utility" to include a recipient of services was a radical change in the historical use of the word by the legislature. The regulations at issue were designed to regulate private property owners who did not fall within the class of persons that the legislature authorized the Department to regulate and were ultra vires of the enabling legislation, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 166, § 25A. Because Mass. Regs. Code tit. 220, § 45.03(1) no longer applied to buildings or to private landowners, the basis for challenging its validity was eliminated. The supreme court vacated an order for injunctive relief because it was not necessary in the circumstances.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded for an order vacating both the injunction and the declaratory judgment with a judgment to enter as ordered.

Commonwealth v. Evans


SJC-08317


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


438 Mass. 142; 778 N.E.2d 885; 2002 Mass. LEXIS 853

November 21, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected January 17, 2003.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Evans v. Massachusetts, 538 U.S. 966, 123 S. Ct. 1763, 155 L. Ed. 2d 521, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 2815 (Apr. 7, 2003)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Ware v. O'Brien, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 41400 (D. Mass., May 15, 2009)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Ware v. Pepe, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 139082 (D. Mass., Dec. 30, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: Suffolk. Indictments found and returned in the Superior Court Department, two on May 17, 1993, and four on August 27, 1993, respectively. The cases were tried before Thomas E. Connolly, J.

DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed from judgments of the Superior Court Department, Suffolk (Massachusetts), convicting them of first-degree murder, robbery, and related offenses, and sentencing them to long consecutive sentences.


OVERVIEW: Defendants, two brothers, assaulted and attempted to rob the primary eyewitness against them only minutes before robbing and killing the victim. Separately or together, they raised 10 different grounds in their direct appeal. The high court held that the evidence was more than adequate to convict both defendants. There was nothing unconstitutional about, nor any abuse of discretion in, denying a defendant the right to be present at a jury view. There was no prejudice to defendants from the reference to their experts' presence at certain DNA testing. A mask not used in the robberies was admissible as evidence that a defendant possessed the means to commit a crime. A proffered memoramdum did not quality as past recollection recorded. Finally, failure to flee was not probative of consciousness of innocence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments and declined to exercise its authority to intervene in the result where required in the interests of justice.
