Blixt v. Blixt


SJC-08643


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


437 Mass. 649; 774 N.E.2d 1052; 2002 Mass. LEXIS 541


February 5, 2002, Argued  
September 9, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected November 1, 2002. Writ of certiorari denied: Blixt v. Blixt, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 1136 (U.S. Feb. 24, 2003).


PRIOR HISTORY: Civil action commenced in the Plymouth Division of the Probate and Family Court Department on June 5, 2000. A motion to dismiss was heard by Catherine P. Sabaitis, J. The Supreme Judicial Court granted an application for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: On direct review, trial court's judgment dismissing the complaint was vacated and the case was ordered to stand for further proceedings in the Probate and Family Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant grandfather sued appellee mother in the Plymouth Division of the Probate and Family Court Department (Massachusetts) for visitation with the mother's child under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 119, § 39D. The trial court declared the statute unconstitutional and granted the mother's motion to dismiss the complaint. The grandfather appealed. The mother filed an application for direct appellate review.


OVERVIEW: The mother was living apart from the adjudicated father of the child. The maternal grandfather sought visitation rights to the child. The trial court agreed with the mother's claim that the grandparent visitation rights statute was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court found that the statute survived a facial challenge on due process grounds and also did not violate equal protection insofar as the mother's statutory classification was concerned. The statute satisfied strict scrutiny because the appellate court's construction of the statute narrowly tailored it to further the compelling state interest in protecting the welfare of a child who had experienced a disruption in the family unit from harm. Because the classification narrowed the impact of the statute, while furthering a compelling State interest, it survived the equal protection challenge. Therefore, the action should not have been dismissed.


OUTCOME: The judgment dismissing the complaint was vacated, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

Commonwealth v. Gentile


SJC-08517


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


437 Mass. 569; 773 N.E.2d 428; 2002 Mass. LEXIS 531


May 10, 2002, Argued  
August 20, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Plymouth. Indictment found and returned in the Superior Court Department on September 3, 1999. Pretrial motions to suppress evidence were heard by Richard J. Chin, J., and the case was tried before him.



DISPOSITION: On direct appeal, trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts) of murder in the first degree on the theories of deliberate premeditation, extreme atrocity or cruelty, and felony-murder (with aggravated rape as the predicate felony). He appealed.


OVERVIEW: The victim telephoned her mother and said her car would not start but that the man who lent her the cell phone was giving her a ride. When the victim did not show up, her mother called police, who traced the cell phone to defendant. He went to the police, admitted giving the victim a ride, and said he smoked marijuana with her. He did not consent to a search of his car, since, he said, it contained a "pot pipe." Police seized his truck and clothes. The victim's body was later found, and defendant's semen was found mingled with her blood. The appellate court held that the warrantless seizure of the truck and clothes to prevent destruction of evidence was proper, as police had probable cause to believe they might provide evidence that defendant harmed the victim. Defendant's admission of drug use provided further justification to seize the truck. Though the prosecutor's statements that the victim "didn't deserve to die this way," and that a defense tactic was "despicable" were improper, they did not create a substantial likelihood of a miscarriage of justice, as the evidence of guilt was very strong. The victim's diaries were properly excluded under the rape-shield statute.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Gavin G.


SJC-08672


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


437 Mass. 470; 772 N.E.2d 1067; 2002 Mass. LEXIS 523


April 2, 2002, Argued  
August 12, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Essex. Complaints received and sworn to in the Essex County Division of the Juvenile Court Department on July 17, 2000. Entry of judgments of dismissal was ordered by David A. Lowy, J., and a motion to expunge the record was heard by Michael F. Edgerton, J. The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant commissioner of probation appealed from that portion of a judgment of the Juvenile Court Department, Essex County Division (Massachusetts), that allowed appellee juvenile's motion to expunge his probation records. On its own initiative, the court transferred the appeal to itself from the Massachusetts Appeals Court.


OVERVIEW: There was considerable evidence that the juvenile's arrest for disorderly conduct was a mistake resulting from his presence near the scene of a fight. The charges were eventually dismissed on his motion, and he also moved for expungement of his police and probation records. The high court held that while the trial court had the authority to order expungement of a juvenile's police record, since otherwise he would have had no remedy, it lacked authority to order expungement of the probation department records because Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 276 contained a very detailed statutory scheme that protected juveniles' records. Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 276, § 100A severely restricted access to the information in the records, and Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 276, § 100B provided the method for having the records sealed altogether. The plain language of the statutes indicated that these were the remedies to which juveniles were to look.


OUTCOME: The court reversed that portion of the expungement order that was directed at probation records, and remanded the matter to the trial court for entry of an order consistent with its opinion.

Gen. Laws ch. 29, § 9C, reducing allotments for certain appropriations previously made by the legislature, commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court, Suffolk (Massachusetts), to the full court.

Although the appropriations power was a power of the legislative department, the executive department was responsible for expenditures.


OUTCOME: The court upheld the governor's action, and remanded the matter to the county court for entry of a judgment declaring the action proper and constitutional.

In re Dutil


SJC-08524


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


437 Mass. 9; 768 N.E.2d 1055; 2002 Mass. LEXIS 299


October 4, 2001, Argued  
May 17, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Dutil v. Murphy, 2008 U.S. App. LEXIS 25353 (1st Cir. Mass., Dec. 15, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Norfolk. Petition for a writ of habeas corpus filed in the Superior Court Department on August 2, 1999. The case was heard by Judith Fabricant, J. The Supreme Judicial Court granted an application for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: On direct review, trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sexual offender was adjudged a sexually dangerous person and confined to a treatment center pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 123A. He filed a pro se petition for habeas corpus, challenging the constitutionality of his commitment. The Superior Court, Norfolk, Massachusetts, denied the petition. The state's highest court granted the offender's application for direct appellate review.


OVERVIEW: The offender committed indecent assault and battery on a child under the age of 14. Soon after being released from prison, he committed four more separate offenses of the same crime. After completing his prison sentence, he was committed to a treatment center as a sexually dangerous person. The state's highest court construed the pre-1990 version of ch. 123A in conformity with substantive due process requirements, and concluded that the offender's commitment did not violate his right to substantive due process or any of the other constitutional rights he claimed. Chapter 123A met the requirements of Hendricks as it required a finding that the offender suffered from a mental condition that created a likelihood that he would engage in sexually dangerous conduct in the future, and that the prohibited behavior was the result of a mental condition that caused a serious difficulty in controlling behavior. Further, ch. 123A was remedial, not punitive; thus the prohibitions of ex post facto and double jeopardy did not apply.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

In re Enforcement of a Subpoena


SJC-08633

Constitutional Law, Freedom of speech and press, Privacy, Impoundment order. Privacy. Practice, Civil, Discovery. Petition filed in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on July 16, 2001. The case was heard by Spina, J.



DISPOSITION: Single justice's order enforcing subpoena affirmed; order impounding the subpoened papers affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner commission sought to enforce a subpoena and impound papers filed in connection with it. A justice ordered the papers impounded. A witness's motion to stay, vacate, or modify the order was denied. The justice ordered the witness to comply with the subpoena. The Suffolk Supreme Judicial Court (Massachusetts) denied the witness's motion for reconsideration, or, in the alternative, for a stay pending appeal. The witness appealed.


OVERVIEW: The action arose during the commission's investigation of a judge's handling of a specific case. The witness against whom the subpoena was served was the judge's spouse. The witness contended that the justice committed an error of law in enforcing the subpoena and in ordering impoundment. On appeal, the supreme judicial court held (1) the witness lacked standing to complain that the judge had not been afforded the full protection she was entitled to under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 211, § 5(1); (2) the witness failed to show how requiring him to comply with the subpoena would chill his rights of expression or association; (3) there was nothing abusive or improper in the commission's inquiry of the judge's friends and supporters as part of the investigation; (4) the privacy interests of the witness and the judge were protected by the commission's confidentiality provisions; and (5) there was no abuse of discretion in the justice's impoundment order, as was supported by the fact that the judge under investigation had not waived her right to confidentiality.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

McClure v. Sec'y of the Commonwealth


SJC-08715


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


436 Mass. 614; 766 N.E.2d 847; 2002 Mass. LEXIS 273


March 7, 2002, Argued  
April 29, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Writ of certiorari denied: McClure v. Galvin, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 8506 (U.S. Nov. 18, 2002).


PRIOR HISTORY: Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the Commonwealth on November 16, 2001. After referral to the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk, the action was returned to the Commonwealth court by Greaney, J., to proceed on an expedited basis.



DISPOSITION: Redistricting plan was held to be constitutional and judgment was entered for defendant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, registered voters living in various precincts of a town, sought declaratory, injunctive, and mandamus relief against defendant, Secretary of the Commonwealth of Massachusetts, to invalidate a 2001 Mass. Acts. ch. 125, § 1 redistricting plan for the 2002 general election for the 160 representative districts of the Massachusetts House of Representatives.


OVERVIEW: The voters argued (1) § 1 was unconstitutional under Mass. Const. amend. art. 101, amended by Mass. Const. amend. arts. 109, 117, 119, (art. 101) since it put portions of the town in four representative districts when art. 101's requirements could be satisfied by dividing it into fewer districts, and (2) the redistricting was unconstitutional partisan gerrymandering violating the Equal Protection Clause. The 2000 United States census showed that, as a result of population growth and shifts, the representative districts no longer met federal population equality standards and had to be significantly altered. The new ideal representative district population was 39,682 persons. All recommended districts were within the federal constitutional purposes presumptively permissible plus or minus five percent range standard. Article 101's emphasis was on population, not territorial, equality. There was no best plan. The voters did not demonstrate beyond a reasonable doubt the legislature's exercise of its discretion was unreasonable or was purposeful political gerrymandering leading to a disproportionately low representation of Republicans in the house as a whole.


OUTCOME: The supreme judicial court entered its judgment for the secretary declaring that the statutory redistricting plan did not violate the commonwealth's constitution or equal protection constitutionality requirements and otherwise denying the relief requested by the voters.

Commonwealth v. Moses


SJC-08374


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


436 Mass. 598; 766 N.E.2d 827; 2002 Mass. LEXIS 270


January 11, 2002, Argued  
April 26, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Indictments found and returned in the Superior Court Department on February 23, 1996. The cases were tried before James D. McDaniel, Jr., J.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted, in the Suffolk Superior Court Department (Massachusetts) of murder in the first degree on theories of deliberate premeditation and extreme atrocity or cruelty, unlawful possession of a firearm, and unlawful possession of ammunition. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: In response to defendant's assignments of error, the supreme judicial court held (1) the evidence was sufficient to sustain the conviction for murder where it showed a significant disproportion between the means necessary to cause death and those used, as well as a significant number of extensive wounds; (2) admission of a dying declaration was not in error where the circumstances supported a finding that the declarant believed death was imminent at the time he made the statements; (3) while defendant should have been given the opportunity to impeach the declarant of the dying declaration, the error was harmless; (4) the judge did not err in refusing to instruction the jury on voluntary intoxication since there was no evidence to demonstrate defendant was impaired at the time of the killing; (5) the judge's references to the prosecution's evidence were not in error wince they were alluded to as examples illustrating legal principles; (6) defendant's conviction of murder in the first degree based on extreme atrocity or cruelty did not violate his right to due process of law; and (7) based on the trial record there was no reason to reduce the conviction or order a new trial.


OUTCOME: The convictions were affirmed.

Mayor of Cambridge v. Sec'y of the Commonwealth


SJC-08716


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


436 Mass. 476; 765 N.E.2d 749; 2002 Mass. LEXIS 200


March 7, 2002, Argued  
April 8, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected May 10, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the Commonwealth on November 19, 2001. After referral to the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk, the action was returned to the Commonwealth court by Greaney, J., to proceed on an expedited basis.



DISPOSITION: Mandamus relief was denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, mayor, city council, and 11 registered voters (mayor), sought a writ of mandamus against defendant, the secretary of the commonwealth, to invalidate the restricting plan for the 160 representative districts of the house of representatives.


OVERVIEW: The mayor argued that 2001 Mass. Acts ch. 125, § 1, which established the new districts, was unconstitutional under Mass. Const. art. 101, as it placed portions of the city in six representative districts when the requirements of Mass. Const. art. 101 could have been met with fewer divisions. The mayor's alternative plans to the redistricting statute, which met the territorial integrity requirement without sacrificing the competing goal of population equality, were not presented to the legislature. The supreme judicial court, in considering the alternative plans as evidence that a plan with fewer divisions of the city was possible, held that as long as the legislature had a reasonable justification for drawing the districts as it did, the supreme judicial court would not question the legislature's determination by comparing its selected plan to alternative plans that were not before it. The redistricting process which required the legislature to avoid the division of cities, towns, and counties "as nearly as may be" could not be interpreted to require that the legislature adopt the plan with the absolute minimum number of districts that crossed county, town, or city lines.


OUTCOME: Judgment was entered for the Commonwealth declaring that the redistricting plan did not violate the Massachusetts Constitution.

C&S Wholesale Grocers v. City of Westfield

DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff company filed an application for direct appellate review of the decision of the Superior Court Department, Hampden (Massachusetts), which ruled in favor of defendant city in an action seeking declaratory relief from a property tax assessment. The supreme court granted the application for direct appellate review.


OVERVIEW: The company paid property tax bills, and filed an application for abatement with the assessors, but the application was denied. Subsequently, the company brought an action challenging the constitutionality of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 59, § 2A(a), and argued the tax levied by the city on its real property was excessive and disproportionate and, therefore, should have been abated. The supreme court concluded the statute was constitutional and properly delegated taxing authority to municipalities. Specifically, the supreme court found the local option, contained in the statute, did not result in disproportionate taxation of property owners within the same municipality. In addition, the supreme court rejected the company's arguments that the local option represented an improper delegation of legislative power.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the judgment of the superior court.

OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Mills


SJC-08572


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


436 Mass. 387; 764 N.E.2d 854; 2002 Mass. LEXIS 192


December 4, 2001, Argued  
March 22, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Indictments found and returned in the Superior Court Department on June 19, 1996. The cases were tried before Thomas E. Connolly, J. After review by the Appeals Court, the Supreme Judicial Court granted leave to obtain further appellate review.

Commonwealth v. Mills, 51 Mass. App. Ct. 366, 745 N.E.2d 981, 2001 Mass. App. LEXIS 261 (2001).
Commonwealth v. Mills, 51 Mass. App. Ct. 366, 745 N.E.2d 981, 2001 Mass. App. LEXIS 261 (Apr. 19, 2001)



DISPOSITION: Court of appeals' jugment was reversed, in part, vacated, in part, and case was remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commonwealth filed an application for further appellate review of the judgment of the Appeals Court (Massachusetts) which: (1) reversed the judgment as to the indictment alleging larceny; (2) reversed the adjudication of defendant as a common and notorious thief and vacated the sentence under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 266, § 40; and (3) remanded the case to the superior court for resentencing. The supreme court granted further appellate review.


OVERVIEW: The issues before the supreme court were whether the trial judge: (1) erred in denying defendant's motion for a required finding of not guilty with respect to the three counts of larceny; (2) erred by adjudicating defendant a common and notorious thief; and (3) considered improper factors when sentencing defendant. The supreme court concluded the trial judge did not err in denying defendant's motion for required findings of not guilty with respect to the three counts of larceny. The supreme court reasoned a rational trier of fact could have found the essential elements of larceny by false pretenses beyond a reasonable doubt. However, the supreme court determined defendant's larceny convictions could not stand because the jury was only given instructions as to traditional larceny. In light of that conclusion, the supreme court found defendant could not be adjudicated a common and notorious thief pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 266, § 40. Finally, the supreme court agreed with the appellate court that the judge's personal feelings interfered with his sentencing decision. Accordingly, the supreme court concluded the circumstances necessitated resentencing by a different judge.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the judgments as to the three counts of larceny and remanded those matters for a new trial, vacated the adjudication of defendant as a common and notorious thief, and remanded the remaining convictions to the superior court for resentencing by a different judge.

Opinion of the Justices to the Senate


SJC-08634


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


436 Mass. 1201; 764 N.E.2d 343; 2002 Mass. LEXIS 148; 30 Media L. Rep. 1522



March 14, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Revised April 11, 2002.



DISPOSITION: Justices concluded that Senate No. 1939 violated the right to freedom of speech guaranteed by the Constitution of the United States and the Declaration of Rights of the Commonwealth.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Massachusetts Senate asked the court whether a pending bill, S. No. 1939 (Mass.), to be codified as Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 258D, an act relative to profits from crime, violated the freedom of speech guarantees of U.S. Const. amend. I and Mass. Const. Decl. Rights art. XVI.


OVERVIEW: After fears of unconstitutionality prompted repeal of an earlier statute aimed at preventing criminals from profiting from their crimes, Massachusetts legislators sought the high court's advice on the constitutionality of a second effort. The statutory scheme would have required publishers, agents, and others contracting with accused persons to pay contract amounts due into an escrow, for eventual distribution to victims of crime. The court held that the proposed legislation violated freedom of expression guarantees of U.S. Const. amend. I and Mass. Const. Decl. Rights art. XVI, because of overbreadth in reaching many works beyond a convicted criminal's efforts to profit from his crime and because it was a content-based prior restraint that failed to provide required procedural protections, including adequate judicial review.


OUTCOME: The court responded in the affirmative, finding the proposed legislation unconstitutional.

Bates v. Dir. of the Office of Campaign & Political Fin.


SJC-08677


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


436 Mass. 144; 763 N.E.2d 6; 2002 Mass. LEXIS 88


February 7, 2002, Argued  
February 25, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Revised April 11, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on October 4, 2001. The case was reported by Martha B. Sosman, J.



DISPOSITION: Case was remanded to single justice with directions to dismiss plaintiffs' claims for declaratory and injunctive relief against the director and the Secretary, without prejudice. Single justice was directed to enter separate judgment for Tolman against the director in the amount of $ 811,050.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A single justice sitting in the instant court for the County of Suffolk (Massachusetts) referred to the full court an action by plaintiff voters and candidates seeking declaratory and injunctive relief against defendant state officials to effectuate the Massachusetts Clean Elections Law, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 55a, § 1 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Massachusetts voters passed an initiative that became the Massachusetts Clean Elections Law, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 55A, § 1 et seq. It provided a mechanism whereunder candidates who satisfied a complicated certification process could receive public campaign funding. To assure its inclusion on the ballot as not violative of Mass. Const. amend. art. 48, cl. II, § 2, framers of the initiative included language indicating that disbursements to certified candidates would be subject to appropriation. The court held that since the measure had not been repealed by the legislature, and since the legislature lacked unfettered discretion to ignore the clear statutory mandate, the money had to be paid to those who qualified, and sovereign immunity would not bar efforts to collect it. In the instant case, only one of the candidates and voters seeking to compel public officials to release funds was actually certified, so only he was entitled to disbursement. Granting the injunctive relief sought, conditioning 2002 elections on compliance with the law, would have violated separation of powers.


OUTCOME: The court ordered relief for the one candidate who qualified for it under the statute, denied the voters the broader relief sought, remanded the matter to the single justice with instruction to dismiss without prejudice, directing that she retain jurisdiction to order relief against the officials as required in the future.

Donaldson v. Farrakhan


SJC-08530


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


436 Mass. 94; 762 N.E.2d 835; 2002 Mass. LEXIS 147


October 2, 2001, Argued  
February 13, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Middlesex. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on February 22, 1995. The case was heard by Regina L. Quinlan, J., on a motion for a directed verdict. The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: On direct appeal, trial court's grant of defendants-appellees motoin for directed verdict was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff shop owners filed a claim against defendants, two individuals, a mosque, and the Nation of Islam, alleging that their civil rights under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, §§ 92A, 98 were violated. Defendants moved for a directed verdict, which the Superior Court Department, Middlesex (Massachusetts), granted. The shop owners appealed. The state's highest court, on its own initiative, transferred the case from the appeals court.


OVERVIEW: Women were denied access to a speech given by one of the defendants. The state's highest court concluded that the shop owners failed to produce sufficient evidence for a reasonable jury to conclude by a preponderance of the evidence that the theatre was a place of public accommodation on the night in question. Further, the mosque's men's class was engaging in its religious meeting for men only, expressing concern for the community, and discussing the moral ideology and roles of men in addressing crime and violence in the community. The expression of religious viewpoints specific to men of the faith would have been impaired by the inclusion of women in the meeting. The admittance of male members of the public to an otherwise non-public mosque meeting did not bring the event within the scope of the Massachusetts public accommodation law. Holding otherwise would have impermissibly burdened defendants' freedom of association under the First Amendment.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Leopoldstadt, Inc. v. Comm'r of the Div. of Health Care Fin. & Policy


SJC-08610


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


436 Mass. 80; 762 N.E.2d 824; 2002 Mass. LEXIS 81


October 4, 2001, Argued  
February 11, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected February 20, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on June 8, 2001. The case was reported by Greaney, J.



DISPOSITION: Cause was remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff temporary nursing agencies (TNA) sought declaratory and injunctive relief regarding defendant division of health care finance and policy's setting of the maximum hourly rates that TNAs could charge to medical facilities for temporary nursing personnel. A single justice of the Supreme Judicial Court, Suffolk (Massachusetts), denied the request for an injunction and reserved and reported the case to the full court.


OVERVIEW: The court concluded that the division did not adopt the challenged regulations in conformity with the requirements of the enabling statutes. Accordingly, they were invalid, and the division was ordered to establish interim rates as provided by Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 118G, § 7, and to recalculate final rates in compliance with ch. 118G, § 7 and Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 111, § 72Y. The division failed to comply with the plain language of ch. 118G, § 7 and Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 111, § 72Y in three ways: (1) by failing to calculate the final rates taking into consideration the reasonable administrative expenses of each pool and the wages and benefits paid by each TNA to the medical personnel supplied to a health care facility; (2) by failing to collect all or substantially all of the cost reports before establishing final rates; and (3) by calculating a "median profit factor" in lieu of a "reasonable return on equity."


OUTCOME: The case was remanded requiring a judgment directing the division to establish interim rates and to recalculate final rates in compliance with the statutes.

Mass. Prisoners Assoc. Political Action Committee v. Acting Governor

DISPOSITION: Trial court's grant of defendants-appellee's motion for summary judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff committee challenged Mass. Exec. Order No. 399 (1997) which directed the department of corrections to prohibit political fundraising in prisons, as required by Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 55, § 14. Plaintiff individual sought to overturn disciplinary sanctions imposed on him. The Suffolk Superior Court Department (Massachusetts) entered summary judgment for defendants and affirmed the disciplinary sanctions. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: The committee argued that Mass. Exec. Order No. 399 (1997) misinterpreted Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 55, § 14, or alternatively, that the statute as applied to prison inmates was unconstitutional. The committee argued that the legislature did not intend Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 55, § 14 to reach conduct on government-owned premises primarily used to accommodate private parties and that prisons were occupied by private parties. The supreme judicial court noted that Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 55, § 14 was not implicated by mere government-ownership of the building, but depended on the purpose for which the building was occupied. The court held, however, that the occupancy by the inmates and staff was in furtherance of and exclusively for an entirely public purpose. As to the constitutional claims, the court held that the regulation was rationally related to the facilities' goal of maintaining security within the prison. As to the disciplinary sanctions against the individual, the supreme judicial court found substantial evidence to support the sanctions imposed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Obershaw


SJC-08303


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


435 Mass. 794; 762 N.E.2d 276; 2002 Mass. LEXIS 70


December 7, 2001, Argued  
February 5, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus denied Obershaw v. Lanman, 2005 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 18200 (D. Mass., Aug. 22, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Plymouth. Indictment found and returned in the Superior Court Department on September 2, 1997. A pretrial motion to suppress evidence was heard by Linda E. Giles, J., and the case was tried before her.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the Superior Court Department, Plymouth (Massachusetts) the convicted him of murder, claiming error in denying his motion to suppress, admitting photographs of the victim, and prosecutorial misconduct.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was given Miranda warnings and spoke with the police numerous times before he eventually confessed to the gruesome murder of his brother. The appellate court held that defendant's question, "Can I talk to a lawyer first?" was not an affirmative request for counsel. Because defendant was not immediately arrested, his statements fell under the six-hour "safe harbor" rule. Although numerous photographs were introduced, they were relevant to show extreme atrocity or cruelty and to show consciousness of guilt. They also contradicted defendant's testimony. The prosecutor's unanswered questions placed nothing before the jury. The jury was given corrective instructions for any improper remarks. It was also properly instructed that they were "permitted to infer," not that they must infer malice. Finally, Apprendi was not implicated by evidentiary considerations.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. The appellate court declined to set aside the verdict or reduce it to a lesser degree of guilt.

Commonwealth v. Bean


SJC-08522


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


435 Mass. 708; 761 N.E.2d 501; 2002 Mass. LEXIS 63


November 8, 2001, Argued  
January 28, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected February 12, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Franklin. Indictment found and returned in the Superior Court Department on October 18, 1999. The case was heard by Bertha D. Josephson, J. The Supreme Judicial Court granted an application for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury-waived trial in the Superior Court Department, Franklin (Massachusetts), defendant was convicted of posing a 15-year-old girl for photographs with her breast exposed, in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, § 29A(a). The Supreme Judicial Court granted an application for direct appellate review.


OVERVIEW: The state's highest court held that the Commonwealth failed to prove lascivious intent beyond a reasonable doubt, which was required for a violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, 29A. In examining the four photographs, it was apparent that they were neither obscene nor pornographic. The photographs appeared to have an artistic quality independent of their specific subject matter. An analysis of the photographs in the context of the Dost factors did not lead to the conclusion that the photographs themselves were lascivious or sufficient evidence of lascivious intent. The photographs (1) did not show sexual behavior or depict a sexually oriented display, (2) were not in a setting generally associated with sexual activity, and (3) did not evince sexual suggestiveness or a willingness to engage in sexual activity. Thus, neither the photographs alone, nor the other evidence on which the Commonwealth relied, demonstrated any lascivious intent by defendant.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed.

Nonetheless, the trial court considered the corporations' claims, finding that the commissioner's directive erased the effect of any constitutional infirmities that existed in the statutory provisions at issue.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

 

257 of 756 DOCUMENTS


Harlfinger v. Martin


SJC-08356


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


435 Mass. 38; 754 N.E.2d 63; 2001 Mass. LEXIS 486


March 12, 2001, Argued  
September 5, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on April 29, 1997. The case was heard by Patrick J. King, J., on a motion for summary judgment. The Supreme Judicial Court granted an application for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In the medical malpractice action filed by plaintiffs, minor and parents, the Superior Court Department, Suffolk (Massachusetts) entered a judgment granting defendant physician's motion for summary judgment, upholding the constitutionality of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 231, § 60D, and rejecting the continuing duty theory. The minor and the parents filed an application for direct appellate review, which was granted by the state supreme court.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the minor and the parents argued that: (1) the statute of repose in Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 231, § 60D violated the due process and equal protection guarantees of the federal and Massachusetts Constitutions; and (2) the physician was under a continuing duty to treat the minor, such that the action alleging a breach of that duty was still timely, notwithstanding the passage of more than seven years since the minor was actually treated by the physician. The state supreme court held, first, that § 60D bore a reasonable relationship to a legitimate legislative purpose (i.e., to curb the cost of medical malpractice insurance), and that it, therefore, survived the due process challenge. Second, § 60D's distinction between claims based on the leaving of a foreign object in a patient's body and all other claims involved no suspect classification, and § 60D itself did not affect any fundamental right. Thus, § 60D did not deny the minor equal protection. Finally, the physician's promise that he would continue to monitor the minor's rehabilitation and therapy did not mean that he was still continuing to treat the minor after his last visit and final physical therapy session.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Longval v. Superior Court Dep't of the Trial Court


SJC-08403


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


434 Mass. 718; 752 N.E.2d 674; 2001 Mass. LEXIS 408


June 12, 2001, Argued  
August 8, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on August 1, 2000. The case was heard by Cowin, J.



DISPOSITION: Single justice's judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate appealed the judgment of the Supreme Judicial Court for the County of Suffolk (Massachusetts) which denied the inmate's request for declaratory and injunctive relief regarding statutory provisions requiring inmates to pay court filing fees in civil cases, pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 261, §§ 27A, 29.


OVERVIEW: The inmate moved to waive filing fees and to docket certain appeals in an unrelated case. Absent the necessary financial information, under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 261, § 29, the appellate court could not take action on either request. Thereafter, the inmate filed an action challenging the constitutionality of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 261, § 29, on the ground that it treated inmates differently and more onerously than the population at large. A single justice denied the inmate's petition without a hearing. On appeal, the inmate argued the amendments to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 261, §§ 27A, 29, that required him to submit documentation establishing indigence and to pay court filing fees, violated his right to (1) access the courts and (2) equal protection under the laws. The supreme court concluded the statute passed constitutional muster because it did not pertain to a suspect class, it involved a right that was not fundamental, and it was rationally related to achieving its purpose of stemming "frivolous" civil litigation by prisoners.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the judgment.

 

259 of 756 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Beale


SJC-08432


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


434 Mass. 1024; 751 N.E.2d 845; 2001 Mass. LEXIS 399



July 19, 2001, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of malicious destruction of property, in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 266, § 127. The Massachusetts Court of Appeals affirmed the conviction. Defendant's application for further appellate review was granted.


OVERVIEW: The state's highest court upheld the appellate court's affirmation of conviction, for the reasons stated by the appellate court. However, the highest court addressed defendant's assertion of a violation of her due process rights. Due to the increased sentencing range triggered by a finding that the value of the destroyed property exceeded $ 250, the value of the property had to be treated as an element of the felony of malicious destruction of property, and a value in excess of $ 250 had to be found by a jury beyond a reasonable doubt. There was nothing amiss in the procedure by which defendant's conviction was obtained. The criminal complaint clearly alleged that the value of the property destroyed was over $ 250, and the judge instructed the jury that they had to find beyond a reasonable doubt that the value of the property exceeded $ 250. There was no possibility that defendant lacked notice of the charge, or was convicted of anything less than a jury's finding of each element beyond a reasonable doubt. Thus, defendant's due process argument failed.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed.

 

260 of 756 DOCUMENTS


Roe v. Attorney General


SJC-08242


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


434 Mass. 418; 750 N.E.2d 897; 2001 Mass. LEXIS 377


September 11, 2000; March 8, 2001, Argued  
June 28, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected October 22, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on October 19, 1999. The case was heard by John M. Xifaras, J. The Supreme Judicial Court granted an application for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Order granting plaintiffs a preliminary injunction vacated, and case remanded to Superior Court for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Massachusetts sex offender registry board appealed Superior Court Department, Suffolk (Massachusetts), judgment preliminarily enjoining it from requiring plaintiff convicted sex offenders to disclose preliminary information for sharing with local police, pursuant to the 1999 amended version of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 6, § 178, the sex offender registration statute.


OVERVIEW: After an earlier sex offender registration and classification statute had been found to violate due process by permitting too much dissemination of information, Massachusetts enacted an amended version of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 6, § 178. Several men with long-ago convictions of sex offenses challenged the facial constitutionality of provisions that required them, without a prior hearing, to submit their names and addresses to the sex offender registry board, which would share that information with local law enforcement. Although it admitted that such provisions could prove unconstitutional as applied, the high court found no facial invalidity in the scheme. The board could not do its job without gathering preliminary information in as unintrusive a manner as possible, and police always had access to criminal records. Therefore, the trial court should not have enjoined the gathering of this information.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the order granting an injunction and remanded for further consistent proceedings.

 

261 of 756 DOCUMENTS


In re Liquidation of Am. Mut. Liab. Ins. Co.


SJC-08332


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


434 Mass. 272; 747 N.E.2d 1215; 2001 Mass. LEXIS 278


March 5, 2001, Argued  
June 1, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Ruthardt v. United States, 164 F. Supp. 2d 232, 2001 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 16350 (D. Mass., 2001)
Appeal after remand at, Certified question answered by, Remanded by In re Liquidation of Am. Mut. Liab. Ins. Co., 2004 Mass. LEXIS 34 (Mass., Feb. 2, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on January 17, 1989. A motion for approval of a plan of liquidation, filed on May 14, 1999, was heard by Judith A. Cowin, J., and questions of law were reported by her.



DISPOSITION: Remanded to the county court for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The receiver of an insolvent insurance company had filed a motion before the Supreme Judicial Court for the County of Suffolk (Massachusetts) for approval of a liquidation plan which outlined general classes of distribution priority. A judge of the appellate court had reserved and reported four questions of law concerning the liquidation plan.


OVERVIEW: In 1989 an insurance company was decreed insolvent and a receiver was appointed. At the time there were two conflicting statutes in place which dictated the order in which creditors should be reimbursed. By 2000 the statutes had been reconciled and the receiver relied upon the reconciliation in setting the class priority for payment of claims. Most of the claims were being handled by guaranty funds. There were not sufficient funds to pay all the claims. The appellate court held the statutory revisions made the statutes retroactive regarding the particular case. The claimants could not argue reliance because the insurance industry was regulated. Thus, changes in legislation should have been anticipated. In addition, there was no evidence the claimants relied upon the former liquidation statutes in purchasing insurance from the insolvent insurer. Even if they had, there was no contractual right to a particular distribution where the recovery was statutorily set. Also, any contractual right to recovery was impaired by the insurer's insolvency, not the 2000 amendments.


OUTCOME: The appellate court answered two of the judge's questions in the affirmative and two in the negative. It remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

262 of 756 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Rotonda


SJC-08411


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


434 Mass. 211; 747 N.E.2d 1199; 2001 Mass. LEXIS 219


March 8, 2001, Argued  
May 21, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on December 23, 1999. The case was reported by Ireland, J.



DISPOSITION: Remanded the case for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Commonwealth challenged the lawfulness of the terms and conditions of a continuance without a finding from the Suffolk County District Court (Massachusetts) that granted the defendant unsupervised probation and conditioned the continuance on the payment of money to the complaining witness.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with violating the civil rights of another without bodily injury and threatening to commit a crime. The district court granted the defendant a continuance without a finding and sentenced him to unsupervised probation for one year on the condition that he not have any contact with the victim, that he publicly apologize to her in front of her fellow employees and members of her union, and that he make a payment of $ 5,000 as restitution to her. On appeal, the Commonwealth argued that the terms and conditions of the continuance did not conform with Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 278, § 18. Upon review, the appellate remanded the matter for further proceedings. The district court judge's disposition pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 278, § 18 did not require the imposition of supervised probation as a term or condition of his continuing the case without a finding, but was unlawful in so far as it included a condition requiring the payment of money, not properly documented as restitution, to the complaining victim.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

263 of 756 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Fickling


SJC-08025


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


434 Mass. 9; 746 N.E.2d 475; 2001 Mass. LEXIS 195


February 9, 2001, Argued  
April 20, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion for new trial granted by Commonwealth v. Fickling, 2010 Mass. Super. LEXIS 68 (Mass. Super. Ct., Feb. 3, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Hampden. Indictments found and returned in the Superior Court Department on August 8, 1996. The cases were tried before Mary-Lou Rup, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction of murder in the first degree by reason of extreme atrocity or cruelty before the Hampden Superior Court (Massachusetts), asserting various trial errors.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder in the first degree by reason of extreme atrocity or cruelty as a result of leaving his 22 month old daughter alone, locked in an apartment, after choking her mother to death. The child subsequently died as a result of starvation and dehydration. Defendant asserted several errors. The appellate court held admission of evidence of past acts of violence by defendant against the mother were proper to show defendant's intent. The appellate court held there was sufficient evidence for the jury to convict defendant since defendant's intent was irrelevant as to the issue of whether he committed an act of extreme atrocity or cruelty, rather the issue was did the child endure considerable suffering. The appellate court also held while the trial court issued erroneous jury instructions, they were not prejudicial since they were sandwiched between the correct instruction and there would be no confusion on the part of the jury.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Black Rose, Inc. v. City of Boston


SJC-08367


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


433 Mass. 501; 744 N.E.2d 640; 2001 Mass. LEXIS 166


January 8, 2001, Argued  
March 15, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected June 8, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on March 31, 1999. The case was heard by Margaret R. Hinkle, J., on motions for judgment on the pleadings. The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The plaintiff challenged a decision of the defendant city's mayor's office of consumer affairs and licensing to suspend the plaintiff's entertainment license for one day. A Suffolk Superior Court Department (Massachusetts) judgment for defendant dismissed plaintiff's complaint. Plaintiff appealed. The supreme judicial court on its own initiative transferred the case from the appeals court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's licensing board granted plaintiff an entertainment license pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 140, § 183A. Plaintiff's staff physically assaulted two patrons. The board held a hearing to determine whether plaintiff's entertainment license should have been suspended or revoked. Plaintiff did not refute the allegations or demonstrate any justification. The board suspended plaintiff's entertainment license for one day. The board was not a state agency, but, the supreme judicial court determined that the superior court applied the correct standard of review of the board's decision, the substantial evidence test, because of the strong similarity between the nature of the claim in such cases and the revocation of an alcoholic beverage license by the state control commission, to which a substantial evidence test had previously been held by the supreme judicial court to apply under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 30A, § 14(7)(e) of the State Administrative Procedure Act. Section 183A provided authority to modify, suspend, or revoke a license for any violation of the licensing authorities' rules and regulations or for any violation of law, such as an assault.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

265 of 756 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Chapman


SJC-08369


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


433 Mass. 481; 744 N.E.2d 14; 2001 Mass. LEXIS 167


December 4, 2000, Argued  
March 15, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Barnstable. Indictment found and returned in the Superior Court Department on August 11, 1998. The case was tried before Richard F. Connon, J., and questions of law were reported by him to the Appeals Court. The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the matter from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court, Barnstable (Massachusetts) finding defendant guilty of wantonly or recklessly permitting substantial bodily injury to her infant child. The case was transferred to the Supreme Judicial Court by its own motion.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's infant child drowned in the bathtub when defendant left the infant alone. Defendant was convicted of wantonly or recklessly permitting substantial bodily injury under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 265, § 13J. The reviewing court affirmed. Death was a risk of injury under the § 13J description of substantial bodily harm, which included any substantial impairment of the physical condition that caused a protracted impairment of the function of an internal organ or a substantial risk of death. Injuries that fell under § 13J included not only external trauma, but also internal trauma, such as the infant's asphyxiation. Section 13J was not vague or overbroad, because it put defendant on notice that her conduct was criminal, and § 13J was sufficiently specific to prevent ad hoc enforcement. There was sufficient evidence for the jury to conclude that defendant was wanton and reckless.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. The crime of wantonly or recklessly permitting substantial bodily injury included internal trauma, such as asphyxiation. The statute was not vague or overbroad, because it put defendant on notice that her conduct was criminal, and it was sufficiently specific.

 

266 of 756 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Peace Chou


SJC-08282


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


433 Mass. 229; 741 N.E.2d 17; 2001 Mass. LEXIS 9


October 6, 2000, Argued  
January 22, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Middlesex. Complaint received and sworn to in the Framingham Division of the District Court Department on June 9, 1998. The case was heard by Paul F. Healy, Jr., J. The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Framingham Division of the District Court Department, Middlesex (Massachusetts) convicting him of accosting or annoying a person of the opposite sex with offensive and disorderly acts or language under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, § 53 after denying his motion for a required finding of not guilty.


OVERVIEW: Defendant produced several "missing person" flyers identifying and describing a young woman he had dated for three weeks. The young woman had broken up with defendant. Determined to "get back" at her, defendant sneaked into her high school one night and hung the flyers at various locations. The word "missing" was printed in large type across the top of the flyers beneath which was the victim's name and a large photograph of her. Numerous references were made in the flyers about the victim's alleged sexual behaviors. Defendant was convicted under the accosting or annoying provision of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, § 53. On appeal, defendant argued that neither his acts nor his language was disorderly under § 53. Conviction was affirmed. Though there was no fighting, or violent or tumultuous behavior in the flyer's unaltered photograph and sexualized description of the victim, nor in defendant's conduct in creating or hanging the flyer at the school, the content of the flyer was threatening and therefore constituted disorderly language under the accosting or annoying provision of § 53. Because defendant's language was a true threat, it was not constitutionally protected speech.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed; the evidence was sufficient to support a finding that defendant's language was threatening and therefore amounted to disorderly language under the applicable criminal statute. The statute was not violative of constitutional free speech guarantees, as the threatening speech constituted a true threat.

 

267 of 756 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Sholley


SJC-08295


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


432 Mass. 721; 739 N.E.2d 236; 2000 Mass. LEXIS 710


October 6, 2000, Argued  
November 30, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied April 16, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 3048.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Norfolk. Complaint received and sworn to in the Quincy Division of the District Court Department on June 25, 1996. The case was tried before Paul F. X. Moriarty, J. After review by the Appeals Court, the Supreme Judicial Court granted leave to obtain further appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of conviction on the charges of threatening to commit a crime and being a disorderly person affirmed. The judgment of conviction on the charge of disrupting court proceedings reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the Quincy Division of the District Court Department (Massachusetts) convicting him of threatening to commit a crime, being a disorderly person, and disrupting court proceedings for his outburst in a courthouse.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was active in an organization dedicated to fathers' rights. Appellant was convicted for his outburst in a courthouse after he learned that a father had been sent to jail in a domestic violence case. On appeal, the court reversed appellant's disrupting court proceedings conviction, even though various persons temporarily suspended their normal courthouse activities, because there was no evidence of any actual impact on any proceeding. The court affirmed appellant's conviction for threatening to commit a crime because his statement "Watch out, Counselor," along with his enraged demeanor and yelling tone of voice permitted the jury to conclude that the statement was intended as a threat. The threatening statement was not protected by U.S. Const. amend. I as political hyperbole. The court also affirmed appellant's disorderly person conviction because appellant's threatening a district attorney and screaming and running through the courthouse corridors was threatening and tumultuous.


OUTCOME: Judgment convicting appellant of disrupting court proceedings reversed because there was no evidence that appellant's outburst had any actual impact on any proceeding. Judgment convicting appellant of threatening to commit a crime and being a disorderly person affirmed.

 

268 of 756 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Gonsalves


SJC-07962


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


432 Mass. 613; 739 N.E.2d 1100; 2000 Mass. LEXIS 699


October 2, 2000, Argued  
November 9, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Plymouth. Indictment found and returned in the Superior Court Department on May 27, 1997. Following review by this court, 429 Mass. 658 (1999), a motion for enforcement of an order for payment of attorney's fees and costs was heard by Greaney, J., and was referred by him to a panel of this court.



DISPOSITION: Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commonwealth appealed Superior Court Department, Plymouth (Massachusetts), order that it pay, because of unavailability of Administrative Office of the Trial Court funds, pursuant to Mass. R. Crim. P. 15(d), costs and fees incurred by defendant in retaining private counsel for Commonwealth's interlocutory appeal of suppression order.


OVERVIEW: Defendant retained private counsel in the underlying drug offense prosecution. After suppression of drugs seized from him, the Commonwealth brought an unsuccessful interlocutory appeal as permitted by Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 278, § 28E, and defendant thereafter moved pursuant to Mass. R. Crim. P. 15 to recover his attorney's fees and costs incurred on that appeal. The Administrative Office of the Trial Court had exhausted the funds that would normally have been used for defendant's expenses, so the trial court ordered the prosecutor's office to pay them. The court held that this procedure was not unconstitutional. A prosecutor's office was not a subject of Massachusetts for purposes of due process and equal protection principles. The rule as applied also did not violate separation of powers rules by fettering prosecutorial discretion. Costs of interlocutory appeals were simply one more budgetary factor that prosecutors would have had to weigh in requesting funds.


OUTCOME: The court found that the rule as applied did not violate constitutional principles of equal protection or separation of powers; therefore it was appropriate for the district attorney's office that sought the appeal in the underlying action to bear defendant's costs if they were not otherwise covered.

 

269 of 756 DOCUMENTS


Boston Herald, Inc. v. Sharpe


SJC-08371


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


432 Mass. 593; 737 N.E.2d 859; 2000 Mass. LEXIS 698; 28 Media L. Rep. 2569


October 6, 2000, Argued  
November 8, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Petitions filed in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk, two on July 31, 2000, and one on August 1, 2000, respectively. The cases were heard by Cowin, J.



DISPOSITION: Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pertaining to intervenors' action seeking access to certain impounded documents relating to respondent's divorce action, respondent appealed a decision of the Supreme Judicial Court for Suffolk County vacating the prior order which had impounded certain disputed affidavits, thus unsealing the requested documents.


OVERVIEW: Respondent husband was arrested and indicted for the murder of his wife. Prior to respondent's trial, intervenor media companies sought access to certain impounded documents in respondent's and his wife's divorce action and a related abuse prevention injunctive action. The court below vacated the prior order which had impounded certain disputed affidavits, thus unsealing the requested documents. Respondent appealed from that decision and the court affirmed. The court held that in the specific circumstances of this case the public had a right of access to all of the relevant judicial records. Pursuant to Mass. Sup. Jud. Ct. R. 1:15, Unif. Impoundment § 7, the court balanced the public's right of access to the judicial records at issue against defendant's U.S. Const. amend. VI right to a fair trial and respondent's privacy rights. There was a rigorous presumption of openness as to the judicial records at issue. In contrast, the disclosure of the records would increase only marginally any prejudice already existing against respondent. Also, since the subject matter of publicity was of legitimate public concern, there was no invasion of privacy.


OUTCOME: Decision of the court below was affirmed. Intervenors had a right of access to the disputed documents, since there was a rigorous presumption of openness as to those documents outweighing concerns that disclosure would interfere with respondent's right to a fair trial.

AG v. M.C.K., Inc.


SJC-08176


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


432 Mass. 546; 736 N.E.2d 373; 2000 Mass. LEXIS 619


September 7, 2000, Argued  
October 13, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on July 8, 1997. After the appointment of a receiver, the case was heard by Diane M. Kottmyer, J., and the matter of the propriety of an order of sale was reported to the Appeals Court by her. The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct review.



DISPOSITION: Remanded to the Superior Court to reconsider the conflicting orders in effect regarding Union Square.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed from two orders of the Suffolk County (Massachusetts) Superior Court, in actions brought by plaintiff seeking sale or closure of defendants' nursing home, pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws. ch. 111, § 72R, part of the Patient Protector Receivership Act.


OVERVIEW: Defendants appealed from two orders of the trial court, one directing that defendants' nursing home be sold and the other directing that it be closed. The motion for closure was brought by the receiver that had been appointed under the Patient Protector Receivership Act. Plaintiff state department of public health then moved for a court-ordered sale of the home under the act, including the real estate. The trial court found that disregard of defendants' separate corporate forms was warranted, and ordered the sale of the real estate as well as the home itself. The court affirmed in part, holding that the scope of a court's authority to sell a "facility" under the act was essentially fact specific, depending on the particular ownership interests in the real and personal property possessed by the licensed entity, and the viability of the facility. The court remanded for further proceedings to decide whether the home should have been sold or closed.


OUTCOME: Trial court judgment affirmed in part, and matter remanded. The order directing sale of the nursing home was proper under the Patient Protector Receivership Act, but further proceedings were required to decide whether the home should have been sold or closed, under the particular facts of the case.

 

271 of 756 DOCUMENTS


Mazzone v. AG


SJC-08348


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


432 Mass. 515; 736 N.E.2d 358; 2000 Mass. LEXIS 613


September 7, 2000, Argued  
October 2, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court for the county of Suffolk on June 6, 2000. The case was reported by Spina, J.



DISPOSITION: Remanded to the county court for the entry of a judgment declaring that the Attorney General's certification and summary of this petition are in compliance with the requirements of art. 48. The Secretary of the Commonwealth shall take the appropriate steps to have the measure placed on the ballot in the upcoming State election.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs filed a complaint in the Suffolk County (Massachusetts) Superior Court Department, seeking certiorari and mandamus relief, challenging the state attorney general's certification of the proposed amendments to the Massachusetts Constitution in Initiative Petition 99-10. The question was then reserved and reported to the full Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, 10 registered voters and the state chiefs of police association and state district attorneys, challenged the state attorney general's certification of a voters' initiative petition. The initiative proposed an amendment to the state constitution to tighten the standards under which assets could be forfeited, and to expand the class of individuals permitted to request drug treatment in lieu of prosecution. The court held that the petition was not unconstitutional in any respect. The petition did not authorize any specific appropriation of money from the state treasury, and there was nothing in the petition that would allow "reversal of a judicial decision." The provisions were sufficiently related to a single, common purpose, to expand the state's drug treatment program. Plaintiffs' concerns about the petition's definition of "drug dependent person" were not reviewable before the legislation was enacted. Finally, the attorney general's summary did not need to provide a comprehensive legal analysis of the measure.


OUTCOME: Matter remanded to the county court for entry of a judgment declaring that the attorney general's certification and summary of the petition were in compliance with the requirements of the state constitution. The measure was therefore to be placed on the ballot in the upcoming state election.

Commonwealth v. Bruno


SJC-08214, SJC-08224, SJC-08225, SJC-08227


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


432 Mass. 489; 735 N.E.2d 1222; 2000 Mass. LEXIS 577


May 2, 2000, Argued  
September 29, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected January 7, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Middlesex. Plymouth. Petition filed in the Superior Court Department on September 20, 1999. A motion to dismiss filed by the defendant Bruno was heard by Charles J. Hely, J. The Supreme Judicial Court granted an application for direct appellate review. Petition filed in the Superior Court Department on October 8, 1999. A motion to dismiss filed by the defendant Wilson was heard by Isaac Borenstein, J.; questions of law were reported by him to the Appeals Court; and a motion to stay the defendant's release from commitment was heard in the Appeals Court by Kenneth Laurence, J. Civil action commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on January 10, 2000. The matters were heard by Ireland, J., and the appeals pending in the Appeals Court were ordered consolidated and transferred to this court by him. Petition filed in the Superior Court Department on October 20, 1999. A motion to dismiss filed by the defendant Davila and a motion to stay the defendant's release from commitment were heard by Margot Botsford, J. On a second motion to stay the defendant's release, the matter was heard in the Appeals Court by Kenneth Laurence, J. The case was transferred to this court [***2] by an order of Ireland, J., sitting as single justice, on the Commonwealth's petition under G. L. c. 211, § 3.



DISPOSITION: Orders dismissing petitions seeking commitment of Bruno, Davilla, and Wilson vacated and remanded. Those portions of Wilson's commitment order directing that he be held separately and that he receive treatment while under observation vacated; order for his commitment for sixty days affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In appeals that were consolidated and ordered transferred by the Massachusetts Appeals Court, plaintiff, Commonwealth of Massachusetts, appealed the trial court order that granted defendant sex offenders' motion to dismiss petitions that sought to commit the defendants civilly as sexually dangerous persons pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 123A, § 1.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were separately convicted for sexual offense crimes. During defendants' imprisonment, the Commonwealth of Massachusetts amended Mass. Gen. Law ch. 123A to provide for the civil commitment of a sexually dangerous person. Plaintiff, Commonwealth, filed petitions prior to defendants' scheduled release requesting each be committed as a sexually dangerous person. Defendants filed a motion to dismiss, alleging that the statute could not be applied retroactively. The trial court granted defendants' motion and the Commonwealth filed an appeal. The petitions were consolidated on appeal. Vacating and remanding the orders, which dismissed the petitions, the court held the conduct that triggered the application of ch. 123A was not the defendants' prior conviction of a sexual offense, but the current mental condition of each of the defendants. Further, ch. 123A did not violate the ex post facto law, as the statute was not criminal or penal in nature. The court further vacated the orders that required one of the defendants be held separately and that he receive treatment while under observation, but the court affirmed his commitment for 60 days.


OUTCOME: Orders dismissing defendants' petitions regarding status as a sexually dangerous person were vacated and remanded. Defendants were not determined to be sexually dangerous persons based upon their conviction for sexual crimes but rather on the current mental condition of each of the defendants. Court vacated the orders that one of the defendants was to be held separately and that he receive treatment while under observations.

 

273 of 756 DOCUMENTS


Belhumeur v. Labor Rels. Comm'n


SJC-08163


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


432 Mass. 458; 735 N.E.2d 860; 2000 Mass. LEXIS 575; 165 L.R.R.M. 2458; 143 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P59,223


April 4, 2000, Argued  
September 21, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied March 5, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Appeal from a decision of the Labor Relations Commission. The Supreme Judicial Court granted an application for direct appellate review.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A decision of the Massachusetts Labor Relations Commission regarding the activities of a teacher's union which could be paid for by agency fees paid by nonmembers of the union was appealed by both the union and certain nonmembers.


OVERVIEW: Nonmember public school teachers required to pay agency fees to teachers' association were entitled to limit the use of those fees to activities germane to duties as the collective bargaining representative. They filed charges in 1989 with the Labor Relations Commission alleging the union's use of agency fees for nonchargeable activities. Both the teachers and the union appealed the commission's 1997 decision. The decision was reasonably prompt, under the circumstances. The formula used to calculate the teachers' agency fee properly did not violate their free speech rights by requiring contribution to nonchargeable union activities. Costs to maintain union's existence were chargeable, except where the union specifically identified them as attributable to nonchargeable activity. Expenses for advocating public education funding were political speech, and not chargeable. Informational support services, including an article about communication points during a strike, were chargeable because they were intended to benefit all members of the bargaining unit. Expenses related to withholding services related to a prohibited strike and were, therefore, not chargeable.


OUTCOME: Labor Relations Commission's decision was affirmed except where nonchargeable accounting expenses were found chargeable, where article intended to benefit bargaining unit was found not chargeable, and where expenses of campaign to restore teaching positions were found not chargeable, since this was directed at implementing collective bargaining agreement.

 

274 of 756 DOCUMENTS


MacLean v. State Bd. of Retirement


SJC-08158


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


432 Mass. 339; 733 N.E.2d 1053; 2000 Mass. LEXIS 522; 25 Employee Benefits Cas. (BNA) 1885


May 2, 2000, Argued  
August 18, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on August 9, 1999. The case was reported by Abrams, J.



DISPOSITION: The case is remanded to the county court where a judgment is to be entered affirming the judgment of the District Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff commenced civil action in Massachusetts in the nature of certiorari under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 249, § 4, to review decision of district court, upholding State Board of Retirement order that pension be forfeited after he pled guilty to two misdemeanors.


OVERVIEW: After plaintiff pleaded guilty to two violations of the conflict of interest law, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 268A, § 7, and was ordered to disgorge his profits as restitution, in return for release of all other claims and charges, defendant state Board of Retirement ordered his pension forfeited under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 32, § 15 (4). The district court affirmed. Plaintiff challenged the ruling, arguing that his settlement agreement with the Attorney General precluded forfeiture and his guilty plea was not a "final conviction" to trigger the pension forfeiture statute. He contended the statute was unconstitutional as applied to him, violated the contract clause, was an excessive fine, and constituted double jeopardy. The appellate court affirmed, rejecting the statutory and constitutional challenges, and remanded to county court for entry of judgment. Plaintiff had a history of public service and was on notice that certain criminal convictions would result in mandatory pension forfeiture under statute. Forfeiture was not disproportionate or excessive but was roughly equivalent to plaintiff's minimum improper gains. "Final conviction" issue was waived.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. Settlement agreement did not preclude revoking plaintiff's retirement benefits, which was mandatory under pension forfeiture statute, which was not unconstitutional, even assuming forfeiture was punitive "fine," amount was not excessive, as it approximated value of improper gain. Revocation was not criminal punishment for double jeopardy purposes.

Pereira v. Commissioner of Soc. Servs.


SJC-08218


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


432 Mass. 251; 733 N.E.2d 112; 2000 Mass. LEXIS 406; 16 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 1043; 141 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P59,024; 79 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P40,392


May 2, 2000, Argued  
August 9, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on September 9, 1996. The case was heard by Herman J. Smith, Jr., J., on motions for summary judgment. The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Superior Court granting summary judgment for Pereira on her civil rights claim and denying the commissioner qualified immunity is reversed. Judgment is entered for the defendants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, Massachusetts Department of Social Services and its commissioner, appealed order of Superior Court of Suffolk County (Massachusetts), granting summary judgment in favor of plaintiff who claimed her employment was terminated in violation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and U.S. Const. amend. I.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, a social worker, was discharged for telling a racist joke at a dinner given for outgoing city council members. She sued defendants, the Massachusetts Department of Social Services and its commissioner, alleging she was terminated for speech protected by U.S. Const. amend. I, and asserting 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claims and common law wrongful termination and infliction of emotional distress claims. The commissioner's decision to terminate plaintiff was within her discretion. The joke was not speech on a matter of public concern to which U.S. Const. amend. I protections applied. Some restraints on other speech by public employees were permissible and sufficient evidence supported finding the joke had a demonstrable impact on the integrity and reputation of the department in the community.


OUTCOME: The court reversed, holding plaintiff's joke was not speech on matter of public concern that was protected by First Amendment, and defendant commissioner's decision to fire plaintiff was within her discretion since remark had demonstrable effect on reputation of defendant department in community.
