Commonwealth v. Edward


No. 07-P-993


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


75 Mass. App. Ct. 162; 912 N.E.2d 515; 2009 Mass. App. LEXIS 1112


September 4, 2008, Argued 
September 2, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Dukes County. Indictment found and returned in the Superior Court Department on August 15, 1990. Following review by this court, 34 Mass. App. Ct. 521, 613 N.E.2d 115 (1993), a motion for a new trial, filed on October 23, 2006, was considered by Gary A. Nickerson, J.
Commonwealth v. Edward, 34 Mass. App. Ct. 521, 613 N.E.2d 115, 1993 Mass. App. LEXIS 555 (1993)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury found defendant guilty of rape of a child, indecent assault and battery on a person who has attained the age of 14, and unnatural and lascivious acts with a child under the age of 16. Defendant was sentenced to 20 years for rape. Defendant's convictions were affirmed on direct appeal. Thirteen years later, defendant filed a motion for a new trial. The Dukes County Superior Court (Massachusetts) denied the motion. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court first concluded that because defendant had a direct appeal in which he raised none of the claims he asserted, his substantive claims, except for that involving the right to a public trial, were waived for appellate review. The appellate court also noted that a fresh complaint instruction was not mandatory, that the jury instructions adequately and clearly defied the limited use the jurors could make of the fresh complaint testimony, and the victim did not self-corroborate. Because there was nothing, save multiple layers of speculation, to support an ineffective assistance of counsel claim, no hearing was required on those claims. Finally, the appellate court found that, on the face of it, the order the close the courtroom was improper. The judge was not required to close the courtroom simply because the victim was under 18. The interests to be protected by the closure were not addressed and did not obviously emerge from the record. The appellate court concluded that a hearing was required to consider, inter alia, whether the courtroom was closed, whether counsel had a sound reason for declining to object, and whether defendant agreed to the closure.


OUTCOME: The order denying the motion for a new trial was vacated and the case was remanded for a hearing on defendant's public trial claim.

Russell v. City of New Bedford


No. 08-P-441


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


74 Mass. App. Ct. 715; 910 N.E.2d 404; 2009 Mass. App. LEXIS 1026


February 6, 2009, Argued

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Russell v. Crry of New Bedford, 2009 Mass. LEXIS 922 (Mass., Oct. 29, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Bristol. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on December 27, 2001. The case was tried before Robert J. Kane, J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Bristol Superior Court (Massachusetts) entered a judgment for plaintiff building owner on jury verdicts of negligence and civil rights violations after he sued defendant city pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 258, § 2 and 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claiming that the city unlawfully demolished two buildings he owned. The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: The building owner obtained two buildings from the previous owner. Thereafter, the city targeted them for demolition. It notified the previous owner by certified mail of its intentions. The letter was returned undelivered. At the time, the buildings were uninhabitable. A representative for the building owner sent a letter to the city's building commissioner describing the building owner's intent to rehabilitate and requesting that the buildings not be demolished. She then submitted a structural report the city requested. The buildings were soon demolished anyway. The building owner then sued alleging negligence and the violation of his civil rights. A jury found for him under both theories. The appellate court found that sufficient evidence supported a finding of negligence by the city in demolishing the two buildings, but also determined that since the buildings were uninhabitable, the correct measure of negligence damages was diminution in value, not loss of use. It also found that the building owner could not prove its 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claims because he did not show that the city's building commissioner was a policy maker whose single decision could bind the city.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment as to liability on the negligence claims, vacated that judgment as to damages, and remanded the case to the trial court for a reassessment of damages on those claims. The appellate court also reversed the judgment, as to both liability and damages, on the civil rights claims.

Commonwealth Empl. Rels. Bd. v. Boston Teachers Union


No. 08-P-1290.


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


74 Mass. App. Ct. 500; 908 N.E.2d 772; 2009 Mass. App. LEXIS 843; 187 L.R.R.M. 3540


March 11, 2009, Argued 
June 25, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Commonwealth Empl. Rels. Bd. v. Boston Teachers Union, 455 Mass. 1102, 914 N.E.2d 330, 2009 Mass. LEXIS 740 (2009)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Boston Teachers Union v. Commonwealth Emp. Rel, 2010 U.S. LEXIS 2303 (U.S., Mar. 8, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on February 8, 2007. A motion for a temporary restraining order and a complaint for contempt were heard by Bruce R. Henry, J., and entry of final judgment was ordered by Geraldine S. Hines, J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Commonwealth Employment Relations Board filed a complaint for contempt against defendant teachers union. The union challenged a judgment of the Superior Court, Suffolk (Massachusetts), which imposed a prospective coercive fine against the union after ruling that it was in contempt of a previous order that enjoined it from engaging in, threatening, or encouraging a strike or work stoppage in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 150E, § 9A.


OVERVIEW: A school committee anticipated that union members would authorize a strike. It petitioned the Board to initiate an investigation pursuant to § 9A(b). The Board found that the union's actions were reasonably construed as constituting inducement or encouragement of a strike or work stoppage in violation of § 9A(a) and that a strike was about to occur. It issued an order requiring the union to rescind and disavow its motion for a strike veto. The union failed to comply with the Board's order. The Board filed a complaint in the superior court, seeking enforcement of its order. The superior court found that the union had engaged in prohibited § 9A(a) activities. The union argued that the Board improperly concluded that a strike was about to occur. The appeals court held that the evidence amply supported the Board's conclusion that the union violated § 9A(a) by encouraging and inducing a strike. A reasonable inference that the union was involved in encouraging a strike was warranted, if not compelled, by all of the evidence. The Board had a substantial interest in preventing a strike by the union members, and any incidental limitation of First Amendment freedoms was justified.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed the judgment.

Commonwealth v. Argueta


No. 08-P-394.


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


73 Mass. App. Ct. 564; 899 N.E.2d 896; 2009 Mass. App. LEXIS 59


December 8, 2008, Argued 
January 20, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Commonwealth v. Argueta, 2009 Mass. LEXIS 265 (Mass., Apr. 1, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Suffolk. Complaint received and sworn to in the Chelsea Division of the District Court Department on May 19, 2005. Following a finding of sufficient facts and entry of an order by Marie O. Jackson, J., that charges be continued without a finding, a motion for a new trial, filed on November 6, 2007, seeking to withdraw the admission to sufficient facts, was considered by Timothy H. Gailey, J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by the Suffolk District Court Department (Massachusetts) of tagging under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 266, § 126B, after sufficient facts were found to convict defendant. The charges were continued without a finding for six months, and were then dismissed on recommendation of the probation department. Defendant's motion for a new trial was denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that the case was not moot as the continuance without a finding was counted as a sentence for purposes of calculating criminal history points in federal sentencing. If defendant's appeal was successful, he could petition for resentencing within one year of his sentencing. Defendant had a continuing personal stake in the outcome of the litigation. The colloquy did not explain to defendant the elements of the crime, nor did counsel represent that the elements of the crime had been explained to defendant. The facts as recited by the prosecutor did not allege that defendant himself sprayed or applied paint or placed a sticker upon anything. He could only have been liable as a joint venturer. The facts did not convey that defendant shared a principal's intent to commit the crime or that defendant had reached agreement with the principal to aid in its commission. Therefore the recitation of facts did not adequately inform defendant that intent and agreement were essential elements of joint venture liability for the crime. Nothing in the colloquy explained the requisite intent or the agreement essential for defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The order denying the motion for a new trial seeking to withdraw defendant's admission to sufficient facts was reversed, and the matter was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings consistent with the opinion. The rescript was to issue forthwith.

Commonwealth v. Dingle


No. 07-P-420.


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


73 Mass. App. Ct. 274; 898 N.E.2d 1; 2008 Mass. App. LEXIS 1169


September 4, 2008, Argued 
December 4, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Commonwealth v. Dingle, 453 Mass. 1102, 2009 Mass. LEXIS 118 (Mass., Jan. 29, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Plymouth. Indictments found and returned in the Superior Court Department on November 13, 2001. The cases were heard by Suzanne DelVecchio, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by the Plymouth Superior Court Department (Massachusetts) of three counts of possession with intent to distribute child pornography and two counts of distributing child pornography, all in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, § 29B. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that § 29B did not contain two separate crimes. Both types of content were depicted in the more than 900 images defendant possessed, and there was no violation of Mass. Const. Decl. Rights art. XII or the federal constitution. No double jeopardy violation arose from the choice to group the images according to the media upon which they were stored. The improper admission of prior bad act evidence was not prejudicial. Trial counsel was not ineffective in failing to file a suppression motion that was likely futile. Defendant claimed that he had a low IQ, but said that he understood the Miranda warnings, and showed computer literacy and proficiency sufficient to permit him to navigate the Internet, download photographs, use software to erase incriminating materials, communicate by email, trade materials with other Internet users, purchase and return computer equipment, and display a level of sophistication about the capabilities of his computer equipment, software, and printers. Further, defendant's ability to offer an exculpatory explanation for the pornography suggested that his statements were voluntary. Defendant's claim of cumulative error was rejected.


OUTCOME: The judgments were affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Werner


No. 07-P-582.


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


73 Mass. App. Ct. 97; 896 N.E.2d 45; 2008 Mass. App. LEXIS 1112


February 8, 2008, Argued 
November 5, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Commonwealth v. Werner, 2008 Mass. LEXIS 964 (Mass., Dec. 17, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Suffolk. Indictments found and returned in the Superior Court Department on November 7, 1991. A motion for a new trial, filed on June 23, 2004, was heard by Robert A. Mulligan, J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Suffolk County Superior Court (Massachusetts), which denied defendant's motion for a new trial as to his convictions for armed assault in a dwelling under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 265, § 18A; assault by means of a dangerous weapon under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 265, § 15B(b); and unlawful possession of a firearm under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 269, § 10(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the Commonwealth had not established the essential elements of armed assault in a dwelling and that his pretrial motion to suppress evidence was improperly denied. On appeal, the court affirmed. While defendant waived the issues as he did not pursue them on direct appeal, the court reviewed them to determine whether any error created a substantial risk of a miscarriage of justice. An entry occurred within the meaning of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 265, § 18A because while defendant was outside the apartment, the gun he used to threaten the victim crossed the plane of the doorway, which was missing its top screen, into the dwelling. About an hour after the victim spoke to the police, the police received a call that a man in a local bar had a firearm. The police arrived in a marked cruiser with its blue lights flashing. The police did not stop defendant in the bar without reasonable suspicion before he reached for his waist after being asked if he possessed a firearm because the use of the blue lights on the cruiser was prior to the police's arrival at the bar and did not convert the officers' exploratory questioning of defendant into a stop.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the motion for a new trial.

Commonwealth v. Lindsey


No. 07-P-696.


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


72 Mass. App. Ct. 485; 893 N.E.2d 52; 2008 Mass. App. LEXIS 1069


February 11, 2008, Argued 
August 29, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Commonwealth v. Lindsey, 452 Mass. 1109, 897 N.E.2d 592, 2008 Mass. LEXIS 941 (2008)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Lindsey v. Massachusetts, 129 S. Ct. 2008, 173 L. Ed. 2d 1087, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 3057 (U.S., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Suffolk. Indictments found and returned in the Superior Court Department on March 28, 2002. A pretrial motion to suppress evidence and a motion to dismiss were heard by Barbara J. Rouse, J., and the cases were tried before Margaret R. Hinkle, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to the Fourth Amendment and Mass. Const. Decl. Rights art. 14, defendant moved to suppress evidence seized from his home. The Suffolk Superior Court (Massachusetts) denied the motion, and defendant was convicted on 14 indictments related to the illegal and unlicensed possession of firearms. He appealed his convictions and the sentence imposed under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 269, § 10(m), for possession of large capacity feeding devices.


OVERVIEW: A 911 caller reported that an elderly woman was trembling and asking for help. An officer was directed to the woman's home. The front door was locked; firefighters forced it open. While searching for the woman, officers entered a bedroom where they saw in plain view two handguns, one with a silencer. Other guns and ammunition were in plain view in the home. Defendant returned home with his elderly mother, who was shaking and disoriented. There were large capacity feeding devices for which defendant had no license; one of the guns had a defaced serial number and another was listed as stolen. The appellate court held the officers' entry into the home and bedroom was permissible under the "emergency exception" to the warrant requirement, as the purpose of the search was to protect life and not to gather evidence of criminal activity. That the prosecution failed to turn over a police report for a year, and that a witness whose address was in the report had moved and could not be located, did not entitle defendant to relief, as he did not show the witness's testimony would have helped him. Section § 10(m) required the trial court to impose a mandatory minimum sentence of 2 1/2 years.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Silva v. City of Attleboro


No. 07-P-488.


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


72 Mass. App. Ct. 450; 892 N.E.2d 792; 2008 Mass. App. LEXIS 905


January 18, 2008, Argued 
August 27, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Silva v. City of Attleboro, 2008 Mass. LEXIS 843 (Mass., Oct. 29, 2008)
Superseded by, Judgment entered by Silva v. City of Attleboro, 454 Mass. 165, 908 N.E.2d 722, 2009 Mass. LEXIS 325 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Bristol. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on April 27, 2005. The case was heard by Richard J. Chin, J., on an agreed statement of facts.
Silva v. City of Fall River, 59 Mass. App. Ct. 798, 798 N.E.2d 297, 2003 Mass. App. LEXIS 1183 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Bristol Superior Court Department (Massachusetts) entered a judgment in a case where defendant cities issued burial permits that found burial permit charges were proper fees assessed by the cities. Plaintiff licensed funeral director appealed.


OVERVIEW: The licensed funeral director contended that the burial permit charges levied by the cities were improper taxes. The charges were imposed to obtain burial permits to meet the Commonwealth's Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 114, § 43M requirement of disposing of dead bodies. The trial court determined from the evidence that the cities incurred significant costs in issuing burial permits. It then found that the licensed funeral director had not shown the charges were taxes. The appellate court determined that distinguishing between a tax and a fee involved application of the three-part Emerson College test. It noted that a legitimate fee was (1) charged for a government service to benefit a particular party, (2) paid voluntarily, and (3) collected to compensate the government entity. It then found that the burial permit charge was collected to compensate the cities, but that there was no question that the issuance of the permits had shared public benefits and that the services were provided involuntarily. It concluded that the third factor weighing in favor of the cities imposing a valid fee was not enough to overcome the weight of the first two factors indicating that the charges were taxes.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment.

Trinh v. Gentle Communs., LLC


No. 07-P-441


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


71 Mass. App. Ct. 368; 881 N.E.2d 1177; 2008 Mass. App. LEXIS 246


December 11, 2007, Argued 
March 10, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected April, 25, 2008


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Middlesex. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on October 30, 2000. The case was tried before Mitchell J. Sikora, Jr., J., and motions for judgment notwithstanding the verdict were heard by him.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee sued defendants, an employer and a supervisor, in the Middlesex Superior Court Department (Massachusetts) for the supervisor's sexual harassment. The trial court allowed judgment notwithstanding the verdict as to a lost income award, a finding of the employer's direct liability, and a punitive damages award against the employer, but otherwise denied such relief. Defendants appealed and the employee cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The supervisor was in charge of the office where the employee worked. The appellate court held enough evidence showed he sexually harassed the employee, based on his sexually suggestive comments and actions, which were objectively offensive and severe and pervasive enough to support a finding of harassment and ensuing emotional distress damages. The employer was vicariously liable for his sexual harassment and for compensatory damages. Judgment notwithstanding the verdict was proper as to the employee's lost income award because she resigned and did not show constructive discharge, as she was transferred to another office, and no adverse action was taken against her. The investigation of her complaint did not show intolerable working conditions, especially since she did not participate after making her complaint. The supervisor's conduct supported a punitive damages award against him, and their amount was not excessive. The evidence did not show the employer inadequately or inappropriately investigated the matter, so its direct liability was not shown, and there was no factual predicate for awarding punitive damages against it directly.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Becker


No. 06-P-1425.


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


71 Mass. App. Ct. 81; 879 N.E.2d 691; 2008 Mass. App. LEXIS 63


September 12, 2007, Argued 
January 25, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected February 19, 2008.
Review denied by Commonwealth v. Becker, 2008 Mass. LEXIS 751 (Mass., June 5, 2008)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Becker v. Massachusetts, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 5992 (U.S., Oct. 6, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Berkshire. Complaint received and sworn to in the Southern Berkshire Division of the District Court Department on February 4, 2005. The case was tried before Fredric D. Rutberg, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, after the denial of his motion for a required finding of not guilty, was convicted by a jury in the Southern Berkshire Division of the District Court Department (Massachusetts) of failing to register as a sex offender pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 6, § 178H (as amended by 1999 Mass. Acts ch. 74, § 2). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's underlying offense was a conviction in New York for sexual abuse in the third degree for touching a 19-year-old woman's buttocks without her permission or consent. Defendant argued that he did not come within the definition of "sex offender" in the Massachusetts Sex Offender Registration Statute, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 6, §§ 178C - 178P, and that he was not required to register as a sex offender. On appeal, the court found that the jury could have rationally concluded that (1) defendant's conviction in New York constituted a sex offense under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 6, § 178C; (2) the New York statute under which defendant was convicted was sufficiently like the prohibition in Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 265, § 13H for indecent assault and battery on a person over 14; (3) defendant was a resident of Massachusetts; and (4) defendant knowingly failed to register. In addition, the trial judge properly instructed the jury. Finally, the Sex Offender Registration Statute was not unconstitutional as applied to defendant as his constitutional right to travel under the Privileges and Immunities Clause was not violated and his right to be free from cruel and unusual punishment was not violated.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Ferreira


No. 06-P-1370


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


70 Mass. App. Ct. 32; 872 N.E.2d 808; 2007 Mass. App. LEXIS 949


May 10, 2007, Argued 
August 30, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected September 21, 2007.
Review denied by Commonwealth v. Ferreira, 450 Mass. 1101, 875 N.E.2d 862, 2007 Mass. LEXIS 756 (Mass., Oct. 31, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Essex. Complaint received and sworn to in the Peabody Division of the District Court Department on March 28, 2005. The case was heard by Santo J. Ruma, J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted, after a jury-waived trial in the Peabody Division of the Essex District Court Department (Massachusetts), of negligently operating a motor vehicle in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 90, § 24(2)(a). The charge resulted from an incident involving defendant's operation of a motor vehicle in a shopping center parking lot. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that there was insufficient evidence to support his conviction. Specifically, defendant challenged the element of negligent operation so as to endanger the lives and safety of the public. The appellate court found that the incident occurred in the middle of the day, in a busy shopping center parking lot with "moderate to heavy" vehicle and pedestrian traffic, and on a surface that had recently been subject to large amounts of snow. The evidence of defendant's behavior, when viewed in relation to the attendant circumstances, was sufficient to prove that his conduct might have endangered the lives of the public. The lack of evidence of continuing excessive speed was only one factor to be considered when determining whether the lives of the public could have been endangered. The evidence was sufficient to withstand a motion for a required finding of not guilty. Defendant's argument that Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 90, § 24(2)(a) was unconstitutionally vague because it failed to give fair warning of the proscribed conduct and was subject to arbitrary application was not entitled to consideration because it was raised for the first time on appeal.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Bellemare v. Clermont


No. 06-P-1047


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


69 Mass. App. Ct. 566; 870 N.E.2d 624; 2007 Mass. App. LEXIS 808


February 13, 2007, Argued 
July 18, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Bellamare v. Clermont, 449 Mass. 1112, 874 N.E.2d 407, 2007 Mass. LEXIS 707 (Mass., Sept. 26, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Essex. Civil action commenced in the Northeast Division of the Housing Court Department on February 13, 2004. The case was heard by David D. Kerman, J., on a motion for summary judgment.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff lead paint victim filed suit against defendant, an attorney's secretary, individually and as trustee and against defendant co-trustees, individually and as trustees, alleging violations of the lead poisoning prevention act, warranty of habitability, and Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 186, § 14. The secretary filed a third-party complaint for indemnification against the estate of the attorney.


OVERVIEW: The Northeast Division of the Housing Court Department, Essex (Massachusetts), granted the secretary's summary judgment motion. The victim appealed. The appellate court held that the adoption of a statutory definition of "owner" after the cause of action accrued was not necessarily retroactive. Further, the secretary was not an owner under the new definition. The attorney and the co-trustees intended for title to the building to be held in a nominee trust. The secretary did not exercise authority with respect to the trust property, and did not receive any benefits as a result of her position. However, the trust instrument used was not normally used to create a nominee trust. The instrument was enforced to reflect the parties' intentions. Thus, the secretary was a nominee trustee and was not exposed to liability under the lead poisoning statute. The victim's claim that the secretary was an "owner" who had control of the premises under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 111, § 189A(ii) was also rejected. The purported authorization to allow the trustees to act as if the property was theirs was of little consequence as the co-trustees had to agree to any expenditure.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Portonova


No. 04-P-1527.


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


69 Mass. App. Ct. 905; 868 N.E.2d 1269; 2007 Mass. App. LEXIS 773



July 6, 2007, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the trial court (Massachusetts) that convicted him of indecent assault and battery on a mentally retarded person under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 265, § 13F; defendant claimed that the Commonwealth failed to show some sexual contact between him and the victim, and that the trial judge incorrectly charged the jury by omitting the element of lack of consent.


OVERVIEW: Defendant drove the victim, a mentally retarded person, to a motel. Once in the room, he repeatedly told her to take off her clothes; she eventually complied because she was scared. Defendant picked her up and put her on the bed, and, inter alia, told her to "play with herself," and she complied because she was scared. The appellate court found that § 13F did not proscribe only forced offensive touchings in which the perpetrator directly engaged in "sexual contact" that caused the offensive touching. In addition, the statute as applied was not unconstitutionally vague. Consent was the focus of the defense, and was an issue referred to in the opening statements and closing arguments of both counsel. Therefore, even though defendant did not object, the trial judge's failure to give a lack of consent instruction for the assault and battery counts was erroneous. Defendant was entitled to a new trial.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, the verdict was set aside, and the case was remanded for a new trial.

 

353 of 756 DOCUMENTS


United States Gypsum Co. v. Exec. Office of Envtl. Affairs


No. 06-P-169


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


69 Mass. App. Ct. 243; 867 N.E.2d 764; 2007 Mass. App. LEXIS 641


December 4, 2006, Argued  
June 4, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected July 13, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Civil actions commenced in the Superior Court Department on January 15, 2003. After consolidation, the case was heard by Ralph D. Gants, J., on motions for summary judgment and for judgment on the pleadings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners one and two filed suits seeking the reversal of a conditional exclusion from a designated port area (DPA) of two other properties. Plaintiff trustee sought the same relief and a boundary review so as to exclude property three from the DPA. The Suffolk Superior Court Department (Massachusetts) denied property owner one's and two's motions for summary judgment and the trustee's motion for judgment on the pleadings.


OVERVIEW: The trial court allowed the cross-motions for judgment on the pleadings and summary judgment of defendants, including the Director of the Massachusetts Office of Coastal Zone Management (OCZM). Property owners one and two, the trustee, and intervenor legal foundation appealed. The appellate court held that the Director did not have discretion to exclude otherwise includable property from the regulatory framework. Further, the Director's decision was not supported by substantial evidence. There was no evidence that the industrial roadway deemed important enough by the Director to exclude otherwise suitable properties from the DPA would ever be constructed, for want of financing, in the reasonably near, or even in the remote, future. There was, however, substantial evidence supporting the decision to continue property three's inclusion in the DPA. The trustee's claim that his due process rights were violated by the OCZM's failure to include him in the negotiations that led to the exclusion of the two other properties was correctly rejected. Finally, the continued inclusion of property three within the DPA did not constitute an unconstitutional regulatory taking.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed to the extent it denied the motions of property owners one and two, the trustee, and the intervenor for judgment on the pleadings and/or summary judgment seeking reversal of the decision excluding the two other properties from the DPA. In all other respects, the judgment was affirmed.

 

354 of 756 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Ramirez


No. 06-P-497


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


69 Mass. App. Ct. 9; 865 N.E.2d 1158; 2007 Mass. App. LEXIS 510


January 17, 2007, Argued  
May 10, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Hampden. Complaint received and sworn to in the Springfield Division of the District Court Department on July 7, 2005. The case was heard by William J. Boyle, J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury-waived trial, the Springfield Division of the Hampden District Court (Massachusetts) found defendant guilty of knowingly failing to register as a sex offender in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 6, § 178H, and accosting or annoying a person of the opposite sex in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, § 53. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient to show that his failure to register as a sex offender was knowing, as required by Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 6, § 178H. The complaint against defendant alleged knowledge of the duty prior to defendant's arrest. The appellate court agreed with defendant, finding that defendant was not shown that have gained knowledge of that duty until the day after the date of the offense listed on the complaint. Since the complaint alleged that defendant's failure was a continuing offense, the time period specified in the complaint was an integral part of the crime, to be proven by the Commonwealth. The Commonwealth further failed to prove that the newspaper notices were seen by defendant. Defendant also argued that the Commonwealth presented insufficient evidence to prove that his conduct was disorderly, as required for a conviction for accosting or annoying a person of the opposite sex under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, § 53. The appellate court agreed, finding that it was not reasonable to infer that defendant intended the victim to fear that harm would befall her and that there was no aggressive or invasive move by defendant toward the victim.


OUTCOME: The judgments were reversed, the guilty findings were set aside, and a judgment of not guilty was to be entered for defendant on each count.

Commonwealth v. Clark


No. 05-P-1290


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


67 Mass. App. Ct. 832; 858 N.E.2d 768; 2006 Mass. App. LEXIS 1297


June 14, 2006, Argued  
December 18, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected January 10, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Middlesex. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on August 15, 2000. The case was heard by Margaret R. Hinkle, J. A motion to waive the entry fee for appeal was considered in the Appeals Court by Greenberg, J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate appealed the denial by a single justice of the Appeals Court (Massachusetts) of his motion for reconsideration of the denial of his Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 261, § 27B motion for waiver of the Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 262, § 4 entry fee on the ground of his alleged indigency.


OVERVIEW: The inmate claimed for the first time on appeal that the statutory scheme was inapplicable to him as a sexually dangerous person who, he asserted, was indigent, and, in any event, unconstitutionally denied him due process and equal protection. The appellate court found that the inmate's appeal was not properly before it. Even granting the inmate the three days' grace afforded by Mass. R.Civ.P. 6(d), his notice of appeal was untimely. There was, thus, no pending appeal, much less any outstanding ruling, to which the inmate's motion for reconsideration could relate or attach. The arguments in the inmate's motion for reconsideration were predicated on his asserted "indigency," which status he never actually established and which appeared to be contrary to the definitions of "indigent" and "inmate" in Mass. Gen. Laws ch. §§ 27A, 29. Therefore, the single justice properly denied both the inmate's Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 261, § 27B motion for waiver of the Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 262, § 4 entry fee and his motion for reconsideration.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

Maher v. Justices of the Quincy Div. of the Dist. Court Dep't


No. 05-P-1785.


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


67 Mass. App. Ct. 612; 855 N.E.2d 1106; 2006 Mass. App. LEXIS 1094


September 14, 2006, Argued  
October 27, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected November 22, 2006.
Review denied by Maher v. Justices of the Quincy Div. of the Dist. Court Dep't, 448 Mass. 1105, 861 N.E.2d 29, 2007 Mass. LEXIS 101 (2007)
Subsequent appeal at, Remanded by Maher v. Ret. Bd. of Quincy, 2008 Mass. LEXIS 773 (Mass., Nov. 6, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Norfolk. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on August 27, 2004. The case was heard by Barbara A. Dortch-Okara, J., on a motion for judgment on the pleadings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, justices of a district court, dismissed plaintiff employee's petition for review, filed pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 32, § 16(3), which challenged a decision by defendant city retirement board that the employee forfeited his retirement allowance. The Superior Court, Norfolk (Massachusetts) then allowed the board's motion for judgment on the pleadings in the employee's action in the nature or certiorari. The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, who was employed as a city inspector, entered pleas of guilty on indictments charging him with violations of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 266, § 18 (breaking and entering with intent to commit a felony); Mass Gen. Laws ch. 266, § 127 (wanton destruction of property); and Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 266, § 20 (stealing personnel records). The board held that the convictions involved violations of laws applicable to the employee's position thereby resulting in forfeiture of the employee's retirement allowance pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 32, § 15(4). The court agreed that there were multiple, direct links between the criminal offenses and the employee's position because the employee removed documents from his personnel file that criticized his job performance in order to improve his chances of being reappointed. However, even though the employee did not raise his Eighth Amendment "excessive fine" challenge before the board, the issue was not waived because the board clearly had no jurisdiction to decide the constitutionality of the forfeiture provision as applied to the employee and the fact finding required to resolve the Eighth Amendment issue did not involve specialized expertise.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the superior court's judgment and remanded the case to the district court for consideration of the employee's Eighth Amendment claim.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fall River District Court (Massachusetts) denied defendant's motion for mistrial or dismissal and entered final judgments of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of two counts of indecent assault and battery on a child under the age of 14. Defendant appealed.

The appellate court found that the evidence sufficiently supported a finding of "indecency," that alleging the exact time he indecently touched them was not an element of the offense, and that the statute sufficiently informed him of the kind of conduct that was improper.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order denying defendant's motion for dismissal or mistrial was affirmed and the trial court's judgments of conviction were also affirmed.

Milton v. Comm'r of Corr.

APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS

Commonwealth v. Milton, 49 Mass. App. Ct. 552, 731 N.E.2d 101, 2000 Mass. App. LEXIS 527 (2000)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate challenged the judgment of the Suffolk Superior Court Department (Massachusetts), which denied, in part, the inmate's motion for summary judgment seeking credit toward a jail sentence in the amount 1,100 days, and was granted only 237 days of credit. Defendant, the Commissioner of Correction, had filed a cross-motion for summary judgment.

The court agreed that a prisoner should not be penalized or burdened by denial of credit when the prisoner has served time under a sentence that was reversed. Commonwealth v. Abramms


No. 04-P-1211


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


66 Mass. App. Ct. 576; 849 N.E.2d 867; 2006 Mass. App. LEXIS 679


August 5, 2005, Argued  
June 23, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected July 20, 2006.
Review denied by Commonwealth v. Abramms, 447 Mass. 1110, 854 N.E.2d 441, 2006 Mass. LEXIS 623 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Hampshire. Complaint received and sworn to in the Northampton Division of the District Court Department on April 1, 2003. The case was tried before W. Michael Goggins, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Northampton Division of the District Court Department (Massachusetts) convicted defendant under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 269, § 2, of failing to obey the order of a police officer to disperse from an unlawful assembly. Defendant appealed the conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that on its face the statute was unconstitutionally overbroad and vague unless the offense of unlawful assembly was qualified by the additional statutory terms "riotous or tumultuous." The appellate court initially found that defendant based his argument on decisional law interpreting a related but separate offense which was not determinative of the offense in question. Defendant also improperly assumed that only the crime of riot was encompassed within Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 269, §§ 1 and 2. Although riot was among the offenses included, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 269, § 2, referred to "rioters or persons unlawfully assembled." The use of the disjunctive "or" supported the conclusion that unlawful assembly was a separate offense. The appellate court held that the statute was not unconstitutional on its face because an essential element of the terms "riot" and "unlawful assembly" was the intent to commit an act of violence. Only peaceful assemblies were protected by the First Amendment. Because the statute was constitutional, and no transcript of the trial was submitted to determine the basis on which defendant was convicted, the judgment had to be affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Mass. Gen. Hosp. v. Comm'r of the Div. of Med. Assistance


No. 05-P-642


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


66 Mass. App. Ct. 485; 848 N.E.2d 1213; 2006 Mass. App. LEXIS 621


March 10, 2006, Argued  
June 8, 2006, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on July 9, 2003. The case was heard by Nonnie S. Burnes, J., on a motion for judgment on the pleadings.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a Medicaid reimbursements dispute, the Superior Court Department, Massachusetts, granted plaintiff hospital's motion for judgment on the pleadings to vacate a decision of the Commissioner of the Division of Medical Assistance, Massachusetts. The Division, which had initially denied reimbursement, appealed from the superior court's judgment. At issue was whether the services were medically necessary under 130 Mass. Code Regs. § 450.204 (2001).


OVERVIEW: The hospital sought reimbursement for inpatient services provided to three Medicaid patients. The Division denied the request, even though the services were medically appropriate under § 450.204, because they should have been provided in an outpatient setting. Thus, the services were ruled not "medically necessary." In disputing the denial, the hospital had argued that the Division's regulations violated due process because they did not give the hospital sufficient guidance for determining when a patient admission was proper. Reversing, the appeals court ruled that § 450.204 and the other regulations were not vague under the Fourteenth Amendment; the hospital did not have to guess at their meaning, and they did not set a standard that could not be ascertained. The court identified several other regulations and guidelines that gave definition to the meaning of "medically necessary," including 130 Mass. Code Regs. § 415.414(C), which gave factors and specific examples. The court also ruled that the regulations did not violate the federal mandate in 42 U.S.C.S. § 1396a(a)(30)(A) with regard to economy of care. The regulatory scheme was not arbitrary, capricious, or contrary to law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the matter to the superior court for a determination of whether there was substantial evidence to support the Division's decision in the three cases.

T & D Video, Inc. v. City of Revere


No. 05-P-109


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


66 Mass. App. Ct. 461; 848 N.E.2d 1221; 2006 Mass. App. LEXIS 620


December 14, 2005, Argued  
June 8, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended June 29, 2006.
Review denied by T & D Video, Inc. v. City of Revers, 447 Mass. 1111, 854 N.E.2d 441, 2006 Mass. LEXIS 652 (2006)
Review granted by T & D Video, Inc. v. City of Revere, 448 Mass. 1101, 858 N.E.2d 1097, 2006 Mass. LEXIS 818 (2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by City of Revere v. T&D Video, Inc., 127 S. Ct. 2905, 167 L. Ed. 2d 1152, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 6104 (U.S., 2007)
Superseded by T & D Video, Inc. v. City of Revere, 450 Mass. 107, 876 N.E.2d 842, 2007 Mass. LEXIS 737 (Mass., Nov. 27, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on November 16, 1994. The case was heard by Ernest B. Murphy, J., and a motion for attorney's fees and costs was also heard by him.
T&D Video, Inc. v. City of Revere, 2004 Mass. Super. LEXIS 72 (Mass. Super. Ct., 2004)
T & D Video v. City of Revere, 423 Mass. 577, 670 N.E.2d 162, 1996 Mass. LEXIS 217 (1996)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporation, which operated an adult video store, filed an action against defendants, a city and others, under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and the Massachusetts Civil Rights Act. The Suffolk Superior Court (Massachusetts) permanently enjoined defendants from enforcing adult entertainment ordinances against the corporation and ordered that defendants pay attorney's fees and costs of $915,027. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that the ordinances violated the First Amendment and Mass. Const. Decl. Rights art. 16. It found that because they effectively removed all possibility that the corporation could operate within the city, they could not be justified as a permissible time, place, and manner restriction. Furthermore, it found that, because the ordinances effectively banned protected speech, they operated as an impermissible prior restraint. The court held that in finding that the ordinances left no reasonable alternative sites for the corporation to operate its business on, the trial court properly credited the testimony of the corporation's land use experts. Next, the fee award under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988 and Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 12, § 11I, which included a request for fees of $500,000 for a trial that lasted less than four days and which did not separate the rate awarded to lead counsel from the rates awarded to others, was excessive. Furthermore, expert witness fees were improperly awarded under the Massachusetts Civil Rights Act because the evidence did not warrant a finding in the corporation's favor under the Act. There was no evidence of threats, intimidation, or coercion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the permanent injunction. It vacated the award of attorney's fees and costs and remanded for further proceedings consistent with its opinion.

Commonwealth v. DePeiza

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the Boston Municipal Court Department, Suffolk, (Massachusetts) that convicted him of illegal possession of a firearm and ammunition; defendant claimed that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress due to an illegal search.


OVERVIEW: Shortly after midnight, police officers in an unmarked automobile in a high crime area observed defendant walking along a sidewalk with his right arm rigid, not moving, and pressed to his side as if he were holding something. The officers approached defendant and asked him some questions. Defendant continued to shield his right side from their view. Believing that defendant's jacket contained a firearm, one of the officers told him that he intended to conduct a pat frisk. When defendant moved back to avoid being frisked, the officer grabbed defendant's right jacket pocket and felt the handle of a handgun. He reached into defendant's pocket and seized the gun. The appellate court found that the manner of defendant's walk, even in conjunction with the other factors, did not provide an objective factual basis for a reasonable suspicion that he was engaged in criminal activity. Consequently, the search violated U.S. Const. ament. IV and Fourth Amendment to the United States Constitution Mass. Const. Decl. Rights art. 14.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

Commonwealth v. Marshall


No. 04-P-680


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


65 Mass. App. Ct. 710; 843 N.E.2d 685; 2006 Mass. App. LEXIS 242


October 3, 2005, Argued  
March 8, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Commonwealth v. Marshall, 447 Mass. 1102, 848 N.E.2d 1212, 2006 Mass. LEXIS 385 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Hampden. Indictments found and returned in the Superior Court Department on May 3, 2001. The cases were tried before Judd J. Carhart, J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Superior Court Department, Hampden (Massachusetts), convicted defendant of home invasion, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 265, § 18C. Defendant appealed only from the home invasion conviction and the sentence imposed on that charge.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had lived with his girlfriend in the apartment for some time. When the couple broke up, defendant moved out. The parties continued to see each other sporadically, and defendant spent some nights at the apartment. On the night in question, defendant broke into a back door and came into the residence without the girlfriend's permission. When defendant found the victim, another man, in the residence, he shot and killed the victim. Defendant argued on appeal that the prosecution failed to prove the first element of the crime of home invasion, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 265, § 18C, that defendant knowingly entered the dwelling place of another. Defendant argued that the apartment partially belonged to him, and thus remained his dwelling place. The appellate court held that the term "dwelling place of another" referred to occupancy, not ownership interests. Defendant did not occupy the apartment at the time of the crime, as he had moved out. His visits with the girlfriend did not constitute continued occupancy. Thus, the conviction was proper. However, the court found that the sentence imposed was illegal and had to be vacated.


OUTCOME: The conviction of home invasion was affirmed. The sentence imposed was vacated, and the matter was remanded for resentencing.

Commonwealth v. Lampron


No. 04-P-982


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS

September 15, 2005, Argued

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Plymouth. Complaint received and sworn to in the Wareham Division of the District Court Department on August 6, 2003. The case was tried before Daniel W. O'Malley, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury of the Wareham Division of the Plymouth District Court Department (Massachusetts) convicted defendant of operating under the influence of liquor, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 90, § 24(1)(a)(1); operating to endanger, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 90, § 24(2)(a); and use of a motor vehicle without authority, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 90, § 24(2)(a). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant raised several issues. The appellate court concluded that defendant's hospital records were generally admissible under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 233, § 79 because there was no doubt that medical personnel obtained and recorded the information contained in the records for the purpose of treating defendant. However, in light of qualifying language in a preliminary toxicology report, it was not sufficiently reliable to be admitted under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 233, § 79. But, the erroneous admission of that report did not require reversal because the evidence of alcohol intoxication was overwhelming. In addition, the statements in the hospital records were not testimonial in fact and did not violate the Confrontation Clause because the challenged notations appear to have been made within hours or a day after his admission and were related to evaluating his condition at the time of his admission in order to determine appropriate treatment. The notations were not made in anticipation of their use in the investigation and prosecution of a crime. Crawford did not render Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 233, § 79 unconstitutional. Defendant was tried on only one theory of impairment.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed.

Amberwood Dev. Corp. v. Bd. of Appeals


No. 04-P-1599


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


65 Mass. App. Ct. 205; 837 N.E.2d 1161; 2005 Mass. App. LEXIS 1125


September 13, 2005, Argued  
November 29, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected January 25, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Land Court Department on June 20, 2000. The case was heard by Karyn F. Scheier, J., on motions for summary judgment.
AMBERWOOD DEV. CORP. v. CARGILL, 12 LCR 328, 2004 Mass. LCR LEXIS 78 (2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant town appealed a judgment by the Suffolk Land Court Department (Massachusetts) that reversed a decision by defendant zoning board of appeals, and ruled that the application of a provision in the zoning by-laws was unconstitutional as applied to plaintiff owner; the town claimed that the owner was not injured by application of the by-laws.


OVERVIEW: The owner obtained approval in 1997 to subdivide a tract containing approximately 22 acres into four separate lots, including the 8.1-acre locus. The local zoning by-laws provided that the minimum street frontage was 250 feet. The locus had frontage of only 100 feet, but the owner was able to build a single family home on the locus by taking advantage of a "frontage exception for larger lots" in the zoning by-laws. Thereafter, the owner sought to convey a two-acre portion of the locus to become part of an adjoining lot, which was owned by the trustee, its president. The owner sought a variance under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 40A, § 10 from the frontage exception provision in Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 240, § 14A. The appellate court held that the owner failed to show significant injury to its interest in the locus, i.e., that the prohibition against conveying out the two-acre parcel was arbitrary, unreasonable, and oppressive. The relief allowed by the Land Court undermined the uniform application of otherwise valid local zoning. The owner's goal could be accomplished without such invalidation.


OUTCOME: The judgment was vacated insofar as it declared the by-law invalid as applied, and a new judgment was entered declaring that the provision was valid as applied; the remainder of the judgment was affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Jean-Pierre


No. 04-P-1292


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


65 Mass. App. Ct. 162; 837 N.E.2d 707; 2005 Mass. App. LEXIS 1106


October 3, 2005, Argued  
November 23, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Commonwealth v. Jean-Pierre, 446 Mass. 1102, 842 N.E.2d 951, 2006 Mass. LEXIS 79 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Middlesex. Complaints received and sworn to in the Woburn Division of the District Court Department on February 24, 2003, and March 14, 2003, respectively. The cases were tried before Barbara Savitt Pearson, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In the Middlesex District Court (Massachusetts), defendant was convicted of assault and battery causing serious bodily injury under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 265, § 13A. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant hit a victim's jaw. The blow broke the jaw and required the victim to be fed through a tube for six weeks pending his recovery. Defendant contended that Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 265, § 13A required that any impairment of bodily function be permanent in order to constitute a serious bodily injury. The court rejected defendant's argument and determined that loss or impairment of a bodily function did not need to be permanent to meet the definition of "serious bodily injury" under the statute. A construction that applied "permanent" to modify only "disfigurement" was the most natural and sensible reading of the sentence structure in the statutory definition. The overall statutory scheme, defining increasingly aggravated forms of assault and battery, with concomitantly increasing penalties, also supported the court's interpretation. Also, it would have been anomalous if a greater injury were required to prove assault and battery causing serious bodily injury than to prove mayhem, a crime which carried a more severe penalty, but which did not require infliction of permanent injury.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgments.

Commonwealth v. Farley


No. 04-P-811


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


64 Mass. App. Ct. 854; 835 N.E.2d 1159; 2005 Mass. App. LEXIS 996


May 13, 2005, Argued  
October 26, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected December 8, 2005.
Review denied by Commonwealth v. Farley, 446 Mass. 1102, 842 N.E.2d 951, 2006 Mass. LEXIS 75 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Worcester. Complaint received and sworn to in the Westborough Division of the District Court Department on August 16, 2001. The case was tried before Paul S. Waickowski, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed, and the matter remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Westborough Division of the District Court Department (Massachusetts) of unlawful possession of a firearm without a license to carry, in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 269, § 10(a). He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for having a handgun in his car without a valid license. He produced evidence at trial that his license to carry the handgun had expired; that as of the date of his arrest, he had not received notice that his license had been revoked, suspended, or denied; and that he had not submitted a renewal application. The appellate court held that this evidence was sufficient to raise the affirmative defense provided by Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 140, § 131(m), and thereby to shift to the Commonwealth the burden of establishing beyond a reasonable doubt that the defense did not exist. The Commonwealth presented no evidence to establish that, had defendant applied, § 131(d) would have mandated denial of his application under one of the seven disqualifying criteria. The trial court reversibly erred by not instructing the jury as to the prosecution's burden to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that this defense did not exist. Defendant was not entitled to an instruction that § 131(e) required the police department to notify him in writing of the reason for denying him an application for renewal of his license, as § 131 did not state that a denial was ineffective if not in writing.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

PRIOR HISTORY: Worcester. Indictments found and returned in the Superior Court Department on November 14, 1997. The cases were tried before Tina S. Page, J., and a motion for a new trial, filed on March 17, 2000, was heard by Timothy S. Hillman, J.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury convicted defendant of three counts of rape of a child and five counts of indecent assault and battery of a child under the age of 14. The Worcester Superior Court Department (Massachusetts) sentenced defendant to concurrent life terms for two of the rape convictions, 28 years for the other rape conviction, and concurrent terms of 20 to 30 years for each of the assault convictions, to be served after the life terms. OVERVIEW: In addition to the charges in the instant action, defendant was charged with similar offenses, relating to the same victim, in another county. Defendant was acquitted on those charges. OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Boston Water & Sewer Comm'n v. Commonwealth


No. 04-P-534


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


64 Mass. App. Ct. 611; 834 N.E.2d 1205; 2005 Mass. App. LEXIS 893


March 11, 2005, Argued  
September 28, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected November 1, 2005.
Review denied by Boston Water & Sewer Comm'n v. Commonwealth, 445 Mass. 1106, 838 N.E.2d 576, 2005 Mass. LEXIS 645 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on January 15, 2003. The case was heard by Christine M. McEvoy, J., on a motion for judgment on the pleadings.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a city utility, filed an action against defendant, a university, seeking a declaratory judgment regarding the validity of the university's taking of land by eminent domain. The Superior Court Department, Suffolk (Massachusetts), dismissed the complaint. The utility appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: When the university was granted authority to build a campus in Boston, it was granted authority to take land, with the exception of land owned by the utility and used for sewer pumping stations and other uses. Eventually, the utility decided to move its sewer operation, and the utility and the university engaged in negotiations concerning the university's taking of the land. In addition, the legislature enacted special legislation which allowed for the taking of the disputed property. At issue was the Spence doctrine, which held that state agencies could not challenge the constitutionality of the acts of another state agency. The utility and the university were both acting in their public capacities, and there was predominantly a public aspect to their dealings. The court held that it was clear from the language of the amendment in question that the legislature intended for title in the property to vest upon the passage of the act. The court further held that the utility could not circumvent the Spence doctrine, and thus it could not challenge the constitutionality of the amendment. Therefore, the trial court properly dismissed the case.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

370 of 756 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Fleury


No. 04-P-1201


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


64 Mass. App. Ct. 282; 832 N.E.2d 1145; 2005 Mass. App. LEXIS 772


May 5, 2005, Argued  
August 17, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Commonwealth v. Fleury, 445 Mass. 1104, 835 N.E.2d 254, 2005 Mass. LEXIS 744 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Essex. Indictment found and returned in the Superior Court Department on February 16, 1983. A motion for a new trial, filed on April 29, 2004, was considered by Richard E. Welch, III, J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was indicted for murder in the first degree but pled guilty in the Essex Superior Court Department (Massachusetts) to murder in the second degree. He appealed when the trial court denied his motion for new trial in which he sought to withdraw the guilty plea.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that although Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 265, § 1 defined murder in the second degree, it did not set forth an existing crime but merely addressed the mitigation of punishment. The court disagreed. At common law, murder was a crime committed with premeditation and malice aforethought. The punishment was death. As murder was codified, initially under 1858 Mass. Acts ch. 154, Massachusetts adopted the common law definition but set murder out in two degrees. Premeditated murder constituted murder in the first degree, while murder committed with malice aforethought but not with premeditation, was considered murder in the second degree, punishable by life in prison. The crime of murder in the second degree existed under Massachusetts statutory law and tracked the common-law definition of murder, incorporating that portion of the common law definition of murder that was not incorporated into the statutory definition of murder in the first degree.


OUTCOME: The denial of defendant's motion for a new trial was affirmed.

 

371 of 756 DOCUMENTS


D.H.L. Assocs. v. Bd. of Selectmen


No. 04-P-699


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


64 Mass. App. Ct. 254; 833 N.E.2d 149; 2005 Mass. App. LEXIS 764


April 7, 2005, Argued  
August 15, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected October 5, 2005.
Review denied by D.H.L. Assocs. v. Bd. of Selectmen of Tyncsdorough, 445 Mass. 1104, 835 N.E.2d 254, 2005 Mass. LEXIS 753 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Middlesex. Civil actions commenced in the Superior Court Department on September 8, 1994, and February 18, 2000, respectively. After consolidation, the cases were heard by Elizabeth M. Fahey, J., on motions for summary judgment.
D.H.L. Assocs. v. Krusell, 1996 Mass. Super. LEXIS 47 (Mass. Super. Ct., Nov. 22, 1996)



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff club brought an action against defendant town, seeking relief from the town's denial of the club's applications for an adult entertainment license. After removal to a federal court, a judgment in favor of the town on the club's federal claims, and a remand, the Superior Court Department, Middlesex (Massachusetts), found in favor of the town on the club's state claims. The club appealed.


OVERVIEW: The town rejected the club's applications for a license nine times because the club was located outside of the town's adult entertainment zone. The federal courts upheld the constitutionality of the adult entertainment zone. The appellate court held that Mass. Const. Decl. Rights art. XVI provided no greater protection from compliance with zoning than did the First Amendment. Mass. Const. Decl. Rights art. XVI only required the town to show that its stated concerns about the secondary effects of adult entertainment had some basis in fact and were actually a motivating factor in the decision to create the zone. These factual matters were conclusively determined against the club in the federal cases, and principles of issue preclusion prevented those issues from being re-litigated. The trial court correctly found that the remainder of the club's state law claims were moot. Because the club could not have been "grandfathered" for purposes of zoning, the constitutionality of the earlier zones became moot issues with the enactment of the current zone. Even if the denial of the licenses in prior years were somehow improper, the club's claims still did not present a live issue.


OUTCOME: The judgments were affirmed.

 

372 of 756 DOCUMENTS


Doe v. Moe


No. 02-P-381


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


63 Mass. App. Ct. 516; 827 N.E.2d 240; 2005 Mass. App. LEXIS 458


November 20, 2003, Argued  
May 16, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Essex. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on September 23, 1997. The case was heard by Thomas P. Billings, J., on a motion for summary judgment.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sued defendant, seeking to recover damages for injuries suffered during consensual sexual intercourse. The Superior Court Department, Essex (Massachusetts), granted defendant's motion to dismiss. Plaintiff appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: While engaged in consensual sexual intercourse, plaintiff was lying on his back while defendant was on top of him. Defendant unilaterally decided to unlock her legs and place her feet on either side of plaintiff's abdomen. When defendant changed her position, she did not think about the possibility of injury to plaintiff. Shortly after taking this new position, defendant landed awkwardly on plaintiff, thereby causing him to suffer a penile fracture. The appellate court held that there were no comprehensive legal rules to regulate consensual sexual behavior and there were no commonly accepted customs or values that determined parameters for the intensely private and widely diverse forms of such behavior. In the absence of a consensus of community values or customs defining normal consensual sexual conduct, a jury or judge could not be expected to resolve a claim that certain consensual sexual conduct was undertaken without reasonable care. Therefore, no duty of reasonable care was owed by defendant. The appellate court further held that the record did not depict conduct that could be categorized as wanton or reckless. Thus, the action was properly dismissed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Urkiel


No. 03-P-1402


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


63 Mass. App. Ct. 445; 826 N.E.2d 769; 2005 Mass. App. LEXIS 429


September 14, 2004, Argued  
May 6, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Franklin. Complaint received and sworn to in the Greenfield Division of the District Court Department on June 19, 2002. The case was heard by Jacques Leroy, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Greenfield Division of the District Court Department (Massachusetts), which, after a bench trial, convicted defendant of unlawfully resisting arrest by certain town police officers in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 268, § 32B. Defendant contended that the trial court erred in its handling of the issue, tendered by defendant, of self defense against excessive force used by the police officers.


OVERVIEW: Police officers went to defendant's house for the purpose of arresting him for violating a restraining order. The officer testified at trial that, when defendant was informed that he was under arrest, defendant pulled the officer aside and attacked him, repeatedly striking him and another officer. He was eventually arrested and was charged with violating § 32B. In contrast to the officer's testimony, defendant testified that the officers never told him of their purpose to arrest him and that, as defendant opened the front door, the officer rushed at him. Defendant testified that the officer attacked him, repeatedly punching him. The trial court refused to accept for his own guidance a general instruction on self-defense, and defendant was convicted. On appeal, the court held that, since there was no indication that the trial judge weighed the evidence on the self-defense proposition, the trial court committed prejudicial error calling for a new trial. According to the court, defendant was entitled to the judge's consideration of an implicit self-defense instruction because the evidence presented allowed the finding that the elements of a self-defense claim existed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.

Commonwealth v. Kendrick


No. 03-P-336


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


63 Mass. App. Ct. 142; 823 N.E.2d 801; 2005 Mass. App. LEXIS 225


February 9, 2004, Argued  
March 11, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected May 9, 2005.
Review granted by Commonwealth v. Kendrick, 444 Mass. 1103, 829 N.E.2d 224, 2005 Mass. LEXIS 316 (2005)
Superseded by Commonwealth v. Kendrick, 446 Mass. 72, 841 N.E.2d 1235, 2006 Mass. LEXIS 28 (Mass., Feb. 9, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Worcester. Complaint received and sworn to in the Clinton Division of the District Court Department on March 22, 1999. A probation revocation hearing was held by Martha A. Scannell Brennan, J.



DISPOSITION: Order revoking probation and imposing sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to two counts of indecent assault and battery on a child, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 265, § 13B, and was sentenced to prison and five years of probation with a special condition that defendant should have no contact with children under 16 years of age. Later, the Clinton Division of the District Court Department, Worcester (Massachusetts), found that defendant had violated the restriction and revoked probation. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that he had an absolute affirmative defense to the no-contact probation violation in that he did not speak to, communicate with, touch, or have physical interaction with any member of the protected class. The court held that the record established that defendant violated the probationary term of no contact with children under 16 years of age and that revocation of probation was warranted. The evidence established that defendant intentionally positioned himself with his dog and antique car at a car show held in the parking lot of a candy store, a place where it was objectively reasonable to believe that children under the age of 16 would likely be in attendance. It was reasonable to find that the encounter at the car show had been contrived by defendant to place himself near the protected class. Further, the modus operandi of displaying his antique car and dog to entice children (a pattern and course of conduct exhibited in defendant's underlying sexual offenses) also supported the probation revocation. Finally, when defendant became aware that children under the age of 16 were present at the car show, he could have and should have left.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order revoking probation and imposing sentence was affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Wilcox


No. 03-P-752


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


63 Mass. App. Ct. 131; 823 N.E.2d 808; 2005 Mass. App. LEXIS 226


February 9, 2004, Argued  
March 11, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected May 9, 2005.
Review granted by Commonwealth v. Wilcox, 444 Mass. 1103, 829 N.E.2d 224, 2005 Mass. LEXIS 317 (2005)
Superseded by Commonwealth v. Wilcox, 446 Mass. 61, 841 N.E.2d 1240, 2006 Mass. LEXIS 26 (Mass., Feb. 9, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Norfolk. Complaint received and sworn to in the Wrentham Division of the District Court Department on August 17, 2000. A probation revocation hearing was held by Robert E. Baylor, J.



DISPOSITION: Order revoking probation and imposing sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who pled guilty to making annoying telephone calls and accosting, appealed the revocation of his probation by the Wrentham Division of the District Court Department (Massachusetts). Defendant argued, inter alia, that it was not proved by the evidence proffered at the revocation hearing that he violated the condition requiring him not to have unsupervised contact with anyone under the age of 16.


OVERVIEW: Defendant followed three young girls, drove his car close to one 14 year old girl as she walked home from school, stared at that girl and two other young girls from within a small grocery store, followed them back to the home of one, and repeatedly drove around the block. The appellate court held that a violation of a probationary no contact condition was proved by defendant's acts, in which defendant, by deliberate design, intentionally and inconsistently with the probationary restriction, positioned and interposed himself in a place wherein he knew or reasonably should have known that a protected person would be present, but nonetheless proceeded intentionally to position himself in that critical space in close proximity to a protected class and maintained a looming presence, posing a real and present risk. The Mass. Dist. Ct. R. Prob. Violation Proc. 6(b) requirement of written findings did not apply because the revocation of probation was not based solely on hearsay evidence as, among other evidence, defendant made inculpatory statements. Defendant cited no authority for the proposition that Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, § 99, applied to recordings made outside of Massachusetts.


OUTCOME: The order revoking defendant's probation and imposing a sentence was affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Rosa


No. 03-P-979


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


62 Mass. App. Ct. 622; 818 N.E.2d 621; 2004 Mass. App. LEXIS 1368


June 9, 2004, Argued  
December 3, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Commonwealth v. Rosa, 443 Mass. 1103, 822 N.E.2d 303, 2005 Mass. LEXIS 49 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Bristol. Indictment found and returned in the Superior Court Department on May 17, 2002. The case was tried before Richard J. Chin, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a Superior Court Department, Bristol (Massachusetts) judgment on a jury verdict, which convicted him of indecent assault and battery on a child under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 265, § 13B, after an incident in which he put his thumb inside the mouth of a 12-year-old girl, while talking to her about sucking it. He challenged the law's constitutionality, the sufficiency of the evidence, evidentiary rulings, and the jury charge.


OVERVIEW: The appeals court held, first, that the evidence was sufficient and the law was not unconstitutionally vague. Massachusetts case law and common understanding provided a strong context for what constituted indecent behavior with a child, and defendant's own statements indicated that he well understood that he committed such behavior when he sought to entice the victim into participating with him in an act of pseudo-fellatio. Testimony regarding the victim's subjective understanding of what defendant meant by his references to sucking was probative on the issue of the indecency of the behavior, and given the other evidence, would not have led to a miscarriage of justice in any event. Finally, defendant's statements to the victim and to the police when they arrived, were highly probative of his intent to engage in indecent conduct. It was not error to instruct jurors that they might take those statements into account in their deliberations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.
