Sabree v. Conley


No. 02-P-1267


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


62 Mass. App. Ct. 901; 815 N.E.2d 280; 2004 Mass. App. LEXIS 1089



September 27, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Sabree v. Conley, 443 Mass. 1102, 820 N.E.2d 259, 2004 Mass. LEXIS 913 (2004)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former inmate filed suit, essentially alleging civil rights violations, against defendant Massachusetts Department of Correction and several correction officers (Department) for a visual body cavity search viewed by several prison visitors. The Massachusetts Superior Court granted the Department's motion for summary judgment based, in part, on grounds of qualified immunity. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: Before returning to their housing units from the recreation yard, the inmate and numerous other male inmates were strip-searched in groups of about three in an outside alcove walled on three sides with the fourth bounded by a chain link fence. A few women and children, leaving the prison, allegedly saw the inmates. The inmate conceded that the search was justified by suspicion of contraband. However, he claimed it was unduly invasive. The appellate court held that his claim for damages under the State Civil Rights Act failed as he showed no threats, intimidation, or coercion associated with the search. Also, it was not conducted for an illegitimate or vindictive purpose. While there were certain factual disputes regarding the search, the Department was entitled to immunity as it was not on fair notice that the search violated the Fourth Amendment. In addition, the trial court did not err in allowing summary judgment on the inmate's claims related to his transfer to a less desirable cell. The trial court correctly allowed the Department's motion for summary judgment as the record raised no inference of retaliatory motive.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Zora Enters. v. Burnett


Nos. 02-P-161 & 02-P-1618


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


61 Mass. App. Ct. 341; 810 N.E.2d 835; 2004 Mass. App. LEXIS 690


December 16, 2003, Argued  
June 21, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Zora Enters. v. Burnett, 442 Mass. 1109, 815 N.E.2d 1085, 2004 Mass. LEXIS 662 (2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Zora Enters. v. Burnett, 543 U.S. 1150, 161 L. Ed. 2d 112, 125 S. Ct. 1322, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 1515 (U.S., Feb. 22, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Plymouth. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on October 24, 1997. The case was tried before Richard J. Chin, J. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on July 24, 2000. A motion to dismiss was heard by Richard J. Chin, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment in Appeal No. 02-P-161 affirmed. Portion of judgment in Appeal No. 02-P-1618 specifying that Zora has acquired title to the disputed portion of Old Knoll Road by adverse possession reversed. A declaratory judgment that the Burnetts have title to that portion of Old Knoll Road that abuts their property shall be entered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated appeals arising from determinations in the Plymouth Superior Court (Massachusetts) regarding ownership of the fee interest in a portion of a way, plaintiff grantees sought review of a judgment declaring that title to the property was in defendant grantor by adverse possession. The grantor sought review of a dismissal of its complaint seeking relief from the operation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 183, § 58.


OVERVIEW: The grantees filed suit against the grantor, seeking a declaration that they were the owners of the fee underlying a way. The grantor counterclaimed, alleging that it had acquired title to the fee by adverse possession. The trial court determined that the deed conveying the parcel in question was governed by § 58. The grantor then filed suit for a declaration that retroactive application of § 58 was unconstitutional. The trial court dismissed the suit pursuant to Mass. R. Civ. P. 12(b)(9) on the ground that a prior action was pending. The grantor subsequently obtained a verdict in its favor in the first action. On appeal, the court held that the trial court properly dismissed the grantor's action because the grantor had an opportunity to litigate its constitutional claim in the first action and did not do so. The court further held that the grantees were entitled to judgment in the first action because the grantor failed to establish its adverse possession claim. The court found that the case was tried by both parties on the theory that the grantor had permissive rights in the way and, thus, the grantor's use of the way was not "irreconcilable" with use of the property as a way.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the grantor's complaint, reversed the trial court's judgment specifying that the grantor had acquired title to the disputed portion of the way by adverse possession, and entered a declaratory judgment that the grantees had title to that portion of the way that abutted their property.

Zanghi v. Bd. of Appeals of Bedford


No. 02-P-1271


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


61 Mass. App. Ct. 82; 807 N.E.2d 221; 2004 Mass. App. LEXIS 465


November 6, 2003, Argued  
May 3, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Zanghi v. Bd. of Appeals of Bedford, 442 Mass. 1106, 812 N.E.2d 922, 2004 Mass. LEXIS 550 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Land Court Department on April 12, 1996. The case was heard by Peter W. Kilborn, C.J. Mark W. Corner for the plaintiff.
Zanghi v. Caban, 2002 Mass. LCR LEXIS 81 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant board of appeals denied plaintiff property owner's petition to reverse the denial of his application for a building permit. The owner filed suit seeking damages and a declaratory judgment that application of Bedford, Mass., Zoning By-laws § 6.2.1 to his lot was unconstitutional because it deprived him of all economically beneficial use of the lot. The Massachusetts land court denied the owner relief, and he sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The owner bought a parcel long before enactment of § 6.2.1, subdivided it, and developed some of the lots. Pursuant to § 6.2.1, a buildable lot in a residential-A district had to have at least 26,000 square feet, no portion of which could be in a flood plain or wetland district. The owners' lot did not comply. The land court found that there was no taking because, inter alia, the lot could be combined with the owner's contiguous lots for cluster development, so he was not deprived of all use of the lot. The appellate court agreed. Further, the owner could have built on the lot before § 6.2.1 was enacted but did not; it was unreasonable for him to assume that the zoning by-laws would never change. The ordinance, as applied to the owner's lot, did not constitute a "taking" because (1) his property was not deprived of all economically beneficial use; (2) the ordinance was valid as applied to his property because it advanced legitimate state interests; (3) his investment-backed expectations were not unreasonably frustrated; (4) the economic impact of the ordinance on the property was not severe; and (5) there was no physical invasion of the property.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Laws ch. 92A 1/2, defendant landowners appealed from a summary judgment of the Superior Court Department, Suffolk (Massachusetts), in favor of plaintiff Commonwealth and finding the Act did not violate due process.

Commonwealth v. Panagopoulos


No. 02-P-631


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


60 Mass. App. Ct. 327; 801 N.E.2d 317; 2004 Mass. App. LEXIS 18


November 6, 2003, Argued  
January 8, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Commonwealth v. Panagopoulos, 441 Mass. 1104, 805 N.E.2d 44, 2004 Mass. LEXIS 185 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Indictment found and returned in the Superior Court Department on November 9, 1998. A motion to dismiss was heard by Elizabeth Bowen Donovan, J., and the case was tried before Robert A. Mulligan, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court Department, Suffolk (Massachusetts), which convicted him of two counts of violating Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 265, § 13J(b).


OVERVIEW: Two young children were killed in a fire while locked in a second-floor bedroom of an apartment which defendant shared with the children's mother. There was evidence that defendant had assisted in modifying the children's bedroom door to lock them in when defendant and the mother found it inconvenient to take care of them. Defendant was not the children's biological father, was not married to the mother, and was not the children's legal guardian, but had assumed the role of their father and provided for their supervision and care. As a result of the fire, defendant was convicted of two counts of §13J(b). The sole issue on appeal was whether Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 265, § 13J was impermissibly vague for failure to adequately define those persons subject to its prohibitions. The court concluded that it was not. The words used in § 13J, in their statutory context, did not require persons of ordinary intelligence to speculate as to their meaning. Persons having "care and custody" were understood to include not only biological parents, but any persons, regardless of formal familial relationship, who had assumed either permanent or temporary responsibility for a child's care.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

Commonwealth v. Walker


No. 00-P-101


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


60 Mass. App. Ct. 255; 801 N.E.2d 267; 2004 Mass. App. LEXIS 3


October 11, 2002, Argued  
January 5, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Commonwealth v. Walker, 441 Mass. 1103, 805 N.E.2d 44, 2004 Mass. LEXIS 162 (2004)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by Commonwealth v. Walker, 442 Mass. 185, 812 N.E.2d 262, 2004 Mass. LEXIS 419 (Mass., July 23, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Norfolk. Indictments found and returned in the Superior Court Department on April 16, 1997; February 25, 1998; and July 25, 1998. A motion for joinder of indictments was heard by H.J. Smith, Jr., J., and the cases were tried before Julian T. Houston, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed in part and reversed in part; verdicts set aside in reversed judgments.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Superior Court Department at Norfolk (Massachusetts) of manslaughter, assault with intent to rape, drugging a person for sexual intercourse, four counts of assault and battery by means of a dangerous weapon, and four counts of mingling poison with food, drink, or medicine. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, on three occasions, brought a total of four women to his home, drugged them with a drink containing a prescribed sleeping medication, and then engaged in conduct that could be construed as a sexual assault or an attempted sexual assault. One of the victims died from the drink that she was given. On appeal, the court found that defendant's act in surreptitiously mixing his prescription sleeping medication with alcohol and serving the mixture to the woman who died showed an indifference to and disregard of the high degree of likelihood that substantial harm would result to her. This was enough to prove that the death resulted from defendant's wanton and reckless disregard of her health when he gave her the mixture of sleeping pills and alcohol. Thus, the involuntary manslaughter conviction was warranted. Further, a doctor's testimony was a sufficient basis from which the jury could infer that the dosage of temazepam administered to her was a poison under Ms. Gen. Laws ch. 265, § 28. However, there was no evidence that the drugs given the other women were a poison under ch. 265, § 28. Finally, the trial judge did not abuse his discretion in trying the cases together.


OUTCOME: The judgments were affirmed with the exception of three of the four indictments for mingling poison with drink. As to the three mingling poison with a drink indictments, the judgments were reversed, the verdicts set aside, and judgments were to be entered for defendant.

Commonwealth v. Lepper


No. 01-P-723


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


60 Mass. App. Ct. 36; 798 N.E.2d 1030; 2003 Mass. App. LEXIS 1281


May 9, 2003, Argued  
November 19, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Commonwealth v. Lepper, 441 Mass. 1101, 803 N.E.2d 332, 2004 Mass. LEXIS 53 (2004)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Lepper v. Russo, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 64436 (D. Mass., Aug. 31, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Worcester. Indictments found and returned in the Superior Court Department on June 12, 1998. The cases were tried before James P. Donohue, J., and a motion for a new trial, filed on November 20, 2001, was heard by him.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed; order denying motion for new trial affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury on 23 indictments of larceny by false pretenses, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 266, § 30, and four indictments of operating as a home contractor without a certificate of registration. A trial judge of the Superior Court Department, Worcester (Massachusetts), adjudicated defendant a common and notorious thief under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 266, § 40 and denied defendant's motion for a new trial. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The charges resulted from defendant's failure to erect metal storage structures for 23 customers after taking a large deposit from each customer, which was never refunded, and promising to commence construction by a specific date. The court found that (1) the evidence was sufficient to convict defendant under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 266, § 30 based either on defendant's or his employee's false statements or on a joint venture with defendant's employee; (2) defendant was properly convicted of operating without a certificate of registration under Mass. Gen. Laws. ch. 142A, § 19 because ample evidence established that the structures defendant promised to build were to be adjacent to owner-occupied buildings; (3) there was a basis for the joint venture instruction because the evidence established both the employee's criminal intent and that he and the defendant were operating in concert; (4) there was no Apprendi violation resulting from defendant's adjudication as a common and notorious thief because each of the 23 convictions was based on proof beyond a reasonable doubt; and (5) trial counsel's assistance at trial was not ineffective because defendant failed to establish harm.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments and affirmed the order denying the motion for new trial.

 

384 of 756 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Given


No. 02-P-544


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


59 Mass. App. Ct. 390; 796 N.E.2d 845; 2003 Mass. App. LEXIS 1004


June 6, 2003, Argued  
September 24, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Commonwealth v. Given, 440 Mass. 1106, 799 N.E.2d 593, 2003 Mass. LEXIS 830 (2003)
Superseded by Commonwealth v. Given, 441 Mass. 741, 808 N.E.2d 788, 2004 Mass. LEXIS 283 (Mass., May 20, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Worcester. Petition for civil commitment filed in the Superior Court Department on November 10, 2000. The case was tried before James P. Donohue, J. The case was submitted on briefs.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts) after a jury, during a trial held pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 123A, § 14 (1999), determined that defendant was a sexually dangerous person.


OVERVIEW: The Commonwealth of Massachusetts filed a petition to commit defendant as a sexually dangerous person prior to his completion of sentences for several convictions of sexually assaulting young children. At defendant's trial, a police report was admitted containing an allegation, which had not led to an indictment, that defendant had assaulted an unidentified child. The court held the admission of that evidence constituted prejudicial error and required a new trial. The record clearly showed that the police report was admitted for the truth of the matter stated therein, namely, that he had sexually assaulted the six-year-old boy on the same occasion he assaulted another young girl; the latter assault had resulted in prosecution and conviction. The assault on the boy was inadmissible under ch. 123A, § 14; it did not constitute a report relating to defendant's prior sexual offenses, and it was not admissible as "any other evidence" tending to show that defendant was sexually dangerous. The error was prejudicial because it supported an inference that defendant was seeking victims beyond those who were known to him and enhanced a picture of him as a predator who was out of control.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded for a new trial.

DuPont v. Comm'r of Corr.


No. 01-P-1792


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


59 Mass. App. Ct. 908; 794 N.E.2d 1254; 2003 Mass. App. LEXIS 935



September 5, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Dupont v. Comm'r of Corr., 441 Mass. 1102, 803 N.E.2d 333, 2004 Mass. LEXIS 102 (2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by DuPont v. Maloney, 542 U.S. 943, 124 S. Ct. 2921, 159 L. Ed. 2d 822, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 4690 (2004)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Dupont v. Nolan, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 13728 (D. Mass., Feb. 25, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Dupont v. Maloney, 2001 Mass. Super. LEXIS 233 (Mass. Super. Ct., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Order denying petition for writ of habeas corpus affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following his incarceration for multiple armed robbery and other convictions, petitioner inmate applied to the Superior Court (Massachusetts) for a writ of habeas corpus. The trial court denied his petition, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: After several convictions and parole revocations, the inmate was assigned to a prerelease halfway house, where he committed another armed robbery and other crimes. The appellate court held he was properly denied good time credit as to the sentence being served while residing at the halfway house. Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 127, § 129 (repealed), in effect when the sentence was imposed, and, therefore, applicable, precluded good time deductions for a prisoner committing a new offense while confined. A halfway house was a confining place of rehabilitation, within the definition of a correctional facility, in Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 125, § 1. The inmate's resentencing on the conviction for which he was serving this sentence, resulting in a shorter sentence that expired before he committed the new crime, gave him no relief, as his confinement when he committed the new crime was lawful until the conviction causing it was reversed. Apprendi did not apply, as a loss of statutory good time was no sentence enhancement. He was not entitled to an evidentiary hearing, as his case involved applying a statute to uncontested facts.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Whiting


No. 02-P-68


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


58 Mass. App. Ct. 918; 792 N.E.2d 1047; 2003 Mass. App. LEXIS 852



August 8, 2003, Decided



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The district court (Massachusetts) convicted defendant of open and gross lewdness in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, § 16, and with accosting or annoying a person of the opposite sex in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, § 53. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pulled into a driveway where five 13-year-old girls were playing. He told them, among other things, that he was drunk, that he was gay, that he was "looking for dick," and that he wanted to be on the Jerry Springer show. On appeal, defendant argued that the language of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, § 16 did not convey an adequate warning that his conduct was proscribed and the language had not otherwise been adequately subject to judicial construction to apply the statute to his conduct. The appellate court agreed and vacated that conviction. However, defendant was adequately notified that his behavior was prohibited under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, § 53. Defendant used sexually explicit language toward the girls, stepped out of his car, and pulled down his pants. Regardless of what the girls saw, the conduct sent them fleeing to the safety of the house. The girls testified that defendant's comments scared and confused them and made them uncomfortable due to the sexual nature of the comments, and that the girls were frightened, scared, and afraid of defendant coming out of the car and hurting them.


OUTCOME: The judgment for open and gross lewdness was vacated. The judgment for accosting or annoying a person of the opposite sex was affirmed.

Laws ch. 119, § 58(b), arguing that the statute was ambiguous and unconstitutionally vague, and that the sentence imposed on him was unlawful.

Laws ch. 119, § 54, on charges of assault with intent to murder, "carjacking," and assault and battery by means of a dangerous weapon. The plea was accepted by the court. Defendant violated his probation within two years. The judge, who was the plea and sentencing judge in the earlier proceedings, imposed the original sentence; that is, he committed defendant to the DYS until age 21 and ordered that defendant thereafter serve two years in a house of correction. The appellate court held the legislature's intent was to preserve the sentencing judge's well-established discretion to fashion either a concurrent or consecutive sentence, depending upon the circumstances. Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 119, § 58 was readily decipherable.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Tierney v. John Hancock Mut. Life Ins. Co.


No. 01-P-435


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


58 Mass. App. Ct. 571; 791 N.E.2d 925; 2003 Mass. App. LEXIS 764


October 16, 2002, Argued  
July 17, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Tierney v. John Hancock Mut. Life Ins. Co., 440 Mass. 1104, 797 N.E.2d 380, 2003 Mass. LEXIS 812 (2003)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Tierney v. John Hancock Fin., 541 U.S. 903, 158 L. Ed. 2d 244, 124 S. Ct. 1602, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 1858 (U.S., Mar. 8, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on January 7, 2000. The case was heard by Allan van Gestel, J., on motions for judgment on the pleadings.
Tierney v. John Hancock Mut. Life Ins. Co., 2000 Mass. Super. LEXIS 677 (Mass. Super. Ct., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and modified in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action for review of an agency decision under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 30A, § 14, plaintiff dissident policyholders appealed from a judgment on the pleadings of the Superior Court Department, Suffolk (Massachusetts), that upheld a decision of the Massachusetts Commissioner of Insurance approving defendant insurance company's demutualization plan, submitted pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 175, § 19E.


OVERVIEW:  Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 175, § 19E provided a method by which mutual insurance companies could convert to publicly held companies. The statute required such companies to submit plans to the commissioner that demonstrated that policyholders, the former owners of the company, would be properly compensated for their interests. Although policyholders overwhelmingly approved the insurance company's plan, and the commissioner had also approved it, two dissident policyholders challenged the plan as not providing sufficient compensation for the loss of certain rights, such as the right to vote for directors. The appellate court approved the deferential review by the trial court of the commissioner's decision, noting that her opinion made clear that she had properly considered all the factors she was required to consider in making her fairness determination and that where she had not made specific findings, she had incorporated by reference voluminous findings made in her approval of a very similar plan submitted by another insurance company, a perfectly permissible approach. The policyholders' other claims were so intertwined with the § 19E claims as to preclude separate consideration.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Commonwealth v. Aviles


No. 01-P-1441


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


58 Mass. App. Ct. 459; 790 N.E.2d 1103; 2003 Mass. App. LEXIS 730


December 16, 2002, Argued  
July 2, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected September 17, 2003.
Review denied by Commonwealth v. Aviles, 440 Mass. 1101, 795 N.E.2d 573, 2003 Mass. LEXIS 656 (Mass., Sept. 5, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictments found and returned in the Superior Court Department on January 27, 1999. A pretrial motion to suppress evidence was heard by Richard E. Welch, III, J., and the cases were tried before him.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury of four counts of rape of a child under 16, in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 265, § 23, and one count of indecent assault and battery on a child under the age of 14, in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 265, § 13B. The Superior Court Department (Massachusetts) entered judgments. Defendant appealed. Claims of error included the denial of a suppression motion and improper closing argument.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raped his wife's child repeatedly. He would ejaculate on her stomach and then wipe it off with either a towel or undershirt. After the rapes were reported, the mother consented to a search of the house. Defendant's genetic material was found on his undershirt. On appeal, defendant admitted that his wife had the authority to consent to the search, and did not challenge the authority of the police to test his undershirt for seminal fluid. However, he contended that his wife's consent could not be extended to authorize the testing of his undershirt for genetic material, as a person could not consent to the testing of someone else's genetic material. The appellate court found that where the police lawfully obtained evidence, it could be subjected to scientific testing. There was no prejudice shown in the admission of the victim's hospital records. Defense counsel's attempt to use portions of the records, in an attempt to illustrate inconsistencies, was a reasonable tactical choice and was not ineffective counsel. Although the prosecutor made a questionable comment in closing, which had the potential to elicit sympathy for the victim, it was unlikely that it was prejudicial.


OUTCOME: The judgments were affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Bartos

APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS

DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgments were affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Salem Division of the District Court Department, Essex (Massachusetts), that revoked his probation on two abuse prevention counts and committed him to concurrent two-year terms of imprisonment after finding, in a previous proceeding, that he had violated the probation by committing assault and battery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with two violations of probation. His counsel moved for a continuance of the violation proceedings to await a psychiatric report. The district court denied the motion, found against defendant on one of the violations, and adjourned the hearing without a final judgment to await the report. When defendant chose to terminate the psychiatric evaluation, the district court revoked his probation and sentenced him to two concurrent two-year prison terms. On appeal, defendant contended that the continuance should have been granted. The Commonwealth moved to dismiss the appeal as moot because defendant's admission to sufficient facts to warrant a finding of guilty had been accepted on an assault and battery charge that had constituted one of the two probation violations. The court denied dismissal of the appeal, pretermitting the issue of mootness as not fully argued. Defendant's admission of sufficient facts on the assault and battery charge was not the equivalent of a conviction. The court affirmed the judgment. The denial of the continuance was within the district court's discretion, and the issue exhausted itself when defendant chose not to continue the evaluation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment.

Dupont v. Chief of Police of Pepperell


No. 01-P-665


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


57 Mass. App. Ct. 690; 786 N.E.2d 396; 2003 Mass. App. LEXIS 372


November 21, 2002, Argued  
March 31, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Middlesex. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on January 10, 2000. The case was heard by Paul A. Chernoff, J., on motions for judgment on the pleadings.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff town resident appealed from a judgment of the Middlesex County Superior Court Department (Massachusetts), which granted defendant town police chief's motion for judgment on the pleadings. The superior court's decision affirmed the chief's decision to revoke the resident's license to carry firearms, requested by renewal application pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 140, § 131, and dismissed the resident's petition.


OVERVIEW: The resident's renewal application of his license to carry firearms was denied by the police chief due to two prior convictions of the resident. The resident contended that his disqualifying acts occurred prior to the amendment that allowed denial due to those types of convictions and accordingly, that retroactive application of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 140, § 131 was erroneous. The denial by the police chief was affirmed by two lower courts and on further appeal, it was again affirmed. The court held that there was no abuse of discretion in the police chief's denial pursuant to ch. 140, § 131(f). The retroactive application of ch. 140, § 131 was reasonable in light of the wording of the statute and the utmost importance of the public safety which regulation by licensing was designed to protect. The resident's constitutional arguments to ch. 140, § 131 were found to lack merit. Claims regarding the unconstitutionality with respect to ex post facto and double jeopardy were inapplicable because ch. 140, § 131 was not punitive. There was no lack of due process or denial of the resident's rights because carrying a firearm was not an absolute right.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Commonwealth v. Hill


No. 00-P-1741


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


57 Mass. App. Ct. 240; 782 N.E.2d 35; 2003 Mass. App. LEXIS 110


May 6, 2002, Argued  
January 29, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected March 14, 2003


PRIOR HISTORY: Middlesex. Indictments found and returned in the Superior Court Department on May 13, 1999. A pretrial motion to suppress evidence was heard by Charles T. Spurlock, J., and the cases were tried before Charles M. Grabau, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Superior Court Department, Middlesex (Massachusetts), which convicted him of breaking and entering a vehicle in the nighttime with the intent to commit a felony in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 266, § 16; possession of burglarious tools in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 266, § 49; and receiving stolen goods with a value less than $ 250 in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 266, § 60.


OVERVIEW: Two automobile break-ins occurred in the early morning and a police investigation led to defendant. Two officers were let into defendant's apartment by defendant, who answered questions. While inside, several items that had been reported stolen were observed. The police returned and defendant agreed to go with them to the police station. Defendant's motion to suppress the seized stolen items was denied and defendant was convicted of several offenses. On his appeal, the court vacated in part, remanded, and affirmed in part. The court first held that defendant's motion to suppress was properly denied because the second entry by the police was made pursuant to defendant's implied voluntary consent. Defendant's motion for a required finding of not guilty was properly denied because the Commonwealth provided sufficient evidence to prove that defendant had intended to commit a felony when he broke into the two vehicles. The trial court erred, however, in instructing the jury that any larceny constituted the felony element of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 266, § 16 because under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 266, § 30, a larceny was not a felony unless the value of the property stolen exceeded $ 250.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the portion of the trial court's judgment that convicted defendant of breaking and entering with the intent to commit a felony and remanded to the trial court for resentencing on the lesser included offense of breaking and entering a motor vehicle with intent to commit a misdemeanor. The court affirmed the remaining portions of the trial court's judgment.

Commonwealth v. Berte


No. 01-P-129


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


57 Mass. App. Ct. 29; 781 N.E.2d 14; 2003 Mass. App. LEXIS 7


September 18, 2002, Argued  
January 8, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected January 17, 2003.
Review denied by Commonwealth v. Berte, 438 Mass. 1109, 785 N.E.2d 382, 2003 Mass. LEXIS 205 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Hampshire. Indictment found and returned in the Superior Court Department on August 10, 1999. The case was heard by Constance M. Sweeney, J.



DISPOSITION: Convictions for home invasion committed with a firearm and for armed robbery, and the sentence on the conviction for armed robbery, affirmed. Sentence on the conviction for home invasion committed with a firearm vacated, and the case remanded for resentencing on this count with a maximum sentence not to exceed twenty years, and a minimum sentence of ten years imprisonment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a jury-waived trial, defendant was convicted for home invasion committed with a firearm and armed robbery, and acquitted of conspiracy to distribute a Class B drug. The Hampshire Superior Court Department (Massachusetts) sentenced defendant to 20 years and a day in state prison on the home invasion charge, and a concurrent sentence of 18 to 20 years for the armed robbery. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 265, §18C, the home invasion statute, was unconstitutional on its face because of various infirmities in its penalty section. Defendant contended that the penalty scheme under which he was tried and convicted was facially unlawful and unconstitutionally vague and ambiguous. Defendant argued that the statute's 20-year fixed term for the aggravated home invasion portion of the statute conflicted with Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 279, § 24, that it inconsistently also mandates a 10-year minimum sentence, that the statute ran counter to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 127, § 133, and that the statute inconsistently provided for and prohibited probation. The appeals court held that the Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 265, § 18C stated that 20 years was the maximum allowable sentence and 10 years was the minimum. In addition, the appeals court concluded that probation was prohibited under the statute. Thus, the appeals court concluded that the trial judge erred in sentencing defendant to 20 years and a day. As for defendant's waiver of a jury trial, the appeals court found no error since the court engaged in a thorough colloquy.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed. The sentence on the conviction for home invasion was vacated. The case was remanded for resentencing with a maximum sentence not to exceed 20 years, and a minimum sentence of 10 years imprisonment.

Daddario v. Cape Cod Comm'n


No. 00-P-1851


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


56 Mass. App. Ct. 764; 780 N.E.2d 124; 2002 Mass. App. LEXIS 1618


September 17, 2002, Argued  
December 18, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Daddario v. Cape Cod Comm'n, 438 Mass. 1110, 785 N.E.2d 383, 2003 Mass. LEXIS 236 (2003)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Daddario v. Cape Cod Comm'n, 540 U.S. 1005, 124 S. Ct. 541, 157 L. Ed. 2d 410, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 8227 (2003)
Related proceeding at Giuffrida v. Zoning Bd. of Appeals, 68 Mass. App. Ct. 396, 862 N.E.2d 417, 2007 Mass. App. LEXIS 230 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Land Court Department on March 1, 1995. Following review by the Supreme Judicial Court, Daddario v. Cape Cod Comm'n (1997), 425 Mass. 411, 681 N.E.2d 833, the case was heard by Peter W. Kilborn, J.
Daddario v. Cape Cod Comm'n, 2000 Mass. LCR LEXIS 30 (2000)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant developer sued appellee commission for refusing to grant him a permit. After remand from the Supreme Judicial Court, the Suffolk Land Court Department (Massachusetts) granted the commission's renewed motion to dismiss, under Mass. R. Civ. P. 12(b)(6), the developer's claims that 1989 Mass. Acts ch. 716 was void for vagueness and, as applied, violated his right to equal protection of the laws. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: The developer said the permit denial was a regulatory taking. The appellate court held the trial court correctly found this claim was not ripe, as further interaction between the developer and the commission would not have been futile. He did not show 1989 Mass. Acts ch. 716, as applied to him, was so vague that men of common intelligence must necessarily guess at its meaning and differ as to its application. The statute had a rational and well-defined basis. It established criteria for the commission's evaluation of the development proposal and required more detailed guidelines providing a framework for a "probable benefits and detriments" analysis. The developer's complaint did not identify his proposal's benefits or how they outweighed its adverse environmental effects and, in conclusory fashion, claimed he satisfied minimum performance standards. He did not allege impermissible considerations such as race, religion, or punishing his exercise of constitutional rights entered into the commission's decision. His general allegation, without specifics, that others similarly situated were granted permits, did not support his equal protection claim, even on a motion to dismiss.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

City of Worcester v. Bonaventura


No. 00-P-1208


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


56 Mass. App. Ct. 166; 775 N.E.2d 795; 2002 Mass. App. LEXIS 1221


March 22, 2002, Argued  
September 30, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected November 8, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Worcester. Civil actions commenced in the Worcester Division of the Housing Court Department, three on November 29, 1999, two on December 7, 1999, and one on December 10, 1999, respectively. The cases were heard by John G. Martin, J.



DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city filed six complaints in the Worcester Division of the Housing Court Department, Massachusetts, seeking permanent injunctive relief against defendant condominium owners. The trial court entered judgment against the city. The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: The city sought to enforce its orders directing the owners to cease and desist from operating their respective condominium units as lodging houses, and to obtain applicable approval and permits as a precondition to operating the lodging houses. The trial court distinguished between tenants and lodgers, noting that a tenant had the right to exclusive possession of the premises, whereas a lodger merely had the right to use the premises. The trial court declared the ordinance to be unconstitutionally vague and concluded that the living arrangements of the owners' group of tenants formed a single housekeeping unit which was entitled to the same treatment as families under the city's ordinances. The city argued that the trial court's finding was an error. The appellate court held that the ordinance was not unconstitutionally vague, as nothing on the record suggested that the ordinance was open to a varied application. The definition of "family" in the city's ordinance did not trespass on constitutional inhibitions.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was vacated and the case was remanded.

Commonwealth v. Sullivan


No. 00-P-1110


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


55 Mass. App. Ct. 775; 774 N.E.2d 679; 2002 Mass. App. LEXIS 1149


January 15, 2002, Argued  
September 10, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Hampshire. Indictments found and returned in the Superior Court Department on September 3, 1997. The cases were heard by Mary-Lou Rup, J.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgments were affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed judgments by the Hampshire Superior Court (Massachusetts) that convicted him, inter alia, for disseminating or possessing with intent to disseminate matter harmful to minors, pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, § 28, claiming that the evidence was insufficient.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was in the habit of going to a pond to view pornographic magazines, smoke cigarettes, and masturbate. On occasions, he let the children look at his magazines and smoke his cigarettes. He claimed that the evidence was insufficient to conclude that the magazines were pornographic. The appellate court held that the children's use of the term "Playboy" to describe the magazines was their generic label for any magazine containing sexually explicit material. Although the trial judge did not live in the county, the appellate court's review of the magazines led it to conclude that no reasonable and disinterested observer anywhere in the Commonwealth would think them suitable for display to children. Accordingly, they could not possibly meet the standards of any of the Commonwealth's counties and necessarily fell below those prevailing in the county at the time of defendant's violation of § 28.


OUTCOME: The judgments were affirmed.

 

398 of 756 DOCUMENTS


JILES v. DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTION


No. 00-P-820


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


55 Mass. App. Ct. 658; 774 N.E.2d 150; 2002 Mass. App. LEXIS 1105


February 15, 2002, Argued  
August 26, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected October 29, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on March 19, 1999. The case was heard by Patrick J. King, J., on a motion for summary judgment.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate filed a complaint alleging that defendants, Massachusetts Department of Correction and certain of its officers, violated his constitutional and statutory rights to counsel and to access to the courts, under both the federal and Massachusetts Civil Rights Acts (MCRA) and Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 127, § 36A. The Suffolk Superior Court (Massachusetts) allowed defendants' motion for summary judgment. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate's claim arose after he met with his attorney in a prison room where the door contained an open grille and where a guard was stationed outside the door. The inmate alleged such an arrangement did not adequately preserve the confidentiality of his communications with counsel. The appeals court concluded that summary judgment was properly entered on the inmate's denial of his right of access to the courts claim. The appeals court noted that the inmate failed to demonstrate that he suffered an actual injury. The appeals court noted that the record established that the inmate was sufficiently able to communicate with counsel such that he was able to file the instant complaint. In addition, the guard's presence outside the door was reasonably related to penological interests since the inmate was placed in the subject room because of an alleged disciplinary infraction. As for the inmate's claims under the MCRA and 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, the appeals court upheld summary judgment since there were no constitutional violations. Finally, as for the right to counsel claim, the appeals court noted that there was no violation since there was no criminal proceeding.


OUTCOME: The grant of defendants' motion for summary judgment was affirmed.

 

399 of 756 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Lally


No. 01-P-133


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


55 Mass. App. Ct. 601; 773 N.E.2d 985; 2002 Mass. App. LEXIS 1093


April 18, 2002, Argued  
August 16, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Norfolk. Complaint received and sworn to in the Quincy Division of the District Court Department on June 16, 2000. A guilty plea was accepted by Mark S. Coven, J., and a revocation of probation proceeding was heard by him.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's order revoking the defendant's probation was vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty in the Quincy District Court (Massachusetts) to one count of assault by means of a dangerous weapon and one count of possession of a class D substance, and he was sentenced to probation. The trial court later found that defendant violated his probation, revoked defendant's probation, and imposed a one-year sentence to the house of correction. Defendant appealed the revocation.


OVERVIEW: The trial court initially imposed as a condition of probation that defendant submit to treatment as deemed necessary. A psychologist evaluated defendant and found that defendant would not benefit from any more treatment, but recommended that random urine screens for drugs and alcohol be made part of defendant probation. A probation officer told defendant that he would be required to submit to random urine testing. Defendant refused to sign the new condition of probation. The appellate court held that judges could order random urine screens as a probation condition, but that condition had to come from the judge, not from a probation officer. Probationers were entitled to reasonably specific conditions that provide clear guidelines as to what and when their actions or omissions would constitute a violation of their probation. Here, the appellate court held the probation condition ordering treatment as deemed necessary was ambiguous, and did not read by implication in that condition the requirement that defendant undergo random urine screens.


OUTCOME: The order revoking defendant's probation was vacated.

 

400 of 756 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Sattelmair


No. 01-P-420


APPEALS COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


55 Mass. App. Ct. 384; 771 N.E.2d 189; 2002 Mass. App. LEXIS 918


March 8, 2002, Argued  
July 9, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Plymouth. Complaint received and sworn to in the Wareham Division of the District Court Department on March 28, 2000. A motion for pretrial probation was heard by W. James O'Neill, J., and the complaint was dismissed by him.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of dismissal vacated; the case was returned to the district court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Wareham Division of the District Court Department, Massachusetts, dismissed the complaint charging defendant with assault and battery on the ground that continuing the prosecution would be inconsistent with the interests of public justice. The Commonwealth appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Commonwealth contended that dismissal was inappropriate because the decision amounted to an unconstitutional usurpation of power reserved exclusively to the executive branch, that the judge did not follow the procedures set out in Brandano, and that dismissal was inappropriate. The court of appeals agreed with the second and third contentions. The Brandano procedure required defendant to file an affidavit containing all the facts and the law relied upon in justification of a dismissal. The Commonwealth then had an opportunity to file a counter affidavit. Upon receipt of the affidavits, the court was to hear disputed matters revealed by the affidavits unless the judge concluded that the affidavits on their face showed that dismissal was unwarranted. After the hearing, if the judge concluded that the dismissal was in the interests of public justice, he had to record his or her findings of fact accompanied by the reasons for the dismissal decision. Defendant's affidavit was signed by counsel, not by a person with personal knowledge of the factual basis of the motion, as required by Mass. R. Crim. P. 13(a)(2). The Commonwealth filed no affidavit, relying instead on oral comment.


OUTCOME: The judgment was vacated and the case was returned for further proceedings.
